                                           Chapter 2

              VEHICLE MANAGEMENT CONTINGENCY OPERATIONS

Section 2A— General Information

2.1. Introduction. This chapter establishes instructions for VFMs and VMSs tasked with a
deployment mission, Air and Space Expeditionary Force (AEF) responsibility, War Reserve
Material (WRM) management, command levy contingency shipment and/or supporting Military
Operations Other Than War (MOOTW). Provisions of this chapter apply to steady state,
transition to surge, Major Theater War (MTW) and reconstitution operations. All Vehicle
Management personnel, regardless of rank, will be familiar with the contents of this chapter.
   2.1.1. This chapter is designed to be used in concert with AFH 24-320, Expeditionary
   Vehicle Management. This chapter contains guidance primarily for use prior to deployment
   and the handbook contains guidance for use during deployment. The handbook provides
   Vehicle Management specific information for combat environment operations and is
   designed to assist deployed Vehicle Management personnel of all grades to establish and
   operate shops in a contingency environment. Its use is mandatory.
2.2. AEF Process Overview. The AEF process is based on a 20-month rotation cycle. The
cycle is designed to allow for training, preparation and on-call deployment eligibility. The
process is designed to provide deployment predictability. Steady-State deployments equal the
capabilities of about two lead wings, one bomber group and associated units. The transition to
Surge Stage occurs when mission requirements start to exceed Steady State capabilities. Surge
may lead to the MTW phase if an established war plan is activated or if force requirements
exceed the amount contained in two full AEFs. Reconstitution is initiated after the MTW phase
ends. Reconstitution’s goal is to return forces and equipment to full Mission Capable (MC) as
soon as possible.

Section 2B— Overall Responsibilities

2.3. AF/A4RE. The AF will have sufficient motor vehicles, manpower, tools, facilities and
shop equipment on hand to support the USAF WMP, AEF operations and/or MOOTW.
   2.3.1. Adjudicate any vehicle sourcing reclama issues.
   2.3.2. Appoint specific MAJCOM A4, as determined by Area of Responsibility (AOR), as
   Point of Contact (POC) for logistical support for specific operation.
2.4. Air and Space Expeditionary Force Center (AEFC):
   2.4.1. Sources personnel after receiving OPLAN or AEF tasking request from parent
   MAJCOM.
   2.4.2. Adjusts or forwards personnel tasking shortfalls as appropriate.
2.5. WR-ALC
   2.5.1. Implements procedures to meet spare parts and TO shortfalls through emergency
   procurement actions to support surge and sustainment phases of contingency operations.
40                                           AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


        2.5.1.1. This does not relieve unit responsibility for maintaining duplicate, deployable
        printed or electronic copies of TOs for WRM or Mobility (Use Code (UC) ―A‖ on
        Vehicle Authorization Listing (VAL)) tasked vehicles.
     2.5.2. Sources vehicles after receiving OPLAN or AEF tasking request from parent
     MAJCOM. WR-ALC will work closely with MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs to
     identify potential sources for MC vehicles. Note: Since WR-ALC is not a force provider,
     Air Combat Command (ACC), as the air component to Joint Force Commander (JFCOM),
     will manage the scheduling and sourcing of forces (including vehicles) to meet the
     Combatant Commander’s (COCOM’s) requirements through the AEFC. ACC/A4XV will
     work directly with WR-ALC to coordinate with other MAJCOMs, where necessary, to
     source required vehicle assets. The same process will be followed by other MAJCOMs who
     have air component/force provider responsibilities in their respective AOR.
     2.5.3. Adjusts or forwards vehicle tasking reclamas as appropriate.
2.6. VEMSO. Provides support necessary to equip expeditionary Vehicle Management forces
with the best tools, equipment, parts, maintenance techniques, policy and general support for
deployed operations. This support is accomplished through research of available commercial
products, development of parts kits, capture and formalization of deployment lessons learned,
and policy change recommendations.
     2.6.1. Tools and equipment will be specifically chosen for transportability (light weight,
     small size); ease of use in the field (power requirements, etc.); and overall
     necessity/practicality for the type of maintenance performed.
        2.6.1.1. VEMSO approved tools and equipment for deployment will be formalized into
        appropriate Unit Type Codes (UTCs) for AEF and contingency tasking.
     2.6.2. Develops vehicle parts support kits such as Temporary Mission Support Kits
     (TMSKs), Mobility Readiness Spares Packages (MRSPs) and Contingency High Priority
     Mission Support Kits (CHPMSKs) to support Vehicle Management activities in an
     expeditionary, deployed environment.
        2.6.2.1. TMSKs, MRSPs and CHPMSKs will be standardized for AF use by vehicle
        make, model and type. A TMSK Library Link is located on the AF Vehicle Management
        Neighborhood Community of Practice (VM CoP), AF Portal website, for AF-wide use:
        https://afkm.wpafb.af.mil/ASPs/CoP/OpenCoP.asp?Filter=OO-LG-AF-66.
     2.6.3. Researches and develops management techniques, procedures and guidance necessary
     to guide Vehicle Management operations in an expeditionary, deployed environment. Tips
     and lessons learned will be captured, developed and distributed to enhance knowledge level
     of personnel subject to deploy.
     2.6.4. Develops vehicle deployment condition standards to ensure maximum reliability in
     field conditions with minimal investment. Monitors condition of vehicles deployed through
     collection and dissemination of "lessons-learned" and other means to institutionalize
     readiness and maximize return on investment.
     2.6.5. Refer to Chapter 8 for additional VEMSO guidance.
2.7. MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs:
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                           41


  2.7.1. Develop supplemental guidance specific to theater-unique operations.
  2.7.2. Ensure Vehicle Management activities are equipped and trained to fulfill wartime and
  AEF mission requirements.
  2.7.3. Program for manpower, facilities, shop equipment, technical manuals and tools
  necessary to support organizational and intermediate management concepts for all vehicles
  committed to wartime and AEF missions.
  2.7.4. Participate in MRSP reviews and validations to ensure sufficient spare parts are
  available to support contingency operations for a minimum of 30 days. Specifically address
  spare parts support concept for initial and follow-on parts support to the theater of operations.
  2.7.5. Coordinate establishment of CHPMSKs with Materiel Management personnel.
  2.7.6. Manage WRM vehicle assets according to AFI 25-101, War Reserve Materiel (WRM)
  Program Guidance and Procedures, as supplemented.
  2.7.7. Contact WR-ALC for vehicle repair assistance above MAJCOM capability.
  2.7.8. Assign primary WRM vehicle management function within the headquarters.
  2.7.9. Establish minimum reporting requirements to identify on-hand vehicle assets and
  ensure shortages, vehicle MC rates and materiel management support problem areas are
  identified.
  2.7.10. MAJCOMs with host base responsibilities are required to provide Vehicle
  Management and spare parts support for inbound forces identified in OPLANs.
  2.7.11. MAJCOMs with host base responsibilities may direct Individual Toolkits (ITKs) for
  all Air Force Specialty Codes (AFSCs) be left in place during rotations. If this happens, the
  host base and MAJCOM should notify inbound forces that ITKs are not required for that
  operating location.
  2.7.12. Where appropriate, tenant MAJCOMs assist the host MAJCOM to source their
  command’s vehicle-specific and peculiar spare parts. The host base Vehicle Management
  organization is responsible for follow-on spare parts support.
  2.7.13. Serve as Functional Area Managers (FAMs) on MAJCOM Crisis or Contingency
  Action Teams (CATs) or equivalent. Identify, source and track deployment actions. Provide
  personnel, vehicle and vehicle-related cargo In-Transit Visibility (ITV) to MAJCOM
  leadership as required. Refer to paragraph A2.2 for additional guidance.
  2.7.14. Contact WR-ALC for additional vehicle requirements to support OPLAN and AEF
  taskings.
  2.7.15. Adjust or forward vehicle tasking reclamas as appropriate.
  2.7.16. Transfer accountability for vehicles that have been deployed from home station. The
  shipping MAJCOM transfers vehicle accountability to the combatant MAJCOM. The
  combatant MAJCOM accepts accountability for vehicles deployed to their AOR. After
  accountability has been transferred, the losing MAJCOM can initiate replacement actions
  with WR-ALC using the command levy process (see paragraph 2.14) or through their
  vehicle buy process. Transfers from AFR and ANG must comply with DODD 1225.6,
  Equipping the Reserve Forces.
42                                           AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


2.8. Base-Level and WRM Deploying Activities:
     2.8.1. Maintain WRM vehicles according to guidelines established in this chapter, related
     AF TOs, Vehicle Management publications and AFI 25-101, as supplemented by the
     MAJCOM.
     2.8.2. Comply with the provisions of TO 36-1-191 and other shipping instructions as
     provided by WR-ALC or MAJCOM.
     2.8.3. Identify problem areas which cannot be resolved locally to the MAJCOM.
     2.8.4. Develop local guidance for Vehicle Management wartime concept of operations as
     directed by the MAJCOM. Include procedures for operating in chemical/biological
     contaminated environments and repairing contaminated vehicles. See AFMAN 10-2602,
     Nuclear, Biological, Chemical, and Conventional (NBCC) Defense Operations and
     Standards, for additional guidance.
     2.8.5. Select best (most serviceable and maintainable) vehicles for deployment. Ensure each
     deployment-tasked vehicle is placed in TO 36-1-191 plus condition, and accompanied with
     an assembled spare wheel/tire, all applicable TOs and a complete TMSK, if required (see
     paragraph 2.15). In addition, each commercially designed light and medium duty vehicle
     (see paragraph 1.1.1) and military designed prime mover must also be equipped with lug
     wrench(es), jack and jack handle.
        2.8.5.1. Assemble TMSKs IAW guidance on the VM CoP. Each kit will include a
        serviceable mounted spare wheel/tire provided by owing organization or vehicle
        management if not available and TOs. TMSKs will be affixed to the vehicle or shipped
        against the appropriate vehicle’s contingency Transportation Control Number (TCN).
        Refer to paragraphs 2.15 and 2.17 in this instruction for additional TMSK and TCN
        guidance.
     2.8.6. Ensure VFMs and VMSs are familiar with current Designed Operational Capability
     (DOC) statement, OPLANs, Base Support Plans (BSPs) and UTC Mission Capability
     (MISCAP) statements.
     2.8.7. Ensure mobility UC ―A‖ vehicles have MRSPs established if authorized by Materiel
     Management guidance or develop a TSMK listing for each asset.
     2.8.8. Research and provide information for CHPMSK establishment if required.
     Coordination with VEMSO, MAJCOM and Logistics Support Center (LSC) personnel may
     be required.
     2.8.9. Deploy with sufficient skilled personnel and equipment resources to satisfy all
     contingency wartime and AEF requirements.
     2.8.10. Document costs to prepare vehicles, spare parts and tech data for shipment. Units
     should retain all expense data associated with the preparation of vehicles for shipment for
     possible reimbursement.
     2.8.11. Monitor the Time Phased Force Deployment Data (TPFDD) to ensure tasked
     vehicles are shipped to the correct location on time. For ITV, units are required to provide
     the MAJCOM with the following information concerning vehicle equipment: Deployment
     TCN (F-Prefixed), Unit Line Number (ULN), UTC, vehicle registration number and
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         43


   departure and delivery dates within the allotted transit times. For tracking purposes, when
   Vehicle Management personnel are tasked to deploy with a tasked vehicle (e.g., natural
   disasters) forward the following information to the MAJCOM: Complete name, grade,
   AFSC and last four digits of the social security number. See AFI 24-201, Cargo Movement,
   Attachment 2, for allotted transit times.
   2.8.12. Maintain duplicate printed or electronic copies of TOs to support WRM outload and
   mobility (identified by UC ―A‖ on VAL) vehicles.
   2.8.13. Deploying units will ensure individual members are trained and equipped for
   contingency operations. Individual members will ensure they are qualified and equipped for
   contingency operations. Refer to Figure A2.4 for specific pre-deployment training
   requirements.
   2.8.14. Fill or shortfall personnel OPLAN or AEF taskings as appropriate.
   2.8.15. Refer to VFM pre-contingency checklist, Figure A2.1, for guidance on thorough
   pre-deployment planning.

Section 2C— Steady-State Operations

2.9. Training:
   2.9.1. Repair Operations: Although difficult to predict the actual operating environment at a
   contingency location, it is possible to exercise personnel in a simulated or practice
   deployment. Personnel selected to fill AEF and mobility positions will receive annual
   refresher training at the unit level to ensure an adequate proficiency level is maintained.
      2.9.1.1. Deployable personnel need to be prepared for flexible operations under adverse
      conditions. They must also be well-trained in the use of all tools and shop equipment.
      2.9.1.2. Mandatory training must be completed on OLVIMS and Automated Fleet
      Information System (AFIS), metalworking, re-supply procedures and maintenance of
      unique deployed vehicles for personnel assigned to an upcoming AEF. Training
      completion will be documented on AF Form 1098. See Figure A2.4 for specific
      guidance.
   2.9.2. Contingency Environment: Operations in a contingency environment will expose
   vehicle maintainers to many situations and problems not encountered in normal peacetime
   operations. Personnel selected to fill AEF or mobility positions will receive annual refresher
   training at the unit level on basic survivability techniques.
      2.9.2.1. Examples include Air Base Survivability, Unexploded Ordnance procedures,
      Self-Aid/ Buddy Care, etc. Refer to AFMAN 10-2602; AFH 32-4014, Vol 4, USAF
      Ability to Survive and Operate Procedures in a Nuclear, Biological, and Chemical (NBC)
      Environment; and AFH 24-320 for additional training guidance.
2.10. WRM Vehicle Storage. WRM vehicles are authorized to bridge the gap between
peacetime and wartime requirements. These vehicles are authorized and maintained separately
from the active peacetime vehicle fleet and are normally preserved in storage. MAJCOMs
develop specific storage concepts for vehicles identified against OPLAN taskings.
44                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     2.10.1. Vehicles are stored in active (ready to roll) or inactive (deep stored) categories.
     MAJCOMs determine the mix of active and inactive stored vehicles. For basic planning, the
     following guidance applies:
        2.10.1.1. Active stored vehicles: Vehicles stored outdoors, under partial cover or
        vehicles required to support initial incoming forces are preserved to Level C as described
        in TO 36-1-191 or as specified by the MAJCOM.
        2.10.1.2. Inactive stored vehicles: Vehicles will be stored in an enclosed building and
        preserved to Level A storage as described in TO 36-1-191 or as prescribed by MAJCOM
        guidance. Note: Dense packing vehicles in an enclosed building does not constitute
        inactive storage.
        2.10.1.3. (Added-PACAF) . Additional guidance is published in PACAFH 24-3.
     2.10.2. Vehicles are controlled according to AFI 25-101, as supplemented.
     2.10.3. Accomplish lubrication at least every 18 months on active stored vehicles. An oil
     and filter change is accomplished every 3 years.
     2.10.4. WRM vehicles are rotated into the active peacetime fleet (where like-vehicle
     peacetime authorizations exist) to ensure equipment dependability/life cycle management
     and to equalize utilization.
     2.10.5. Develop a parking plan for each storage location.
     2.10.6. Fire extinguishers and chocks are mounted to or located in each vehicle, or
     positioned in the vehicle storage area.
     2.10.7. When inside storage cannot be provided, outside storage areas are well lit, have
     adequate drainage and are secured by a chain link or equivalent fence.
     2.10.8. Exceptions to Storage Policies. Fuel servicing, fire fighting, aircraft cargo loaders
     and certain other vehicles are equipped with systems that must be exercised more frequently.
     To the maximum extent practicable, fully exercise operational systems on these vehicles
     every 30 days.
2.11. WRM Manpower Determination. Vehicle Management and Manpower Office consider
the following factors when developing manpower requirements supporting vehicle storage:
     2.11.1. The quantity and complexity of vehicles to be stored (vehicle equivalents).
     2.11.2. The storage level (active storage requires more manpower than inactive storage).
     2.11.3. Frequency of inspection and the average amount of time required for each inspection.
     2.11.4. Age of the Fleet. Older vehicles may require more maintenance than pre-positioned
     new vehicles.
     2.11.5. The degree and frequency of vehicle fleet involvement in exercises (that is, used to
     support Joint Chiefs of Staff (JCS), intra-theater or local exercises).
     2.11.6. Rotation.   This will affect the number of Limited Technical Inspections (LTIs)
     required.
     2.11.7. If applicable, the amount of time required for vehicles to be placed in or removed
     from storage.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          45


   2.11.8. Hours of operational coverage, e.g., 24 hours a day, 7 days a week.
   2.11.9. Material handling and surface movement of cargo to, from and between operating
   locations in support of surge and sustainment operations at bare base versus fixed facilities.
   2.11.10. Fleet size for management and dispersed locations.
   2.11.11. Contractor Operated Storage. Contractor operated storage is the AF Standard.
   Explore the use of military personnel only if local environment and political conditions
   prevent contract establishment. Vehicle Management and Manpower Office also consider
   manpower ceilings, contractor availability, cost, location, and duration of storage as
   governing factors. Assign technically competent (7-level personnel in AFSC 2T3) AF
   vehicle repair technicians as Quality Assurance Personnel (QAP) and ensure QAP-specific
   training is provided. See Chapter 9 for additional information on QAP.
2.12. WRM Pre-Positioned Support. MAJCOMs identify the types of items and appropriate
quantities to develop WRM MRSP and TMSK. Spares for pre-positioned vehicles will be
identified, maintained and accounted for. Normally, MRSP and TMSK are designed to support
30 days of operations. Go to VM CoP for comprehensive TMSK content listings.
   2.12.1. Ensure MRSPs, TMSKs and CHPMSKs are adequate to support increased wartime
   usage. Each WRM vehicle identified for deployment to an un-established operating location
   will be equipped with an MRSP, TMSK or CHPMSK. An un-established operating location
   is defined as a base without bench/working stocks capable of supporting the out-loaded
   vehicle.
      2.12.1.1. (Added-PACAF) . Collocated Operating Base (COB) locations will ensure
      the development of TMSK lists identifying the types of items and appropriate quantities
      for the vehicle fleet.
      2.12.1.2. (Added-PACAF) . Mission Support Readiness Parts (MSRP) kits will only be
      initiated with the approval of PACAF/A4RV.

Section 2D— Transition to Surge/Deployment Preparation

2.13. Personnel:
   2.13.1. Closely review all deployment tasking MISCAPs and line remarks. Also, review
   AOR reporting instructions found on the AEFC web page under deployment requirements.
   Current MISCAP information can be obtained from the Unit Deployment Manager (UDM).
   Contact the Installation Deployment Officer (IDO) for assistance if UDM is unavailable.
      2.13.1.1. The MISCAP describes the performance level required by the tasked UTC. The
      tasked unit is responsible for ensuring deploying personnel can meet all MISCAP
      requirements.
   2.13.2. If the unit cannot support the tasking, forward a shortfall request through appropriate
   channels immediately.
   2.13.3. Personnel with AFSCs 2T3X1, 2T3X2A, 2T3X2C, 2T3X5 and 2T370 will deploy
   with a complete ITK of standard and metric hand tools unless specifically directed to deviate
   by the host MAJCOM. ITK should also include any AFSC-specific tools required to fulfill
   MISCAP requirements. See Figure A2.6 for recommended items.
46                                           AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


        2.13.3.1. Personnel with AFSCs 2T370, 2T390 and 2T300 will deploy with publications
        and forms listed in Figure A2.2 and Figure A2.3 Ensure all publications and forms are
        the most current versions. Electronic copies (floppy disc, CD, data stick, etc.) are
        preferable if computer support capable of reading media is confirmed.
     2.13.4. Personnel with AFSC 2T3X7 will deploy with an ITK consisting of laptop, all-in-one
     printer/ scanner/fax, 30 days of administrative office supplies and current versions of
     electronic publications and forms listed in Figure A2.2 and Figure A2.3, unless specially
     authorized to deviate by host MAJCOM.
        2.13.4.1. The 2T3X7 ITK will consist of a functional, fully tested and modern laptop
        computer. Software will include current versions (AF standard) of Microsoft® (MS)
        Outlook®, Word®, Excel® and PowerPoint® as a minimum. Laptop will have internet,
        floppy disk and CD-RW/ DVD capability. It will be loaded with the most current and
        fully functional version of OLVIMS and AFIS. A compatible printer with extra ink or
        toner cartridges will accompany the VM&A laptop. Ensure laptop can read electronic
        publications. Laptop will be exercised before departure to ensure full capability. See
        Figure A2.7 for additional guidance.
        2.13.4.2. The deploying unit should send an in-use OLVIMS computer and printer.
        Replacement computers can be easily sourced for home station use. It is imperative the
        deploying members be able to establish and operate OLVIMS at the deployed location as
        soon as practical.
     2.13.5. Material Control personnel will deploy with an ITK for materiel control operations
     consisting of laptop, printer, fax machine, 30 days of administrative office supplies and
     current versions of electronic publications and forms listed in Figure A2.2 and Figure A2.3,
     unless specially authorized to deviate by host MAJCOM.
        2.13.5.1. The ITK supporting materiel control will consist of a functional, fully tested
        and modern laptop computer. Software will include current versions (AF standard) of
        MS Outlook, Word, Excel and PowerPoint as a minimum. Laptop will have internet,
        floppy disk and CD-RW/DVD capability and any appropriate software needed for
        conducting Materiel Control functions. A compatible printer with extra ink or toner
        cartridges will accompany the Materiel Control laptop. Ensure laptop can read electronic
        publications. Laptop will be exercised before departure to ensure full capability. See
        Figure A2.8 for additional guidance.
        2.13.5.2. The deploying unit should send an in-use Materiel Control computer, printer
        and supplies. Replacement items can be easily sourced to backfill for home station use. It
        is imperative the deploying members be able to establish and operate Materiel Control
        functions at the deployed location as soon as practical.
     2.13.6. ITKs will be limited to 70 pounds and 62 linear inches (length + width + height) to
     ensure commercial air transportation capability. Some domestic flights may have a 50-pound
     weight limit. Ensure excess baggage allowance is authorized on deploying member’s orders
     if the member is deploying with an ITK.
     2.13.7. The combatant MAJCOM may direct ITKs for all AFSCs to be left in place during
     rotations. If this happens, the combatant MAJCOM should notify inbound forces that ITKs
     are not required for that operating location.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                           47


   2.13.8. Units are responsible for ensuring each deploying member has all required individual
   equipment. Items such as steel toe boots, safety glasses/goggles, reflective belts and hearing
   protection are mandatory. See Figure A2.5 for other mandatory and recommended items.
2.14. Command Levy Vehicle Tasking:
   2.14.1. MAJCOM forwards WR-ALC command levy request to tasked base. MAJCOM also
   provides shipping information based on TPFDD.
   2.14.2. Tasked units send reclama requests back to MAJCOM as soon as possible. This
   enables better decision-making and prevents short-notice taskings to the same or other units.
   2.14.3. Funding. Tasked units fund all costs to place vehicles into TO 36-1-191 plus
   condition and build TMSKs from their O&M budgets, unless otherwise provided in the
   shipping instructions. Units document and retain all expense data associated with the
   preparation of vehicles for shipment for possible reimbursement.
   2.14.4. Preparation for Shipment: Units ensure that only their best (newest/most serviceable
   and maintainable) vehicles are shipped to meet OPLAN, AEF or command levy shipment
   taskings. Rotate vehicles as necessary within the wing to satisfy home station priority needs.
   Leasing may be required. The following steps will be accomplished prior to vehicle
   shipment:
      2.14.4.1. Perform an LTI.
      2.14.4.2. Place vehicle in TO 36-1-191 plus condition. Repair or replace components
      and subassemblies, which do not meet TO 36-1-191 plus standards.
      2.14.4.3. Service vehicle fluid systems or perform PM&I and Special Inspections if due
      within 90 days of shipment date. Complete all Time Compliance Technical Orders
      (TCTO), Service Bulletins (SB), One-Time Inspections (OTI), Manufacturer Recalls and
      delayed maintenance prior to deployment. Contact the MAJCOM for guidance if unable
      to comply before the shipment date.
      2.14.4.4. Vehicle Historical Data. A copy of pertinent historical data is required along
      with a spare set of keys for the vehicle. Secure data and spare keys in cab or operator’s
      compartment for shipment. If shipped data and/or keys are not readily visible, identify
      location with a prominently placed label.
      2.14.4.5. Each tasked 60K-loader will deploy with one air transport configuration tool.
      2.14.4.6. When deploying aircraft refueling vehicles the losing organization will contact
      the gaining organization for specific fuel type, filters and/or additives used at the
      deployed location. LRSs will install appropriate filters prior to aircraft refuelers being
      shipped.
      2.14.4.7. Ensure each deployment-tasked vehicle deploys with an assembled spare
      wheel/tire, all applicable TOs , a complete TMSK, if required (see paragraph 2.15) and
      spare key(s). In addition, each commercially designed light and medium duty vehicle
      (see paragraph 1.1.2) and military designed prime mover must also be equipped with
      lug wrench(es), jack and jack handle.
      2.14.4.8. Ensure vehicle deployment TCNs are generated and tracked IAW guidance in
      paragraph 2.17
48                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


2.15. Pre-deployment Parts Kit Development:
     2.15.1. TMSKs:
        2.15.1.1. Each vehicle identified for deployment to an un-established operating location
        will be shipped with a TMSK. Vehicle-specific TMSK listings are available for
        download on the VM CoP. If a listing is not available on the website, download the
        template and refer to paragraph A2.4 for a list of items to include when building one.
        Provide a copy of the competed listing to VEMSO for posting on the VM CoP.
        2.15.1.2. Unless otherwise required by the MAJCOM, TMSKs are packages of common
        and high-use items developed and purchased for vehicle sustainment when no MRSP is
        available for this vehicle type. TMSKs are designed to sustain a vehicle operating in
        adverse conditions for 30 days.
        2.15.1.3. Kits are individually assembled, boxed, and shipped within the cab, trunk, and
        truck bed or on the forks of each vehicle, if physically possible. Kits will be packed in
        reusable cabinets for ease of inventory, access and security at the deployed location. If
        more than one vehicle of the same type is deploying to the same location, those kits can
        be consolidated into a larger kit. When consolidating kits, quantities and breadth of the
        kits should be increased. Each small general purpose vehicle and military designed prime
        mover needs to deploy with lug wrench(es), jack and jack handle so operators are self-
        sufficient to change out a spare tire; especially, in remote or hostile locations. This
        ensures availability of items if vehicles are redistributed, diverted or forward deployed.
        2.15.1.4. Every effort should be made to ensure the TMSK is affixed to the vehicle to
        prevent separation. If this is not feasible, consider placing the most critical items (TO
        and critical parts) in the cab or other vehicle compartments. Any over-sized kits should
        be shipped IAW paragraph 2.17.1.6 to ensure the kit arrives at the same location with
        the vehicle.
           2.15.1.4.1. If items shipped inside the vehicle are not readily visible (e.g., inside high
           reach or telephone maintenance truck compartments), identify location with a
           prominently placed label.
        2.15.1.5. Mobility (UC ―A‖ on VAL) and deployment-prone vehicles can have TMSKs
        pre-built if authorized by the MAJCOM. The unit will have emergency acquisition
        procedures in place for any kits that are not pre-assembled.
        2.15.1.6. Mark each TMSK exterior with vehicle make, model, registration number,
        shipping unit, gaining unit (if known) and shipping unit POC with Defense Switch
        Network (DSN) phone number. Each TMSK item inside the kit will be individually
        labeled with part number, NSN, description, vehicle type and model year.
        2.15.1.7. Ship current printed or electronic copy of TO and any other necessary technical
        data for maintenance with each vehicle, unless directed otherwise by the MAJCOM.
        When several vehicles of the same make/model/type are deployed as a package, each
        vehicle should be accompanied with a complete TO set. This ensures availability of
        technical data if vehicle is redistributed, diverted or forward deployed. If a unit is tasked
        to deploy a vehicle and has only one TO for the vehicle, the unit ships that TO or a photo
        copy with the vehicle.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                     49


   2.15.2. MRSPs:
      2.15.2.1. Each mobility UC ―A‖ vehicle listed on the VAL should have an MRSP
      established if authorized by materiel management guidance or develop a TMSK list for
      each asset.
      2.15.2.2. Deploying units and MAJCOMs ensure that if an MRSP is authorized and built
      to support a number of vehicles, each vehicle deploys with its assigned MRSP in the
      event vehicles are shipped to separate locations. Ensure local materiel management
      personnel are notified when a vehicle with an MRSP is being deployed. If an MRSP is
      not available, develop a TMSK list for each tasked vehicle IAW paragraph 2.15.1
   2.15.3. CHPMSKs:
      2.15.3.1. CHPMSKs can be established to support mission-critical vehicles. CHPMSKs
      can provide lateral support to multiple bases. They should be developed and deployed to
      locations that can best serve the entire theater if possible. Kit consists of NSN items
      requested by owning/maintaining unit and approved by MAJCOM. The CHPMSK is
      maintained in the materiel management warehouse and is deployed with the vehicle.
      Ensure local materiel management personnel are notified when a vehicle with a
      CHPMSK is being deployed.
      2.15.3.2. Contact the applicable LSC and MAJCOM for additional guidance.
   2.15.4. (Added-PACAF) . Follow-on spare parts support will be provided from the
   deploying base or other commercial sources as necessary. Contact PACAF/A4RV for
   guidance upon vehicle deployment.
2.16. Tools and Equipment Deployment:
   2.16.1. VFMs and VMSs at all levels must be aware of their UTC taskings. This information
   is available from the UDM, base-level Readiness Flight or the MAJCOM Logistics Plans and
   Readiness function.
   2.16.2. Tasked units build and deploy tool and equipment kits from host Vehicle
   Management shops as necessary to meet wartime taskings. Figure A2.9 provides mandatory
   items for UTC UFMXK, Transportation Vehicle Management Support Kit. UTC UFMXK is
   designed to support Vehicle Management operations for 30 days.
   2.16.3. Transformers may be required for some overseas locations. Contact MAJCOM if
   specific guidance is required.
   2.16.4. Deliver kits in air transportable tool storage cabinets to facilitate shipping and
   secured storage at pre-positioned and contingency locations.
2.17. Vehicle Deployment:
   2.17.1. Process:
      2.17.1.1. No vehicle will be deployed from an installation without coordination through
      the host VM&A activity. Units deliver vehicles to Vehicle Management Customer
      Service Center (CSC) for an LTI to ensure suitability for deployment. The VFM, VMS
      or designated representative will inspect and approve each vehicle and documentation
      package prior to shipment to ensure suitability and compliance with TO 36-1-191.
50                                       AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     Unsuitable vehicles are either repaired or replaced with another vehicle. Note: VM&A
     will contact parent MAJCOM to validate unit directed vehicle shipments.
        2.17.1.1.1. (Added-PACAF) . All vehicles deployed to contingency locations will
        be shipped in ―T.O. 36-1-191‖ Plus condition (see PACAFH 24-3, Attachment 4).
     2.17.1.2. Upon satisfactory completion of LTI, VM&A prepares a deployment package
     consisting of: Operator’s Inspection Guide and Trouble Report; Waiver Card; DD Form
     518, Accident Identification Card; AF Form 1297, Temporary Issue Receipt; Standard
     Form (SF) 91, Motor Vehicle Accident Report; copy of LTI; Vehicle Historical Record
     and DD Form 1348-1A. See paragraph A2.3 for more specific guidance.
        2.17.1.2.1. (Added-PACAF) . Ship a copy of the applicable T.O. with the
        deploying vehicle. Do not ship duplicate copies for like vehicles deploying to the
        same location.
     2.17.1.3. Prepped vehicles are delivered to the Cargo Deployment Function (CDF) or
     Traffic Management Flight (TMF) as directed by local policy. Vehicle Management may
     be responsible for transporting TMSKs if they are not affixed to the vehicle. The
     Installation Deployment Plan (IDP) should provide additional guidance on air and surface
     shipment standards and deploying unit UDM responsibilities.
     2.17.1.4. Any vehicle or equipment shipped against a TPFDD tasking will have a
     contingency TCN automatically generated from the Logistics Module (LOGMOD). The
     UDM or IDO should be able to determine if a vehicle is tasked against the TPFDD. The
     TCN for a TPFDD shipment will start with ―FF‖ if generated correctly.
        2.17.1.4.1. If LOGMOD is unavailable, use the following guidance to ensure correct
        TCNs have been manually generated: The TCN for each vehicle is built using the
        ULN from the TPFDD. Contingency TCNs are identified by ―$‖ symbols in the 7th
        and 8th position of the 17-character data element. Refer to DOD 4500.9-R, Defense
        Transportation Regulation, Part II, Cargo Movement, and Part III, Mobility, for
        additional guidance.
     2.17.1.5. Any vehicle or equipment not shipped against a TPFDD tasking will have a
     standard TCN created. Do not have a standard TCN created for a TPFDD-tasked vehicle
     shipment.
     2.17.1.6. Vehicle Management will closely coordinate with deploying unit UDM when
     the TMSK is not affixed to the vehicle. TMSKs shipped with, but not attached to,
     vehicles are moved as multi-piece shipments. Ensure they are correctly marked (i.e., item
     2 of 2) against shipment’s contingency TCN. Also, ensure the proper priority and
     Required Delivery Date (RDD) is assigned to all TMSKs that are shipped separately.
     This ensures the kit will arrive in time to support the vehicle.
     2.17.1.7. This data is entered into the Cargo Movement Operations System (CMOS) or
     Global Air Transportation Execution System (GATES) and initiates ITV through the
     Global Transportation Network (GTN).
     2.17.1.8. Document and retain all TCNs for deploying vehicles and related cargo.
     Monitor all shipments and provide all data to MAJCOM and gaining unit.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         51


   2.17.2. Surface Movement: Do not move vehicles to sea port until contacted by Surface
   Deployment and Distribution Command (SDDC) with a call forward date. SDDC replaced
   Military Traffic Management Command (MTMC) as of 1 Jan 04.
   2.17.3. MAJCOM staff tracks TPFDD deployment actions and operates MAJCOM CATs or
   equivalent. See paragraph A2.2 for specific guidance.
2.18. Home Station Survival. Deployment and AEF taskings can impact home station
operations beyond sustainability. The following paragraphs give VFMs and VMSs possible
options to mitigate the impact of heavy deployment taskings. Refer to the VM CoP for additional
survival tips and examples. Ensure leadership is informed and approves implementation of any
operational changes.
   2.18.1. Manpower:
       2.18.1.1. Augmentation. Explore the use of civilian over hires, or ANG and AFR
       backfills. Contact Base Civilian Personnel Office for guidance on civilian over hires.
       Contact nearest ANG or AFR base for possible augmentation. Also, contact MAJCOM
       POC for Individual Mobilization Augmentee (IMA) support. Manning Assistance can
       also be requested through the MAJCOM. Requesting unit is responsible for funding
       Temporary Duty (TDY) costs. A contingency Emergency and Special Program (ESP)
       code may be available for reimbursement.
       2.18.1.2. Training. Prior to deployment, accelerate 3-level training while the majority of
       your trainers are still available. Compensate for reduced capability by training non-
       deploying members in critical shop operations. This should help maximize shop
       productivity during heavy deployment periods.
   2.18.2. Shop Operations:
       2.18.2.1. Develop and implement a vehicle parking plan. Identify serviceable, non-
       essential vehicles to be parked. Identification method could be from across the base,
       focused on deploying unit’s vehicle fleet, commander’s or equivalent’s option or by
       number/type of mechanics deployed. If the last option is selected, compute the total
       number of vehicle equivalents earned by the deploying mechanics, then park the proper
       fleet mix based on the total vehicle equivalents. Extensive coordination with base
       leadership must occur before implementing any type of parking plan. The following
       guidance should be used if a parking plan is implemented.
          2.18.2.1.1. The vehicles should be stored in a controlled and monitored environment.
          They should be parked for the duration of the deployment. A parking plan and map
          are recommended.
          2.18.2.1.2. Ensure parked vehicles are preserved to the appropriate storage level
          IAW TO 36-1-191.
          2.18.2.1.3. Do not cannibalize from parked vehicles. This will cause increased
          workload before vehicles can be returned to using organizations.
       2.18.2.2. Focus on quality of maintenance performed. Use the approved vehicle
       Minimum Essential Levels (MEL) and paragraph 3.29 as a gauge to develop
       maintenance priorities and establish in-house MC rate goals. Established goals should be
       thoroughly briefed and approved by the commander.
52                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


        2.18.2.3. Contract Maintenance. Preplanning potential contract maintenance is crucial.
        Contact local Contracting Office to set up Blanket Purchase Agreements (BPAs) or short-
        term maintenance contracts. Maximize use of ESP codes for funding support.
        2.18.2.4. ISSA. If available, contact local DOD components or government maintenance
        operations in your area. Discuss establishing an ISSA for Vehicle Management support
        during contingencies and/or AEF rotations. Ensure any ISSAs address AF unique
        requirements for priority, types of maintenance and quality of services.

Section 2E—Deployed Location Operations:

2.19. Handbooks:
     2.19.1. Personnel will deploy with and use AFH 24-320.
     2.19.2. Personnel will deploy with and use the Vehicle Maintenance Safety Handbook.
     2.19.3. Personnel will deploy with and use AFMAN 10-100, Airman’s Manual.
2.20. VFM and VMS. After the initial phase of all contingencies, the deployed VFM and/or
VMS implements responsibilities outlined in Chapter 1 and Chapter 3 of this instruction at the
deployed location. When the deployed LRS does not have a VFM or VMS assigned, the senior
ranking military member with AFSC 2T3XX assumes those duties.
2.21. Qualification Training. Initiate immediately if needed. The senior deployed 2T3XX
ensures personnel are qualified on available shop equipment, local safety procedures, emergency
response actions and assigned vehicle fleet.
2.22. Mission Critical Vehicle List. Each deployed Vehicle Management operation employs a
maintenance priority system which considers current battle conditions and requirements. The
deployed VFM or VMS assigns priorities as necessary.

Explosive Ordnance Disposal M-113 Armored Personnel Carrier (APC), M1116 High Mobility
                            Multipurpose Wheeled Vehicle (HMMWV), Armored Conversion
Fuel Support                   Truck Tank 1200 gallon, Trailer, Fuel 600 gallon
Rapid Runway Repair (RRR) Truck, Dump; Tractor Dozer; Loader; Roller; Truck Tractor;
                          Excavator; Grader; Sweeper Vacuum; Trailer; Farm Tractor, with
                          broom

                               plows, blowers and/or brooms; Farm Tractors equipped with
                               brooms
Security Forces Vehicles       HMMWV; M-113 APC; air conditioning equipped K-9 vehicles;
                               other critical vehicles assigned to SFS
2.23. Materiel Control. A Materiel Management Specialist (AFSC 2S0X1) may be assigned to
Vehicle Management to perform Materiel Control functions as specified in Chapter 5.
   2.23.1. Materiel Control personnel will follow standard supply procurement procedures and
   utilize the Standard Base Supply System (SBSS) when procuring repair parts and supplies.
   Material Control personnel can also coordinate with the servicing Contracting Office to
   establish vehicle parts procurement via local purchase. Innovations in information
   technology, worldwide commercial delivery and government reforms have made internet
   parts sourcing through commercial vendors with BPAs and the Government Purchase Card
   (GPC) a viable alternative to traditional parts acquisition methods. Aggressive use should be
   made of commercial style transportation parts delivery alternatives.
   2.23.2. The combatant MAJCOM specifies how to accomplish follow-on spare parts support
   to the theater of operations. An LSC will be in place to support contingency operations.
   Other support systems will be identified in theater-unique supplements.
       2.23.2.1. The LSC Ground Support Flight provides service for Vehicle Management
       activities. They manage Mission Impaired Capability Awaiting Parts (MICAP) and NSN
       items. The LSC will also have a local purchase element to handle non-NSN requirements.
   2.23.3. Aggressively follow up with local ELRS Materiel Management function, NAF or
   combatant MAJCOM to establish contact with the appropriate LSC.
54                                           AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     2.23.4. After initial deployment, vehicle parts support may be improved by establishing a
     CHPMSK. A CHPMSK is established through coordination with the LSC and approved at
     the parent MAJCOM-level.
        2.23.4.1. CHPMSKs support mission-critical vehicles and consist of parts requested by
        owning unit (after approval by combatant MAJCOM). Once established, they are stored
        at the deployed location in the LSC warehouse. Parts are issued when a supply demand is
        levied. LSC personnel automatically requisition replacements. CHPMSK requisitions
        receive a much higher priority than regular bench stock. CHPMSKs can provide lateral
        support to multiple bases. They should be developed and deployed to locations that can
        best serve the entire theater if possible.
        2.23.4.2. Contact local LSC personnel and combatant MAJCOM for additional guidance.
     2.23.5. Refer to AFH 24-320, for supply sources and additional guidance.
2.24. VM&A:
     2.24.1. A 2T3X7, or qualified vehicle maintenance technician, is responsible for AF Form
     1823/ 1823-1, (computer generated) Vehicle and Equipment Work Order, preparation and
     ensuring vehicle repairs are accomplished consistent with priorities established by the VFM
     or VMS.
     2.24.2. If a 2T3X7 is not available, use checklists in AFH 24-320 to establish and operate
     OLVIMS. Contact NAF or MAJCOM for additional assistance if required.
     2.24.3. All maintenance performed on vehicles requires documentation IAW procedures
     established by the combatant MAJCOM. OLVIMS is implemented and used as soon as
     practical, normally within 30 days. See Figure A2.2 and Figure A2.3 for publications, TO,
     and forms needed to operate at a deployed site.
        2.24.3.1. (Added-PACAF) . Vehicle management personnel will maintain hand written
        records until OLVIMS support is established. Every effort will be made to establish
        OLVIMS support at the earliest possible date. Upon implementation of OLVIMS, all
        data, previously hand written, will be entered into OLVIMS using the applicable dates.
     2.24.4. Establish a vehicle control point upon arrival at a forward operating location. The
     vehicle control point’s primary function is to establish and maintain accountability for the
     base vehicle fleet as soon as possible. Vehicle fleet size is controlled by AS 019 and/or
     vehicle sets identified in the ―Force Module Construct‖.
     2.24.5. Establish a VCO program. Generate VCO/VCNCO list with 24-hour contact
     information. Brief VCOs/VCNCOs (in mass or individually as mission permits) on official
     use, accident and abuse procedures, use of DD Form 518 and SF 91, Motor Vehicle Accident
     Report, accountability, host nation/local use restrictions, weather/geographic related
     conditions, drivers license requirements, discrepancy reporting, add-on equipment requests,
     other vehicle management procedures, and vehicle related items listed in AFI 24-301,
     Vehicle Operations (mainly drivers license requirements), AFJMAN 24-306 and Chapter
     10.
     2.24.6. Ensure all fleet data is accurately entered into AFIS. AFIS is implemented and used
     as soon as practical, normally within 30 days. Reconcile AFIS with OLVIMS. Generate
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          55


   hand receipts for unit VCOs and/or VCNCOs to review and sign. A VAL may not exist but
   hand receipts are used to establish accountability.
   2.24.7. Create and maintain a tracking system for all commercial leased vehicles. At a
   minimum, the system will contain: License/tag number, lease date, lease length, using
   organization, monthly lease cost, monthly miles traveled, fuel consumption by fuel type,
   PM&I and Special Inspection intervals.
   2.24.8. Create a contingency vehicle MEL and Vehicle Priority Recall Listing (VPRL) if not
   already established. If both listings are already in place, review for accuracy and update if
   required. Route vehicle MEL and VPRL to Expeditionary MSG Commander for final
   approval. Brief vehicle MEL and VPRL purpose and procedures to VCOs and VCNCOs, and
   to Unit Commanders as needed.
   2.24.9. Destroyed/Contaminated Vehicle Replacement. Vehicles may be destroyed or
   rendered unusable by conventional, chemical, biological, radiological or nuclear weapons
   during combat operations. Rotate vehicles from lower to higher priority units to maintain
   base operations. Leasing may be required to fill shortages. Contact NAF or MAJCOM to
   obtain replacement vehicles if necessary. Note: Contaminated vehicles can be considered
   serviceable. Do not abandon or stop reporting items contaminated. Follow guidance in
   paragraph 2.30
2.25. Reporting Requirements. Host MAJCOMs and other AF agencies require information
for decisions necessary to support a deployed unit.
   2.25.1. During the deployment phase, report capability to NAF and MAJCOM weekly or as
   directed. Send information copies to the main operating base and tenant organizations.
   Ensure Vehicle Management personnel at NAF and MAJCOM are aware of Situation Report
   (SITREP) inputs.
      2.25.1.1. During the first 30 days, the following information is required at weekly
      intervals or as directed. It will be provided by classified message or e-mail to the
      combatant MAJCOM Commander, with information copies to the main operating base
      and tenant organizations.
      2.25.1.2. Total priority 1 and priority 2 vehicles assigned, total vehicle losses, and total
      vehicles Non Mission Capable Supply (NMCS) and Non Mission Capable Maintenance
      (NMCM).
      2.25.1.3. Facility, equipment, tools, technical data and part shortfalls.
      2.25.1.4. Personnel and skill shortages.
      2.25.1.5. For specific materiel management support difficulties requiring MAJCOM
      assistance, list vehicle registration number and type, part number, date parts ordered,
      requisition number, and status. MAJCOMs develop procedures for reporting vehicle
      status when repairs exceed local capability (including other military and contract
      sources).
   2.25.2. After the initial 30-day period, initiate reporting from AFIS. Required documents
   are: Ship, Salvage and Rotate Report; Newly Received Vehicle Report; and Host Base
   Transmit/Receive Report. Reports are due to the combatant MAJCOM No Later Than (NLT)
   the 10th of each month.
56                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     2.25.3. The combatant MAJCOM Commander establishes additional reporting requirements
     and timelines.
     2.25.4. Reports Control Symbol. MAJCOMs and other AF agencies assign a reports control
     symbol to recurring and one-time reporting requirements.
2.26. Facilities:
     2.26.1. Facilities at forward operating locations may consist of host nation buildings,
     expandable structures, tents, or other appropriate mobile units. Vehicle Management
     facilities support PM&I, Special Inspections, unscheduled and intermediate levels of
     maintenance. Care needs to be taken in planning to include ample electrical service, wash
     facilities, exhaust ventilation, compressed air source and explosion-proof utility systems for
     refueling vehicle shops. For planning purposes, shop working areas must accommodate
     approximately 5 percent of the fleet at one time in addition to ancillary functions. Refer to
     AFH 32-1084, Facility Requirements, for exact space authorization.
     2.26.2. WRM mobile facility authorizations are outlined in AS 157 (Basic Expeditionary
     Airfield Resources (BEAR)) and AS 158 (Harvest Falcon).
        2.26.2.1. The Vehicle Management Facility is a component of the AS 157 BEAR
        Industrial Operations (B-IO) Set (UTC XFBRC) and a component of the AS 158 Harvest
        Falcon Industrial Operations (IO) Set (UTC XFBTD). It is designed specifically for
        Vehicle Management operations. It contains a large structure for repair operations and a
        smaller shelter for administrative support. The kit also comes with AM-2 matting for the
        large shelter only. VFMs or VMSs need to request and monitor shipment of UTC
        XFBRC in BEAR or UTC XFBTD in Harvest Falcon when operating at an austere
        location without dedicated repair facilities.
     2.26.3. Facilities should be accessible to the key functions supported, e.g., sortie-generating;
     consider placement of repair facilities in close proximity to flight line and Aerial Port
     Operations Center (ATOC). It may be necessary to establish dispersed Vehicle Management
     locations.
     2.26.4. A separate facility for refueling trucks is highly desired. Some contingency locations
     may not have the capability to establish a separate refueling maintenance facility. Those
     operating locations may be driven by necessity to combine with Vehicle Management
     operations. Combined maintenance operations can only be conducted under strict adherence
     to the following guidelines:
        2.26.4.1. Applies only to vehicles transporting diesel or Jet Propulsion (JP)-8.
        2.26.4.2. Properly train all assigned personnel in fuels management safety procedures.
        2.26.4.3. Maximum of one fuel truck inside shop at any time.
        2.26.4.4. Properly ground vehicle with ground reel IAW TO 00-25-172, Ground
        Servicing of Aircraft and Static Grounding/Bonding.
        2.26.4.5. No smoking within 50 feet of vehicle or shop area.
        2.26.4.6. No spark or flame within 50 feet.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         57


       2.26.4.7. A truck or trailer mounted refueling system will not be opened inside the main
       shop. Repairs and service will be limited to the actual prime mover only (chassis,
       exterior, drive train, etc.). Refueling system repairs must be accomplished in designated
       area/shop and will not be accomplished inside a combined Vehicle Management shop.
       2.26.4.8. Drain refueling system fuel storage tank as much as possible prior to entering
       shop to reduce mass spill potential. If the storage tank/system cannot be drained, ensure
       fuel system is completely closed and there are no leaks before entering shop. Comply
       with all installation spill containment procedures.
2.27. Tools and Equipment:
   2.27.1. UTC UFMXK, Vehicle Management Support Kit, is designed to support
   maintenance operations at a bare base location in the 1-30 day range. It is a light, lean, air
   transportable kit limited to one aircraft pallet position. Each UFMXE, Wing Vehicle
   Management Element Team, tasked to support a bare base location should be equipped with
   one UFMXK. If not, immediately contact local TMF, ATOC, Reception Control Center
   (RCC), NAF and/or MAJCOM to determine the UTCs actual location. If known, the TCN
   expedites tracking efforts.
   2.27.2. UTC UFMXT is a heavier follow-on kit designed for arrival in the 30-60 day range.
   The kit contains tire machines, portable shop cranes, wheel dollies, hydraulic hose
   equipment, heavy jacks, etc. This kit should be immediately requested through NAF or
   MAJCOM if operating location is projected to remain open more than 30 days.
2.28. Forward Vehicle Deployment. Forward vehicle deployment refers to moving vehicles
from one forward operating location to new or captured bases. The unit may have minimal
response time to meet forward deployment taskings. New or captured bases will be operating
with minimal support functions. It is imperative that the best vehicles and equipment are forward
deployed. To ensure full MC; the following vehicle shipment standards apply:
   2.28.1. Perform an LTI and service all fluid systems. Vehicle must be safe and serviceable.
   Vehicle must be able to perform assigned mission with no or very minimal support. Vehicle
   will be shipped with an assembled spare wheel/tire and all applicable TOs. Commercially
   designed light and medium duty vehicles and military designed prime movers should be
   equipped with lug wrench(es), jack and jack handle.
   2.28.2. Assemble TMSK with 30-day supply of available working/bench stock items. If time
   permits, purchase any vital parts or supplies not readily available. Include TOs (may require
   copying manual or shipping only available copy). See paragraph 2.15 for TMSK shipment
   guidance.
   2.28.3. Secure OLVIMS data and spare keys in cab or operator’s compartment. Shipping
   base should maintain copy of historical data until gaining location accepts and loads vehicle.
   If shipped data and/ or keys are not readily visible, identify location with a prominently
   placed label.
   2.28.4. Contact NAF or MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs for guidance if unable to
   meet the above standards by the shipment deadline.
2.29. Maintaining Other Government Motor Vehicle Conveyances (OGMVC) and Non-
REMS Reportable LSV in a Contingency Environment. All OGMVCs and non-REMS
58                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


reportable LSVs will be inspected and maintained to manufacturer specifications. This ensures
both safe operations and full life expectancy from AF equipment. When possible, using
organizations will have OGMVCs and non-REMS reportable LSVs maintained through a local
vendor contract. Refer to paragraph 4.20 for additional guidance on tracking OGMVCs and
non-REMS reportable LSVs.
2.30. Contaminated Environment Operations. Detailed guidance for Vehicle Management
operations in a Nuclear, Biological and Chemical environment are contained in AFMAN 10-
2602, paragraphs A4.5. and A4.9.

Section 2F—Reconstitution. Reconstitution in the context of this publication refers to
drawdown and base closure operations after hostilities have ended. Reconstitution includes
activities at home station and the deployed location.

2.31. Personnel (Home Station):
     2.31.1. Training. Evaluate training status after personnel have returned to home station.
     Initiate training for any appropriate areas. Ensure all personnel supporting OPLAN and AEF
     taskings can fulfill MISCAP requirements.
     2.31.2. Reporting: IAW AFI 10-201, Status of Resources and Training Systems (SORTS).
     Accurately report status of all personnel UTCs in the Air and Space Expeditionary Force
     Reporting Tool (ART). Ensure training status and skill level concerns are reflected in the
     comments section. Reporting in Status of Resources and Training System (SORTS) does not
     fulfill ART reporting responsibilities.
2.32. Vehicles (Deployed Location):
     2.32.1. Accountability. Maintain accountability of all vehicles that have been redeployed
     from closing locations. HQ USAF, NAF or MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs will
     provide redeployment/ shipment guidance. Provide current shipping status to NAF and
     MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs as required.
     2.32.2. Disposition Authority (USCENTAF AOR Only). Deployed sites do not have local
     authority to salvage vehicles. For non-critical vehicles that are replacement eligible or have
     exceeded the one-time repair limit, this decision is left to USCENTAF/A4RV. All other
     disposition decisions will be made by the MAJCOM. To request salvage instructions units
     need to submit an AFTO Form 91, Limited Technical Inspection-Motor Vehicle, to
     CENTAF-AUAB, e-mail: uscentafa4lgtv@shaw.af.mil.
     2.32.3. DRMS Procedures. Contact Regional or Zone DRMS Manager for processing
     guidance after a vehicle has been approved for DRMS. Notify NAF or MAJCOM Vehicle
     Management Staffs if unable to locate a Regional or Zone DRMS Manager for your theater
     of operations. If DRMS representation is not able to assist with disposal, the MAJCOM or
     NAF Vehicle Management Staffs will direct disposal IAW DOD 4160.21-M, Defense
     Materiel Disposition Manual, Chapter 8, Abandonment or Destruction (A/D). Some general
     guidance is listed below:
        2.32.3.1. Property cannot be A/D without proper confirmation that necessary Defense
        Militarization (DEMIL) has been completed and certified. DOD 4160.21-M outlines
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                       59


      DEMIL procedures and certification official criteria. Some A/D Officer and witnessing
      party guidance is listed below.
          2.32.3.1.1. The A/D Officer may not be the Accountable Officer, responsible
          Property Officer or serve as a witnessing party to A/D actions.
          2.32.3.1.2. The witnessing party shall attest to having observed actual
          accomplishment of A/ D action. The witnessing party will normally not be involved
          in the receipt, classification or accounting of property.
      2.32.3.2. The accountable activity shall document all actions on or attached to, DD Form
      1348-1A. The 1348-1A will be used to credit the appropriate account.
      2.32.3.3. VM&A personnel will fax, mail or e-mail scanned copy of DRMS issued 1348-
      1A (for each approved asset) to Langley AFB.
      2.32.3.4. Refer to DOD 4160.21-M and https://www.drms.dla.mil/ for more guidance.
   2.32.4. Vehicles Sent to DRMS (USCENTAF AOR Only). All SBSS transactions for the
   AOR are processed at Langley AFB. Before HQ ACC will salvage a vehicle in SBSS they
   require a signed 1348-1A for their records, and this form will have to be generated locally.
   Once the form is filled out and signed by all parties, fax to DSN 965-2801 or scan it and
   email to acc.a4tvf.swa@langley.af.mil.
2.33. Tools and Equipment (Home Station):
   2.33.1. Reporting. Report all equipment UTC status in ART. Ensure reporting is accurate as
   compared against UTC MISCAP. Use comments section to describe details if necessary.
   2.33.2. Replenishment. Air Staff or MAJCOM will issue replenishment guidance. The
   message will contain funding information, points of contact, applicable units and purchase
   deadlines.
60                                             AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


                                              Chapter 3

 THE OBJECTIVES, RESPONSIBILITIES, ORGANIZATION AND PRINCIPLES OF
                  MANAGING THE AF VEHICLE FLEET

Section 3A— Objectives

3.1. Objectives of Vehicle Management. Use economical, reliable and up-to-date procedures
for life cycle management of the AF Vehicle Fleet.
3.2. Application of this Chapter. Managers at all levels use this chapter to ensure they are
adhering to the responsibilities, objectives and principles of Vehicle Management.

Section 3B— Responsibilities

3.3. HQ USAF/A4L Responsibilities.
     3.3.1. Set policy for life cycle management of AF vehicles and vehicular equipment.
     3.3.2. Facilitate MAJCOM programming and funding requests for vehicle infrastructure.
     3.3.3. Manage personnel, training and manpower matters for the career fields.
     3.3.4. Analyze, improve and implement vehicle automated management systems.
3.4. VEMSO Responsibilities. VEMSO is an AF Element assigned to HQ USAF/A4L. They
are tasked as an adjunct staff to Air Staff to work vehicle and equipment issues. Information
regarding VEMSO can be found in Chapter 8 of this instruction.
3.5. WR-ALC Responsibilities. WR-ALC provides Vehicle Management aid in wartime for
AF forces worldwide when needs are beyond the MAJCOM capability. They implement
procedures to meet spare parts and TO shortfalls through emergency procurement actions to
support surge and sustainment phases of contingency operations. Responsibilities include:
     3.5.1. Support central logistics of registered vehicles.
     3.5.2. Provide central logistics support of registered vehicles and vehicular equipment items
     (W200 series management code).
     3.5.3. Implement warranty policy and managing its result.
     3.5.4. Implement manufacturer defect notification and measuring its impact.
     3.5.5. Manage depot-level maintenance for AF vehicle needs.
     3.5.6. Act as the central procurement agency for all AF vehicle purchases.
3.6. MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs Responsibilities.
     3.6.1. Develop supplemental guidance and plans for Vehicle Management to support
     contingency operations in their specific theater of operation.
     3.6.2. Equip and train their Vehicle Management units to fulfill their wartime vehicle
     mission requirements.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                    61


   3.6.3. Program for vehicles, manpower, facilities, shop equipment, technical manuals and
   tools to support organizational and intermediate maintenance concepts for all vehicles
   committed to wartime missions.
   3.6.4. Ensure enough spare parts are available to support contingency operations for a
   minimum of 30 calendar days.
   3.6.5. Manage WRM vehicle assets according to AFI 25-101, as supplemented.
   3.6.6. Request vehicle repair assistance, as necessary, from WR-ALC according to TO 00-
   25-107, Maintenance Assistance.
   3.6.7. Establish minimum reporting requirements to identify on-hand vehicle assets and to
   identify shortages.
   3.6.8. Provide vehicle support for tenant forces identified in OPLANs where MAJCOMs
   have host base responsibilities and ensure host base vehicle management activities update
   supported units in OLVIMS annually with reimbursement distribution code of 3 or 4.
   3.6.9. Identify force structure requirements in support of contingencies.
   3.6.10. (DELETED) .
      3.6.10.1. (DELETED) .
      3.6.10.2. (DELETED) .
   3.6.11. Develop and provide guidance/instructions on the control and management of Air
   Force watercraft to base level Vehicle Management activities as required.
   3.6.12. Provide COCOM reporting and LIMS EV data as directed.
   3.6.13. Assume responsibilities as the Command or Equivalent Account Manager (CAM) for
   the DOD Fleet Fuel Card Program for base-level organizational accounts within their
   MAJCOM. Additional program information and specific responsibilities can be found in
   paragraph 4.4 , DESC-P-8, Government Fuel Card (GFC) Program Roles, Responsibilities
   and Accountability, and DOD 4140.25-M, Volume II, Chapter 16, Government Fuel Card
   Program Management Office Department Of Defense (DOD) Fleet Card, Air Card, And Sea
   Card.
3.7. Wing and Center Commanders or Equivalents Responsibilities.
   3.7.1. Recognize the policies and procedures in this AFI.
   3.7.2. Responsible to the MAJCOM for the management of vehicles and equipment.
   3.7.3. Direct organizational maintenance according to technical directives.
   3.7.4. Support the AF vehicle abuse and accident prevention policy.
3.8. MSG Commanders or Equivalents Responsibilities.
   3.8.1. Act as the installation’s vehicle authorization review authority.
   3.8.2. Review and approve the installation annual vehicle buy submission.
   3.8.3. Approve the installation VPRL and the vehicle MEL.
   3.8.4. Administer the installation vehicle abuse and accident program.
62                                             AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


3.9. LRS Commanders or Equivalents Responsibilities. Ensures vehicles and equipment are
managed and maintained in a safe and serviceable condition with the least expenditure of
manpower, funds and material. They also ensure that:
     3.9.1. Vehicle Management facilities are adequately programmed to eliminate deficiencies
     and appropriate status is maintained for vehicle repair projects in the military construction
     program.
     3.9.2. Material is available to support Vehicle Management.
     3.9.3. Vehicle Management quality standards comply with AF policy.
     3.9.4. Vehicle Management budget programs are accurate and submitted on time.
     3.9.5. Personnel are available, according to mission requirements, to prevent disruption of
     the shop workflow.
     3.9.6. Approve and disapprove all requests that exceed a vehicle’s one-time repair limit, and
     requests for disposition. This authority may be delegated in writing no lower than the VFM
     or VMS. Any recommendation to process a vehicle identified as ―AF critical‖ in the Vehicle
     Management Index File (VMIF) or on command critical vehicles, or vehicles not in
     replacement code A-J, for disposal (salvage) is forwarded to the MAJCOM Vehicle
     Management Staff for final disposition.
     3.9.7. Ensure personnel are properly trained to progress in the 2T3XX Air Force Specialty
     (AFS).
     3.9.8. The rotation of 2T3XX personnel outside the Vehicle Management Flight is limited to
     a period not longer than 18 months within a 3-year period.
     3.9.9. Manage logistics readiness vehicle resources at the installation or activity level.
     3.9.10. Ensure vehicle data reconciliations are accomplished at least monthly to maintain
     accurate vehicle accountability.
     3.9.11. Ensure REMS personnel receive Air Force Equipment Management System
     (AFEMS) and SBSS training.
     3.9.12. Set target dates for beginning and completing repairs on off-season vehicles and
     equipment to ensure their readiness when seasonal needs require their use.
3.10. VFM and VMS Responsibilities. The VFM and VMS are responsible for overall vehicle
fleet management. Responsibilities are as follows.
     3.10.1. Establish a layout for work centers, considering such factors as workflow,
     equipment, tools and supplies. Note: Provide a separate facility for vehicles and equipment
     that transport or dispense combustible materials such as fuel, oil, water-alcohol vehicles,
     hose carts, filter and separator units and so forth.
     3.10.2. Establish local vehicle fleet management procedures for assigning and using
     government owned, leased, or rented motor vehicles. Ensure procedures comply with AF and
     MAJCOM Vehicle Management policy.
     3.10.3. Coordinate on all correspondence above unit-level dealing with Vehicle Management
     issues.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          63


  3.10.4. Ensure maintenance facilities and programs for deficiency elimination are adequate.
  3.10.5. Assign responsibilities and give authority to supervisors to ensure all functions
  within the Vehicle Management Flight operate effectively.
  3.10.6. Resolve technical problems or ask for technical aid to solve problems that involve
  maintenance beyond local capabilities.
  3.10.7. Ensure personnel are available to meet workload demands and productivity of
  assigned personnel is maintained.
  3.10.8. Authorize minimum essential repairs to uneconomically repairable vehicles. Develop
  a Vehicle Management OI prescribing essential repairs to accomplish without written
  approval. Define the repair authority by vehicle components or dollar value, and do not
  exceed the one-time allowance unless authority is delegated IAW paragraph 3.9.6
  3.10.9. Assume the responsibilities of the Functional Commander or Functional Director for
  the Contractor-Operated Parts Store (COPARS) contract, as prescribed by AFI 63-124,
  Performance-Based Services Acquisition (PBSA).
     3.10.9.1. Authorize personnel to order and receive parts from the COPARS store. Keep
     authorizations to a minimum consistent with effective management and control.
         3.10.9.1.1. A current, up-to-date listing of those personnel authorized to purchase
         parts must be posted in the store and a copy kept in the contract file. The list reflects
         the printed name and sample of the individual's signature by organization (as a
         minimum, first and last name) and includes personnel from other organizations using
         COPARS when authorized. Changes are given to the COPARS contractor and
         Materiel Control as they occur.
  3.10.10. Authorize the use of the GPC and ensure its use conforms to prescribed directives.
  3.10.11. Coordinate with the Materiel Management Flight to make sure required supplies are
  available.
  3.10.12. Approve NMCS requisitions.
     3.10.12.1. (Added-PACAF) . VFM/VMS may delegate Non Mission Capable (NMCS)
     requisition approval authority to work center.
  3.10.13. Approve or disapprove all cannibalization requests, or delegate authority in writing.
  3.10.14. Develop an OI to ensure that tire/battery issues and inventory controls are
  implemented to identify fraud, waste and abuse.
  3.10.15. Develop an OI specifying tool control and accountability procedures.
     3.10.15.1. Develop a tool kit list for each AFSC or work center.
     3.10.15.2. Ensure tool kits, shop tools and equipment are safe and serviceable, and used
     for their intended purposes.
     3.10.15.3. Choose the type of toolkit to be used, either an ITK or Composite Toolkit
     (CTK).
     3.10.15.4. Make frequently used special tools available in the work centers.
64                                           AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


        3.10.15.5. Ensure shop equipment requiring an AFTO Form 244 is inspected and
        serviced monthly at a minimum unless more frequently required by manufacturer. Also
        ensure compliance with requirements in Air Force Occupational, Safety and Health
        Standard (AFOSHSTD) 91-66, General Industrial Operations.
        3.10.15.6. Ensure procurement of special tools, test equipment and training for newly
        received vehicles. Note: The latest VEMSO evaluations on new tools and equipment can
        be accessed at the VM CoP.
     3.10.16. Assign responsibility for the technical publications library to the section that can
     maintain it most effectively.
     3.10.17. Perform organizational quality control for AFTO Form 22, Technical Manual (TM)
     Change Recommendation and Reply.
     3.10.18. Develop continuity folders to track major problems, construction projects, long-
     range plans, approved waivers and/or deviations, and unique operating requirements and past
     maintenance practices.
        3.10.18.1. (Added-PACAF) . At a minimum, continuity books will contain all written
        approvals to deviate from prescribed regulatory requirements, unique operating
        requirements, and information pertaining to proposed new construction projects. All
        short tour locations will have work center-oriented continuity books to ensure the smooth
        transition of work center supervisors. VFM/VMSs will determine content.
     3.10.19. Develop and submit an annual Vehicle Management budget. Control expenditures
     during the budget year and act as Cost Center Manager.
     3.10.20. Evaluate training requirements and request formal training by:
        3.10.20.1. Checking training progress and needs by personal observation and
        coordination with supervisors, using VM&A analysis of workload output, reviewing
        recurring maintenance reports, evaluating skill levels and assessing training status
        reports.
        3.10.20.2. Ensuring On-the-Job Training (OJT) is conducted according to AFI 36-
        2201v3, Air Force Training Program On the Job Training Administration, and choose a
        qualified person to set up and administer the training program. Ensure an Air Education
        and Training Command (AETC) Form 156, Training Quality Report (TQR) is submitted
        when technical graduates do not meet the training proficiency level of the approved
        Career Field Education and Training Plan (CFETP). Submit an AETC Form 156 also
        when deficiencies are identified in Career Development Courses (CDCs). Refer to AFI
        36-2201v3 for specific instructions.
        3.10.20.3. Submitting requests for formal training to MAJCOM Vehicle Management
        Staff.
     3.10.21. Perform duties of AF Innovative Development through Employee Awareness
     (IDEA) program OPR for vehicle related suggestions (see AFI 38-401, The Air Force
     Innovative Development Through Employee Awareness (IDEA) Program).
     3.10.22. Provide VCO and VCNCO orientation. See Chapter 10 for further guidance.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         65


  3.10.23. Be familiar with the vehicle buy program and know what new vehicles are due in.
  When such information is available, the VFM or VMS should identify vehicles in
  replacement codes A-J that will be tentatively disposed of when the replacement vehicles are
  received.
  3.10.24. Maintain liaison with and visit using activities. In addition, be aware of their
  mission and operation, and provide technical assistance for organizational maintenance.
  3.10.25. Develop local procedures to ensure all requests to locally purchase equipment that
  Vehicle Management has primary or assistance maintenance responsibility for are
  coordinated through the VFM or VMS. This ensures that maintenance can be performed and
  parts are readily available. The VFM and VMS are not obligated to accept maintenance
  responsibility for equipment if the request to purchase the equipment was not properly routed
  through Vehicle Management for coordination. O&M costs for locally purchased equipment
  are paid by the using organization. VFMs and VMSs also need to be aware that they do not
  earn manpower for locally purchased equipment items. Be very careful when you agree to
  take on maintenance responsibility.
  3.10.26. Take full advantage of part and vehicle warranties as outlined in paragraph
  7.28.16.5 and TO 36-1-191.
