  3.10.27. Control the contract maintenance program IAW PWS and AFI 63-124.
  3.10.28. Ensure proper documentation of vehicle accident and abuse repairs.
  3.10.29. Ensure vehicle deficiency reports are processed IAW USAF Joint Deficiency
  Reporting System (JDRS), TO 00-35D-54, USAF Deficiency Reporting and Investigating
  System, and TO 36-1-191. Act as certifying official for the accuracy and release of
  deficiency reports. Note: JDRS user log-in is mandatory. Contact the DRIS Helpdesk, DSN
  787-5578 or dristeam@dris.wpafb.mil, for ―Originating Point‖ training assistance.
     3.10.29.1. (Added-PACAF) . All reports submitted through the Joint Deficiency
     Reporting System (JDRS) deficiency reporting system will include a courtesy copy e-
     mailed to OL-A PACAF/LGR at olahqpacaf.lgr.uc@robins.af.mil and
     PACAF/A4RVM at pacaf.a4rvm@hickam.af.mil.
  3.10.30. Ensure VM&A maintains vehicle active and historical data IAW paragraph 7.6
  and Table 7.1, and retains/disposes active and historical data IAW Air Force Records
  Disposition Schedule (RDS) located at https://afrims.amc.af.mil/.
  3.10.31. Analyze reports received from VM&A (manpower, MC rates, cost, etc.) to find
  weak or deficient areas, and set up corrective policies and procedures.
     3.10.31.1. (Added-PACAF) . When preparing historical records for offsite vehicle
     transfer action, VM&A will send a copy of the VEH File created by the OLVIMS ―AX‖
     transaction via email to the gaining unit’s (VM&A).
  3.10.32. Review workloads, schedule work assignments, leave schedules, standby rosters
  and recall rosters.
  3.10.33. Look at inspections and quality assurance findings with supervisors and take
  corrective action when it is indicated. Identify specific vehicles, vehicle types or users that
66                                           AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     require an excessive amount of maintenance effort and initiate the process to correct the
     problem.
     3.10.34. Conduct shop meetings with section supervisors to identify and solve maintenance
     problems.
     3.10.35. Conduct weekly Roll Call with all Vehicle Management employees. These weekly
     meetings should help keep Airmen and civilians informed on current issues, clear up
     confusion and dispel rumors, and provide additional face-to-face communication between
     supervisors and their teams. A weekly product, called ―Roll Call‖ highlights the topics that
     supervisors should include in the weekly meetings. Note: The weekly Roll Call requirement
     is not applicable to contracted vehicle management operations.
     3.10.36. Ensure LTIs are prepared promptly and accurately.
     3.10.37. Ensure vehicles requiring an LTI for acceptance, shipping, disposition action and
     repair decisions meet the processing time limits.
     3.10.38. Ensure vehicles are placed in proper condition prior to shipment IAW TO 36-1-191.
        3.10.38.1. Personally inspect all vehicles prior to shipment. (Final shipping inspection
        responsibility may be delegated to the most senior-ranking shop supervisor during the
        absence of the VFM or VMS). For contracted vehicle maintenance units, vehicles must
        be inspected and documentation completed IAW the PWS.
        3.10.38.2. When validated by losing MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff (losing and
        gaining MAJCOM when applicable), the losing unit, including contracted vehicle
        maintenance units, are obligated to reimburse gaining unit for unserviceable conditions
        and damage not caused by shipping.
     3.10.39. Stay abreast of all environmental matters associated with Vehicle Management.
     3.10.40. Promote safety, occupational health and fire prevention. As a minimum:
        3.10.40.1. Refer to AFI 91-202, The US Air Force Mishap Prevention Program, for
        Vehicle Management safety standards, practices and procedures.
        3.10.40.2. Maintain an AF Form 55, Employee Safety and Health Record, for all
        assigned personnel as required by AFI 91-301, Air Force Occupational and
        Environmental Safety, Fire Protection, and Health (AFOSH) Program.
        3.10.40.3. Schedule meetings to discuss safety and hazards at least twice a year.
        3.10.40.4. Ensure surveys of shop noise levels, lighting, fume, and exhaust, paint booth
        and welding extraction systems are performed by the Base Bioenvironmental Engineering
        Section as required (i.e., quarterly, annual, etc.) by regulation, or whenever a major
        change in shop operations occurs that creates a hazardous condition.
        3.10.40.5. Ensure at least two people are in the work center when repairing vehicles.
        When repairs are required after duty hours and/or by mobile maintenance, a qualified
        operator for the type of vehicle being repaired satisfies the two-person requirement when
        the mechanic is a five skill-level or higher.
        3.10.40.6. Satisfactorily complete the safety checklist in AFOSHSTD 91-20, Vehicle
        Maintenance Shops, Attachment 7, at least quarterly. File a copy of the completed
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                        67


       checklist in the Vehicle Management Flight’s safety handbook and retain for 1 year. In
       addition, reference other applicable AFOSHSTDs as identified in AFOSHSTD 91-20.
   3.10.41. Prepare seasonal equipment for use at the start of the operating season. Any local
   procedures must comply with MAJCOM guidance.
   3.10.42. Ensure VM&A updates tenant units in OLVIMS annually with reimbursement
   distribution code 3 or 4.
       3.10.42.1. (Added-PACAF) .      Every effort should be made to ensure all
       reimbursements for vehicle management go directly back into the RC/CC from which
       they were expended.
3.11. Primary Responsibility for Vehicle Management. Vehicle Management provides the
AF with safe and serviceable motor vehicles, watercraft and railroad equipment to meet the war
fighter’s requirements. Vehicle Management is responsible for the management, repair and
accountability of the AF vehicle fleet.
   3.11.1. Organizations procuring non-REMS equipment (i.e., OGMVCs, All-Terrain Vehicles
   (ATVs), mowers, etc.) will coordinate with the VFM or VMS to ensure parts, facilities,
   manpower, funds, etc. are available to support the equipment prior to acquisition.
   Organizations must first consider purchasing a maintenance agreement to support the
   equipment. As a minimum, Vehicle Management will be reimbursed by owning
   organizations for O&M expenditures to equipment maintained by Vehicle Management.
   VM&A will load non-REMS equipment in OLVIMS as refundable/reimbursable (R/D Code
   3 or 4). For vehicle equivalents being calculated for manpower or funding, equivalents will
   be excluded for "X" registration equipment. Maintenance negotiated prior to the release of
   this publication for organizational equipment will be determined by the VFM or VMS for
   O&M reimbursement.
       3.11.1.1. When Vehicle Management is responsible for the non-registered item:
          3.11.1.1.1. Master records are loaded into OLVIMS.
          3.11.1.1.2. Vehicle equivalents are added according to the information in the "Help
          Function" in OLVIMS.
          3.11.1.1.3. Vehicle Management schedules all required inspections, to include PM&I
          and Special Inspections.
          3.11.1.1.4. Using organizations bring equipment to Vehicle Management for
          inspections or repair, or arrange for servicing by mobile maintenance. Information on
          gains or losses is provided to VM&A by the using organization. If units refuse or fail
          to comply with scheduled maintenance requirements for unit-purchased equipment,
          notify the unit VCO or VCNCO, Unit Commander or equivalent, and the host Base
          Safety Office in writing that the equipment is no longer considered safe to operate
          until maintenance requirements are met.
       3.11.1.2. Special tools designed for operator preventive maintenance shipped with a
       specific piece of equipment are transferred with the equipment to the using organization.
       3.11.1.3. Where no repair criterion is established by the Item Manager (IM), the one-
       time repair limit is the lesser of:
68                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


            3.11.1.3.1. 75 percent of the acquisition cost or.
            3.11.1.3.2. Multiply the replacement cost by two and divide the result by the
            expended age in years.
        3.11.1.4. Attachments that originally come with a vehicle or registered piece of
        equipment, for which Vehicle Management has prime responsibility, are maintained or
        replaced by Vehicle Management. If the using organization purchases additional
        attachments for the same vehicle or piece of equipment, it is the using organization's
        responsibility to maintain or replace them unless the VFM or VMS agrees to do so.
        Associated O&M costs are paid by the owning organization.
        3.11.1.5. Maintenance on major specialized systems mounted on standard vehicle chassis
        is the responsibility of the using organization. Specialized systems include, but are not
        limited to, communications equipment, munitions maintenance systems, environmental
        systems, special hoists and sensitive test equipment. Using organizations arrange for in-
        house or contract repair of the equipment. Vehicle Management is only responsible for
        maintaining the basic vehicle body, chassis and power train.
        3.11.1.6. Paint and mark vehicles following guidance in TO 36-1-191, Chapter 2.
        3.11.1.7. Use TO 36-1-191, Chapter 5 to determine the logistics supportability of
        obsolete vehicles. Perform an LTI and make a repair decision when logistics
        supportability is in question.
3.12. Assistance Responsibility for Vehicle Management. When requested, and when within
its capabilities, Vehicle Management will assist organizations owning the vehicles and
equipment listed in the "Help Function" of OLVIMS. Maintenance and parts support for this
equipment will be on a reimbursable basis if deemed necessary by the VFM or VMS. Note: If
recurring maintenance is done on any of these vehicles or equipment by Vehicle Management,
they will be loaded into OLVIMS using the management code in the "Help Function" of
OLVIMS. Scheduled maintenance dates, miles/hours/kilometers, etc., are loaded for all powered
equipment.
3.13. Organizational Responsibilities. Vehicle operators and using organizations are
responsible for and will perform at a minimum the following inspections, servicing, and
maintenance:
     3.13.1. Using the applicable AF Form (AF Form 1800, Operator’s Inspection Guide and
     Trouble Report or AF Form 1807, Operator’s Inspection Guide and Trouble Report (Fuel
     Servicing)), using organizations will perform a vehicle serviceability/functional check of
     vehicles under their control at least weekly. Fire Trucks, Refuelers and 463L equipment will
     be checked daily, if used, or at least weekly. MAJCOM Vehicle Management staff may
     increase the frequency of serviceability/functional checks at their discretion.
        3.13.1.1. Check all fluid levels IAW applicable TOs. General-purpose vehicle operators
        will check and service fuel, engine oil, and the windshield washer reservoir. All other
        fluid levels, i.e., coolant, automatic transmission, power steering, brake and batteries are
        checked by the vehicle operators and reported to Vehicle Management for servicing when
        required. Vehicle Management checks manual transmissions and differential fluid levels
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                        69


     at PM&I intervals. Additionally, for special purpose vehicles, vehicle operators check
     and service hydraulic fluid reservoirs on special units or attachments.
     3.13.1.2. Tire pressure checks/adjustments will be accomplished by the 10th of each
     month and documented on the applicable AF Form 1800 or 1807. Refer to Section 7B—
     Operator's Inspection Guide and Trouble Report Forms for further guidance.
     3.13.1.3. Keep vehicles clean at all times to include the interior. Operators will not
     steam clean engines or engine compartments. Wash vehicles as needed and IAW TO 36-
     1-191, Table 6-3. Wax vehicles often enough with a manual application type wax to
     preserve the painted finish (prevent oxidation), but do not wax vehicles with flat or
     Chemical Agent Resistant Coating (CARC) finishes. Vehicle management will not
     accept dirty vehicles. If excessively dirty vehicles are towed in, the using organization
     should clean the vehicle prior to being accepted in the CSC.
     3.13.1.4. Keep tires properly inflated and change flat tires. Operators may request
     assistance from Vehicle Management for mounting and demounting outsized tires.
     3.13.1.5. Operators assist tire shop personnel in the removal and installation of tires on
     vehicles when vehicles are taken to Vehicle Management for tire-only repair work.
     3.13.1.6. Unit VCOs and VCNCOs ensure adequate assembled spare wheels/tires and
     tools are on hand to support their requirements. Spare wheel/tires received with new
     vehicles will be given to the using organization. If no spare is included with a vehicle as
     original equipment and a unit requires a spare, or if a unit requires more spares, then the
     unit purchases the initial requirement, and vehicle maintenance covers the cost of
     replacement tires after the original purchase.
     3.13.1.7. Tighten loose nuts, bolts and screws, replace light bulbs and windshield wiper
     blades.
     3.13.1.8. Special purpose vehicle operators purchase and replace wire ropes/cables on
     assigned vehicles so equipped. They will immediately notify VM&A of any wire
     rope/cable replacement and provide VM&A with copies of all certification paperwork.
     They also make adjustments to mechanisms affecting operating characteristics of the unit
     (for example, crane and dozer clutches and brakes, power control units, shoes, deflectors,
     etc). Inspect and grease vehicles as required by the TO or manual, and report any
     problems to vehicle management.
     3.13.1.9. Fire truck operators maintain and replace accessory fire fighting equipment
     such as power saws, air breathing apparatus, smoke extractors, ladders, portable fire
     extinguishers, pike poles, prying or cutting tools, nonattached hoses, rescue and first-aid
     equipment, and portable lights or lighting systems, even if they are shipped as part of the
     vehicle purchase.
     3.13.1.10. Medical personnel maintain and replace non-vehicular medical equipment
     such as life sustaining or support equipment, oxygen systems, rescue, and first-aid
     equipment, even if they are shipped as part of the vehicle purchase.
     3.13.1.11. Organizations assigned tracked vehicles procure and replace track shoes.
70                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


        3.13.1.12. Base communications or contract maintenance (arranged for by the using
        organization) repairs two-way mission radio and intercom systems, even if they are
        shipped as part of the vehicle purchase.
        3.13.1.13. Maintenance of locally procured vehicle-mounted equipment and attachments
        costing under $10,000. Note: Organizations must coordinate with the VFM or VMS to
        make sure facilities and manpower are available to support any equipment before it is
        acquired. Associated O&M costs are paid by the owning organization. This topic will be
        briefed at VCO meetings.
        3.13.1.14. Include maintenance and parts publications in the request to locally purchase
        equipment to be supported by Vehicle Management. Send the publications to Vehicle
        Management after the equipment is received. The VFM or VMS do not assume
        management responsibility for locally purchased equipment without the necessary
        technical data if, in their opinion, inspection, servicing, adjustment or repair work cannot
        be performed properly.
        3.13.1.15. Buying jacks, jack handles, lug wrenches, wax, highway warning kits, spare
        tires, wheels, tire chains, fire extinguishers, wheel chocks, placards, shoring, dunnage,
        lubricants, lubrication equipment, starting fluid, windshield washer fluid, special tools,
        and accessories to meet operating requirements. Note: When equipment operators are
        responsible for lubricating equipment before and during use, Vehicle Management may
        advise operators regarding the lubricant to be used, tools needed and frequency of
        lubrication. The using organization procures required tools and lubricants, and is
        responsible for replacing equipment and special tools lost, worn or damaged beyond
        economical repair.
        3.13.1.16. (Added-PACAF) . Using organizations will accomplish initial or diagnostic
        weight testing after major organizational, intermediate, or contractor maintenance is
        performed on assigned cranes, in coordination with Vehicle Management. Using
        organizations will ensure annual weight testing of all nuclear-certified cranes, high-reach,
        derrick, or other boom-equipped vehicles with personnel baskets is accomplished.
        Coordinate with Vehicle Management when performing any weight tests on assigned
        vehicles. Refer to vehicle technical orders and AFOSH Standard 91-46, paragraph 8.2.4.
        for detailed requirements.
     3.13.2. Vehicle Discrepancies. Using organizations ensure delayed discrepancies do not
     affect the vehicle safety or mission. Refer to paragraph 4.10.1
        3.13.2.1. Vehicle operators record maintenance discrepancies as they perform
        inspections, or when discovered. Operators record discrepancies in the appropriate
        section of the applicable Operator's Inspection Guide and Trouble Report, to be reported
        to Vehicle Management within one normal workday.
        3.13.2.2. Operators do not delay discrepancy reporting on systems or devices adversely
        affecting the safety of personnel or the operation of vehicles/equipment. When any of the
        discrepancies listed below are identified, the operator will discontinue use of the vehicle
        and report the discrepancy to Vehicle Management as soon as possible. Note: If the
        discrepancy occurs outside Vehicle Management duty hours, discontinue vehicle use and
        notify Vehicle Management of the discrepancy the next duty day.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         71


          3.13.2.2.1. Tires or brakes.
          3.13.2.2.2. Steering mechanisms.
          3.13.2.2.3. Operating levers controlling power transmission, hoisting, dumping and
          tripping devices. Warning lights such as turn signals, brake lights, emergency and
          rotating flashers.
          3.13.2.2.4. Headlights, reflectors and clearance lights (unless the vehicle or
          equipment is not used during hours of darkness and restrictions are identified by a
          decal).
          3.13.2.2.5. Windshield wipers and defrosters (when weather conditions require them
          to be operated).
          3.13.2.2.6. Other similar safety and warning equipment and devices peculiar to
          special purpose units.
          3.13.2.2.7. Any other condition reasonably considered to be a safety hazard.
   3.13.3. CES Responsibilities. CE personnel will:
       3.13.3.1. Rewrap or change the broom, filter bags, skid plates and deflectors on all
       sweepers. Maintain correct adjustment of brooms, deflectors and caster wheels on all
       sweepers. Change the moldboard cutting edges and shoes on earth-moving and snow-
       removal equipment. Sharpen and change blades and deflectors on grass-cutting
       equipment. Conduct or arrange for weight and dielectric tests and provide documentation
       to VM&A. Replace wire ropes/cables on assigned equipment. They will immediately
       notify VM&A of any wire rope/cable replacement and provide VM&A with copies of all
       certification paperwork. The user and Materiel Management Flight ensure these
       requirements get requisitioning priorities according to the mission being supported. Note:
       The using organization funds for and buys these items and associated hardware such as
       nuts and bolts.
       3.13.3.2. Maintain installed equipment related to the normal CE function, such as stoves,
       refrigerators, heaters, air-conditioners, sanitary facilities, similar CE items mounted in
       government-owned trailers (including house trailers) and truck cargo compartments.
       3.13.3.3. Fund for and maintain real and non-real property equipment assigned on the CE
       Equipment Authorization Inventory Data (EAID) and tenant equipment assigned to CE
       according to AFI 25-201 agreements. This includes mobile (wheeled or skid-mounted)
       engine-driven utility-type generator sets, pumps, air compressors, liquid gas generators,
       house and office trailers, and so forth, to which USAF/AFEMS vehicle registration
       numbers have not been assigned.
       3.13.3.4. Store and inspect seasonal equipment not in possession of Vehicle Management
       every month during off-season months, using the applicable Operator’s Inspection Guide
       and Trouble Report. Fully operationally check motorized equipment during this
       inspection.
3.14. ―Maintenance Purposes Use Only‖ Vehicle Operator Certification. The VFM or VMS
appoints ―Maintenance Purposes Use Only‖ vehicle trainers, in an OI, who will ensure that
personnel are qualified to operate general purpose vehicles and telephone maintenance trucks
72                                                  AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


over 14,000 GVW, passenger vehicles with a carrying capacity of more than 15 passengers,
special purpose vehicles, tactical vehicles, construction equipment, materiel handling equipment,
and railway equipment (locomotives or cranes) for maintenance purposes before authorizing use.
     3.14.1. Follow procedures in AFI 24-301, paragraph 8.21.
     3.14.2. Personnel will retain a copy of the most current completed and signed AF Form(s)
     171 when transferring to another unit and give to new supervisor.
     3.14.3. (DELETED) . NOTE: ―Maintenance Purposes Use Only‖ vehicle operator
     certification will not satisfy local law enforcement licensing requirements if vehicles are not
     properly licensed for off base/site use. Check with local law enforcement authorities to
     ensure compliance with local laws if vehicles are tested off base/site. All personnel who
     operate AF vehicles must have a valid AF Form 2293, USAF Motor Vehicle Operator
     Identification Card. Contractor employees must follow procedures in AFI 24-301, paragraph
     8.10.

Section 3C— Organization

3.15. Organization of Vehicle Management. Organize the Vehicle Management activity IAW
AFI 38-101, Air Force Organization. Follow the guidance in AFI 38-101 if directed to contract
Vehicle Management (See Figure 3.1 for a typical shop organization chart). All Vehicle
Management functions are consolidated under the VFM and VMS. HQ USAF/A4LE is the
approval authority for requests to deviate from consolidation. Exception: Mobile units with
organic maintenance capability, having separate Vehicle Management facilities, sufficient
manpower and an organizational structure, usually including VM&A and Materiel Control,
maintain their own equipment when in garrison. These units may be consolidated under the
installation VFM; however, they do not require HQ USAF/A4LE approval to operate
independently.
3.16. Maintenance Work Centers. Establish work centers as focal points for the labor, parts,
and tools needed to do the job. Determine the number of work centers by the type and quantity of
vehicles to be serviced and the location of shop buildings. The work center supervisor is
responsible for all work done in the work center.
3.17. Administration Section. If applicable, the administration section performs administrative
functions as directed by the VFM or VMS.
3.18. Battery Service Center:
     3.18.1. Maintain an adequate stock of batteries to give quick service.
     3.18.2. Test, fill and charge all batteries.
     3.18.3. Keep all batteries under lock and key to prevent theft.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                           73


Figure 3.1. Sample Vehicle Management Organization Chart.




Note :
*1. Except where approved by HQ USAF/A4LE, consolidate all Vehicle Management functions
under the VFM or VMS. Exception: Mobile units with organic maintenance capability.
2. The VFM or VMS typically establishes minor maintenance, lubrication, mobile maintenance,
tire repair and battery shop work centers under CSC.
3. The total number of work centers required depends on facilities, staffing and type of vehicles.
4. If needed, the VFM or VMS can place other work center supervisory responsibilities under
VM&A.
   3.18.4. Keep all assigned equipment, such as battery chargers, tools and safety equipment in
   good operating condition. Comply with all applicable safety standards.
   3.18.5. Use an AF Form 1827, Minor Maintenance Work Order, work order number J9998,
   to account for direct labor hours spent in battery servicing that cannot be accounted for
   against a specific vehicle (see Chapter 7 for documentation procedures).
   3.18.6. Refer to AFOSHSTDs 91-20, 91-66 and 91-501, Air Force Consolidated
   Occupational Safety Standard, for additional guidance.
3.19. CSC. CSC is the POC between the vehicle user and Vehicle Management. CSC
technicians debrief vehicle operators and perform incoming inspections on vehicles for the
purpose of determining maintenance requirements. Note: The VFM or VMS determines (in an
OI) the extent of completed work to be inspected, what types of repairs and services are
inspected, and by whom. The skill level of personnel, the vehicle complexity and critical mission
support are determining factors. Generally, all completed PM&I, steering and brake repairs
receive an outgoing inspection. The technician in charge of this section is well experienced in all
aspects of Vehicle Management. In this section, consideration of the needs of the using
organization is given to avoid unnecessary vehicle downtime and increase MC time by providing
74                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


service within the shortest turn-around time possible. Quality and service is the byword of this
section; it must be readily accessible and recognizable to the customer. VFM and VMS ensure
this section provides timely service. When necessary, personnel from other sections are used
during peak workload periods. Specific responsibilities of CSC include the following:
     3.19.1. Provide fast and dependable service to the user.
     3.19.2. Debrief vehicle operators.
     3.19.3. Verify malfunctions and perform a complete inspection using diagnostic test
     equipment when required. Use AF Form 4355, Vehicle Incoming Inspection, to document
     vehicle’s condition. Note: Using AF Form 4355 to validate vehicle’s safe operating
     condition, whenever a vehicle is turned in for maintenance or at least annually, will satisfy
     the annual safety inspection requirements listed in DOD 4500.36R.
     3.19.4. Determine if the malfunction is a result of suspected accident or abuse, and if so, take
     proper action. Waiver only non-essential work. Using the appropriate series Operator’s
     Inspection Guide and Trouble Report as a permanent waiver card is optional at the discretion
     of the VFM or VMS. Alternatives for tracking waivered items can be established through the
     use of a computer listing, card file index, etc.
        3.19.4.1. (Added-PACAF) . In the interest of standardization throughout the command,
        all vehicle management functions will use an Automated Waiver Program (AWP) or the
        appropriate 1800 series AFTO Form as a means of documenting permanently waivered
        items. If the AFTO Form is used, the words ―Permanent Waiver‖ will be written at the
        top of both the front and back of the AFTO Form to be used. ―X‖ out the AFTO Form
        from opposing corners on the front and back of the form. All markings on the outside of
        the form are accomplished in red. Only those individuals designated in writing by the
        VFM/VMSs are authorized to waiver maintenance. Personnel waivering maintenance
        must print and sign their names to all discrepancies for which they are waivering
        maintenance to include the date waivered. When using the automated program, quarterly
        updates will be provided to the unit Vehicle Control Officer (VCO).
     3.19.5. Delay work when necessary, only when safety defects are not involved and when
     deficiencies will not cause further damage to or problems with the vehicle. Complete
     delayed/deferred work as soon as is practical, i.e., parts are on hand and vehicle is in the
     shop.
     3.19.6. Perform minor maintenance as required. Portable test equipment and a small
     working/bench stock enhance the CSC operation. The CSC and outlying work centers use AF
     Form 1827 for repairs that take no more than 2 total labor hours time for all jobs required and
     requires only the installation of low-cost stock parts. Do not use the AF Form 1827 for
     PM&I, Special inspections, TCTOs, SBs and OTIs. The AF Form 1827 will not be used
     when the total repair time (including awaiting maintenance, awaiting parts and actual labor)
     exceeds 2 hours. A normal work order will be processed to capture NMC downtime
     exceeding the 2-hour limit. The AF Form 1827 will not be used to record multiple jobs on the
     same vehicle during the same repair time frame. Each line on the AF Form 1827 is
     interpreted as a separate work order in OLVIMS.
     3.19.7. Vehicle and Equipment Work Order and Vehicle Processing (Main Shop). When the
     vehicle operator reports to the CSC/shop with the vehicle inspection guide, the operator stays
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                           75


   with the vehicle until the inspection and debriefing are complete. Operators will perform
   required operator care, to include interior and exterior cleanliness, before turning the vehicle
   over to the CSC. Processing steps essentially follow the pattern below (the VFM or VMS
   may adjust procedures for vehicle in-processing as necessary to meet local conditions and
   mission):
      3.19.7.1. Using the Operator’s Inspection Guide and Trouble Report form along with the
      AF Form 4355, the inspector makes a complete inspection to verify the vehicle's
      malfunctions, validate waived items and to ensure repairs that effect safe vehicle
      operation are addressed. CSC personnel use the proper diagnostic and test equipment to
      identify and isolate the malfunctions when required.
      3.19.7.2. The CSC determines if there are any delayed/deferred or scheduled inspections
      due. Install delayed parts that have been received, workload permitting.
      3.19.7.3. The CSC will initiate an AF Form 1823/1823-1 if the vehicle requires any one
      of the following:
          3.19.7.3.1. PM&I, Special Inspections, TCTO, SB or OTI are required/due.
          3.19.7.3.2. Repair action takes two or more hours to complete.
          3.19.7.3.3. Vehicle/equipment NMC downtime has been longer than two hours. See
          paragraph 3.31
          3.19.7.3.4. If required part used is other than low-cost bench/working stock.
      3.19.7.4. The CSC enters the actual/suspected malfunctions on the AF Form 4355, to
      include all tests that have been performed, and the direct labor-hours spent to perform the
      inspections and tests, and forward (and AF Form 1823/1823-1 if processed in the CSC) to
      VM&A.
      3.19.7.5. The "look phase" of PM&I, lubrications, and oil filter changes may best be
      performed by the CSC section. Enter labor-hours for this work on the AF Form
      1823/1823-1.
      3.19.7.6. The VFM or VMS determines which outgoing quality inspections will be done.
          3.19.7.6.1. (Added-PACAF) . As a minimum, 10% of all unscheduled maintenance
          and 100% of all PM&I’s, Time Compliance Technical Order (TCTO), Service
          Bulletins as well as all other scheduled maintenance will have a Quality Control
          inspection conducted.
      3.19.7.7. Perform road tests as needed. Ensure road test locations are approved in
      advance through SFS and wing safety.
3.20. Lubrication Center:
   3.20.1. VFM or VMS may request adjustment of lubrication intervals, and engine oil and
   filter change intervals (PM&Is) when justified by local operational conditions. Changes to
   intervals in TO 36-1-191 are supported by written justification and approved by the
   MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff.
76                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     3.20.2. Inspect vehicles by the visual and feel method during lubrication. Report deficiencies
     noted during this inspection to VM&A. Assign a qualified technician to the lubrication work
     center to ensure the quality of inspections during the lubrication process.
3.21. Shop Facilities:
     3.21.1. The AF has a large investment in Vehicle Management shops because the majority of
     intermediate maintenance is done in these fixed facilities. Productivity is increased by using
     new methods and procedures to get the most out of personnel, tools and space. For example,
     to have good workflow, locate VM&A and the CSC in places that are easy for customers to
     reach. Ideally, related work centers are located close together.
     3.21.2. Use AFI 32-1024, Standard Facility Requirements, as a guide to compute total space
     needs to provide adequate facilities, to identify deficiencies in the shop, and as the basis to
     initiate corrective action.
     3.21.3. Send requests for real property construction, modification or changes to the CE on
     AF Form 332, Base Civil Engineer Work Request.
     3.21.4. Send requests for maintenance or repair of real property facilities to the CE.
     3.21.5. Activities that do not have standard AF shops develop a plan to use the shop areas to
     gain the most efficiency and productivity. The VFM or VMS consider the following in their
     plans:
        3.21.5.1. Type, size and number of vehicles to be worked on.
        3.21.5.2. Type of work and service to be done.
        3.21.5.3. Time needed to do a job.
        3.21.5.4. Space required for each type of repair.
        3.21.5.5. Locations of water, air, electrical outlets and exhaust fume ventilators.
        3.21.5.6. Location of shop tools, such as hydraulic floor jacks, transmission jacks,
        portable lubrication equipment, etc.
        3.21.5.7. Locations of COPARS, VM&A, CSC and Materiel Control are as close to each
        other as possible. Be sure that the CSC section is easy for vehicle users to find.
        3.21.5.8. Size of the shop parking area.
        3.21.5.9. Location of vehicle publications.
3.22. Tire Repair Section:
     3.22.1. Repair all vehicle tires.
     3.22.2. Maintain all assigned tire repair and servicing equipment in a safe operating
     condition.
     3.22.3. Ensure strict compliance with safety standards.
     3.22.4. The vehicle operator has primary responsibility for removing and installing mounted
     tires; however, Vehicle Management personnel remove and install mounted tires once the
     vehicle has been accepted into the shop, unless it has been previously agreed upon that the
     operator will provide assistance.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          77


   3.22.5. Use an AF Form 1823/1823-1 to cost new or recapped tires that are put on vehicles
   (see Chapter 7 for documentation).
   3.22.6. Use an AF Form 1827, work order number J9998, to account for direct labor hours
   spent in tire repair that cannot be accounted for against a specific vehicle (see Chapter 7 for
   documentation).
   3.22.7. Personnel assigned to the Tire Shop will be thoroughly trained in all aspects of tire
   inspection and repair procedures. Document training certification in appropriate military and
   civilian training records. Copies of TOs 36-1-191 and 36Y32-1-142, Organizational, Direct
   Support, and General Support Maintenance Care, Maintenance and Repair of Pneumatic
   Tires and Inner Tubes, will be available in the Tire Shop. Personnel must be familiar with the
   instructions outlined in these publications. Exercise extreme caution when working with
   split-rim wheels. Refer to AFOSHSTD 91-20 for additional guidance.
3.23. Training Leader. The Vehicle Management Training Leader sets up and administers a
training program as outlined in Chapter 6 and AFI 36-2201 V3, Air Force Training Program
On The Job Training Administration.
3.24. VM&A. VM&A is the focal point for determining repairs and authorizing the expenditure
of manpower and material through the work centers. It is also the focal point for the movement
of vehicles and equipment to and from the work centers and for commercial contract repair
activities. VM&A ensures the efficient and economical operation of the base vehicle fleet.
VM&A oversees the Vehicle Control Program (VCP), Fleet Analysis and REMS functions.
Specific responsibilities are outlined in Chapter 4.
3.25. Work Center Supervisors. Are responsible for:
   3.25.1. Coordinating with VM&A to ensure priorities are met and maintenance tasks are
   completed on time.
   3.25.2. Assigning work to personnel commensurate with their skills.
   3.25.3. Ensuring that proper tools and equipment are readily available and serviceable, and
   that subordinate personnel are properly trained in their use. The supervisor reports shortages
   and deficient equipment to the VFM or VMS.
   3.25.4. Ensuring technicians comply with safety procedures and technical data. Note:
   Complying with technical data does not mean an open book reference for each repair task. It
   does require the technician to be familiar with the procedures for each job. Complex repair
   tasks, performance specifications, torque ratings, special tolerance adjustments and so forth,
   do require reference to technical data, and, in some cases, repeated reference at the job
   location. Technical data for vehicles or vehicular equipment, including nuclear certified
   assets, must be current. Any of the following data sources, in printed or digital form, are
   acceptable: TOs; commercial manuals, printed material, microfilm or software provided by
   or procured from the asset manufacturer; commercially procured after-market parts and
   repair manuals, such as Chilton® Manuals; or digitized technical data such as Mitchell1® or
   its equivalent.
   3.25.5. Inspecting incoming vehicles and equipment not processed through CSC. The
   supervisor coordinates with VM&A if additional repairs not listed on the AF Form
   1823/1823-1 are required and revises the Estimated Time In Commission (ETIC) as needed.
78                                           AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     3.25.6. Inspecting repaired vehicles and equipment to ensure all vehicles are in a safe
     serviceable condition.
     3.25.7. Briefing newly assigned personnel.
     3.25.8. Assigning personnel to duty positions to ensure full use and progression
     opportunities.
     3.25.9. Determining the most efficient and economical means of returning vehicles to
     service. The supervisor will carefully consider the repair or replacement of individual
     assemblies or subassemblies and components to make effective use of resources. In addition,
     adhere to any safety and serviceability standards, and avoid ―over-maintaining‖ the vehicle.
     3.25.10. Informing VM&A of the requirement for more work so that maximum productivity
     may be obtained from assigned personnel.
     3.25.11. Checking with Materiel Control on parts requirements and availability.
     3.25.12. Accounting for labor hours for work center.
     3.25.13. Setting up training needs, sending training requirements to the VFM and VMS, and
     assisting in OJT.
     3.25.14. Ensuring parts received for vehicles during the work phase are properly protected
     and not improperly stored on the vehicle’s seat or other soft trim.
     3.25.15. Ensuring vehicles are properly prepared and maintained for storage when placed in
     NMCS status (see TO 36-1-191).
     3.25.16. (Added-PACAF) . All deadlined vehicles will be preserved at storage level ―C‖ as
     prescribed in T.O. 36-1-191, Chapter 8, Storage and Shipment, unless stored inside. All
     vehicles stored outside, exposed to the elements while awaiting parts, will be preserved in
     accordance with the above reference and inspected for condition every 30 days. Battery
     ground cables will be disconnected at the battery on vehicles down for parts longer than five
     days. All disassembled components are to be tagged and stored in such a manner as to
     prevent deterioration. A placard will be readily displayed on, or in, deadlined vehicles.
     Units will use the NMCS informational ―placard‖ produced by OLVIMS or a locally
     fabricated placard containing OLVIMS info at a minimum.

Section 3D—Principles

3.26. Cannibalization Rules. The VFM and VMS use cannibalization primarily to meet
mission goals. Cannibalization action is documented according to Chapter 7 and proper cost
accounting will be done.
     3.26.1. MAJCOM or WR-ALC may direct the repair of critical vehicles pending disposition.
     Cannibalization of the major components or assemblies of critical vehicles (as identified in
     the VMIF https://sevpgm.robins.af.mil/vehicle/vmif ) pending disposition instructions must
     be approved by the MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff.
     3.26.2. The AFEMS (C001) provides an on-line query, with the exception management code
     ID (IIEM), to determine the vehicle criticality. A critical vehicle is identified by the
     exception management code ―C‖.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                            79


   3.26.3. The VMIF also identifies vehicles as critical or non-critical.
3.27. Contract Operated Vehicle Management Activities. All Performance Based Work
Statements (PWS) for vehicle management should be performance-based. Vehicle management
functional managers at all levels should use AFI 63-124, Performance-Based Services
Acquisitions (PBSA) and this AFI (citing specific chapters and/or paragraphs) as the basis for
developing a performance-based PWS. Also, Chapter 9, Quality Assurance Personnel should be
reviewed for additional information concerning contract activities. Note: It is not mandatory to
rewrite PWS' completed prior to the publication of AFI 63-124, dated 1 Aug 05. However, once
those contracts expire, AFI 63-124 and its requirements will have to be followed when
developing new PWS’.
3.28. Deficiency, Warranty and Unsatisfactory Reporting. Reporting deficiencies, warranty
repairs and unsatisfactory conditions for vehicles and equipment is mandatory. See TOs 36-1-
191 and 00-35D-54 for policy and reporting procedures.
3.29. Maintenance Priorities. Each Vehicle Management activity applies priorities to support
the mission and customer needs. The MSG Commander or equivalent approves these priorities,
which are set as follows:
   3.29.1. MEL for vehicles are developed and verified each year between using organizations
   and the LRS. The MEL shows the number of vehicles, by authorized type, any substitutes,
   that can be in the shop at one time and not seriously affect the user's mission.
       3.29.1.1. (Added-PACAF) . A current Minimum Essential Level (MEL) list will be
       located in VM&A for reference. VM&A will notify the VFM/VMS when an
       organization’s MEL is exceeded. The automated MEL function in OLVIMS should not
       be used as the sole determinant for establishing RED priority maintenance for vehicles.
   3.29.2. The VFM and VMS review the vehicle MEL for maintenance priorities and for
   backfilling primary vehicles when vehicles are in Vehicle Management. Questions on the
   proposed vehicle MEL and any problems in maintaining the levels are resolved with the
   using organization before the final publication of the list. Normally, it is not possible to have
   100 percent of any vehicle type in an organization listed as MEL. Allowance must be made
   for scheduled maintenance, normal breakdowns, etc. The vehicle MEL is presented to the
   MSG Commander or equivalent for approval. This list serves as the vehicle maintenance
   priority repair list.
   3.29.3. Vehicle Management assigns a "routine" priority to all vehicles, regardless of type or
   use, unless one of the conditions in the following paragraph applies.
       3.29.3.1. Use a RED priority when one or more of these conditions exists:
           3.29.3.1.1. A unit is below the minimum essential vehicle level, further loss of
           vehicles will degrade mission support and other base assets cannot fulfill the need of
           a particular vehicle.
           3.29.3.1.2. A special project requires a certain type of vehicle in service.
           3.29.3.1.3. Severe weather or other natural circumstances create a need for certain
           types of vehicles.
80                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     3.29.4. Vehicle Management ensures that minimum essential vehicle levels and mission
     needs are met. This may require withdrawing vehicles from organizations currently above
     their MEL or with lower priorities. Within Vehicle Management, it may be necessary to
     consolidate the work force, work overtime, cannibalize parts, delay work or make temporary
     repairs to return priority vehicles to service.
     3.29.5. Installed emergency warning lights, military radios or other such accessories do not
     automatically cause a vehicle to be a higher priority. Like and possibly dissimilar vehicles
     without such accessories are generally sufficient to perform the mission until the equipped
     vehicle is returned to service.
     3.29.6. When a replacement vehicle is temporarily given to a user, the prime vehicle
     receives a routine maintenance priority.
3.30. Modification Policy. Process major modifications to vehicles and equipment as follows:
     3.30.1. Change configuration only when the customer needs cannot otherwise be met. Note:
     Secondary restraint systems (airbags) will not be disabled unless approved by the National
     Highway Transportation Safety Administration (NHTSA). Wing-level, and MAJCOM
     Safety and Vehicle Management areas, prior to submission to the NHTSA, will validate
     requests for such action.
     3.30.2. Adding special equipment or a commercial optional part or accessory to meet certain
     operational needs is not considered a modification if the vehicle is still used for its original
     purpose. Requesting organizations send written add-on equipment justification to Vehicle
     Management. If approved, when workload and resources permit, Vehicle Management may
     elect to install these items. Requests to add special equipment (add-ons) to nuclear certified
     assets must be coordinated with Vehicle Management and Base Safety Office prior to
     installation IAW AFI 91-103, Air Force Nuclear Safety Design Certification Program. File
     written authorization to install equipment in the permanent portion of the vehicle record
     jacket. Comply with established safety standards when installing these items. Note: Using
     organizations budget for initial and replacement items, such as air conditioners, camper
     shells, hydraulic tailgate lifts, cargo covers, bed liners, light bars, radios and special
     equipment needed to meet special operational requirements. The using organization provides
     necessary funds for the installation of these items at the time of purchase. Likewise, the using
     organization funds for damages from installation of such items when the vehicle is identified
     for rotation and redistribution. In addition, the add-on equipment will be retained by the
     original organization.
        3.30.2.1. Requesting organizations send written change justification to Vehicle
        Management for add-on equipment/changes to government leased vehicles. If approved,
        VM&A will submit to leasing agency (i.e., GSA) to obtain approval for installation of
        add-on equipment or changes to vehicle. Leasing agency's concurrence or non-
        concurrence will be maintained in the requesting organization’s vehicle control records in
        VM&A.
        3.30.2.2. Add-on equipment will be assigned vehicle equivalents and captured in
        OLVIMS for government owned assets. Vehicle Fleet Managers should take the
        following guidance into consideration when deciding whether or not to claim additional
        equivalents for locally added or factory-installed optional equipment:
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                        81


         3.30.2.2.1. Items are only claimed once, regardless of how many are on the vehicle.
         Examples are pintle hooks on bobtails, roof mounted air conditioning units on buses,
         etc.
         3.30.2.2.2. Some examples of items not to count as add-on equipment are standard
         (original equipment) shelving, bins, flashing lights, additional wiring on ambulances,
         standard plows and blades on snow plows and graders, standard AM/FM radios, anti-
         lock brakes, air bags, mud flaps and electronic fuel injection systems.
         3.30.2.2.3. (Added-PACAF) . Vehicles enhanced with addition of a pintle hook
         will be permanently marked with the maximum towing capacity stenciled
         prominently in the general area to the pintle hook as practical.
  3.30.3. Bases must get MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff approval prior to modifying
  vehicles. MAJCOMs must get approval for modifications from the prime ALC. The prime
  ALC ensures the configuration changes to special mounted equipment is documented in
  appropriate technical data and that necessary adjustments are made to logistics support plans.
  Permanent local modifications to special mounted equipment are usually not approved unless
  required to correct isolated problems. Controlled vehicles are: aircraft and ground support
  equipment tow tractors, major crash fire rescue vehicles, 463L MHE, aircraft refuelers,
  compressed gas servicing equipment, special aircraft and missile cranes, personnel lifting
  mechanisms on high reach trucks or cranes, M-series tactical vehicles, support equipment in
  the W-series USAF management codes and munitions MHE. Additional guidance is provided
  in AFI 91-103, Air Force Nuclear Safety Design Certification Program, for nuclear certified
  assets.
3.31. NMC Hours:
  3.31.1. NMC hours start at the time the customer signs in at the Vehicle Management CSC
  shop. The date and time is also entered on the Operator’s Inspection Guide and Trouble
  Report as the date/time that the discrepancy is reported to Vehicle Management. The CSC
  adjusts the start time to account for actual downtime beginning with any preliminary wrecker
  service or mobile maintenance support. Adjustments should be coordinated with VM&A and
  Vehicle Operations Dispatch to confirm the operator’s original request for repair assistance.
  Upon VFM or VMS request, VM&A provides a NMC report reflecting hours controlled by
  Vehicle Management (in-house) and repair hours not controlled by Vehicle Management
  (contract, warranty, etc.). NMC time ends after completion and verification of all
  maintenance actions.
  3.31.2. To support MAJCOM management programs, separate MC percentage goals can be
  established to apply as a metric (management indicator). This may be by major vehicle type
  or overall fleet. Note: The MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs may exclude reporting
  NMC hours for excess vehicles awaiting disposition instructions, vehicles in depot and
  seasonal equipment during the off season such as snow removal, deicing equipment and
  lawnmowers. Additionally, MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs may exclude reporting
  NMC hours for vehicles owned or under the control of the Advanced Power Technology
  Office (APTO) located at Robins AFB. These vehicles are placed in fleets around the AF to
  collect O&M data in an effort to develop and perfect new technologies for AF use.
  Significant NMC hours are expected during these tests. Vehicle downtime begins when the
  vehicle is turned in for maintenance or when a request for maintenance support (wrecker,
82                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     mobile, etc.) is received. Vehicles awaiting accident, abuse and repair decisions/repairs will
     draw downtime. This includes those awaiting repair decisions by MAJCOM, WR-ALC or
     local.
     3.31.3. NMCS vehicles are not normally repaired until all the parts have been received,
     unless approved by the VFM or VMS. For example, an engine received for a crash fire
     fighting vehicle may be installed even though a required converter has not been delivered.
     After the engine is installed, the status of the vehicle reverts to NMCS. The supply priority
     for the converter is not downgraded. Note: Vehicles on NMCS status should be prime
     candidates for corrosion control repairs. Remove the vehicle from NMCS status in OLVIMS
     only until the corrosion repairs are completed, then return the vehicle to NMCS status until
     the parts are received.
     3.31.4. Use MC data to support manning, shop equipment, vehicle replacement criteria, new
     vehicle buy budgets and reliability and deployment programs.
3.32. Reclamation Procedures:
     3.32.1. Accomplish reclamation to the extent necessary before or after processing to DRMS.
     VM&A coordinates with using organizations for removal of organizational equipment prior
     to transferring a vehicle to DRMS. Document removed parts on AFTO Form 91. MAJCOM
     Vehicle Management Staffs establishes policy regarding retention of DRMS-bound vehicles
     for purposes of parts reclamation or for training purposes.
        3.32.1.1. (Added-PACAF) . PACAF vehicle management flights are authorized to
        retain vehicles for parts reclamation within the following guidelines:
        3.32.1.1.1. (Added-PACAF) VM&A will place vehicles retained for reclamation in
        status code "E", ASC code 048 (excess). Establish a 180-day suspense.
            3.32.1.1.2. (Added-PACAF) . Do not retain vehicles longer than 180 days after
            receipt of disposal instructions.
     3.32.2. Withdraw vehicles from DRMS for special projects or an authorized need upon
     written MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff approval. VFM and VMS provide technical
     assistance in selecting vehicles to be withdrawn. Requirements for withdrawing vehicles
     from DRMS are in AFMAN 23-110, USAF Supply Manual, Volume 2, Part 2.
     3.32.3. VFM or VMS will monitor the repair and turn-in of vehicle parts to ensure
     serviceable parts with a foreseeable need are not turned in for disposal. To reduce the
     potential for fraud, waste and abuse, inventory and store serviceable, non-credit turn-in parts
     for which there is a projected need, as work order residue.
3.33. Staff Assistance. MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs provide staff assistance to the
base Vehicle Management activity. A visit is made when required by the MAJCOM or requested
by the senior commander or equivalent, and approved by the MAJCOM.
3.34. Shop Publications. Necessary technical literature, including TOs and service manuals
will be available at all times. Technical data for vehicles or vehicular equipment, including
nuclear certified assets, must be current. Any of the following data sources, in printed or digital
form, are acceptable: Current TO or commercial manual; printed material, microfilm or software
provided by or procured from the asset manufacturer; commercially procured after-market parts
and repair manuals, such as Chilton® Manuals; or digitized technical data such as Mitchell1®.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                             83


When conflict occurs between technical data sources, or questions arise about the accuracy of
any technical data, repair procedures or replacement parts, other than AF-directed inspection
criteria, the final decision authority lies with the representative or dealer for the manufacturer of
the vehicle or equipment item in question. Rationale being the manufacturer or their
representative should have the latest procedures and parts information available.
   3.34.1. Set up a central publication file accessible to all work centers.
       3.34.1.1. Geographically separated work centers will have current publications such as
       TO 36-1-191, AFOSHSTDs, etc., available in printed or digital form to prevent wasted
       travel time to the central library. The work center supervisor, with VFM or VMS
       approval, determines which publications are needed in their work center.
   3.34.2. Order commercial books or TOs when new vehicles are received without
   publications, using the emergency ordering procedures in TO 00-5-1, AF Technical Order
   System.
   3.34.3. (Added-PACAF) . In locations where foreign nationals are employed, publications
   will be maintained in English and the host country language as locally determined by vehicle
   management to be feasible. In locations where local national supervision is fluent in English
   and can perform translating functions, only critical information areas of listed publications
   are required to be maintained in a bilingual format. Critical information can be defined by
   the VFM/VMS.
3.35. Technical Publications. Report deficiencies on AFTO Form 22 IAW TO 00-5-1. Return
all excess copies of new vehicle or equipment TOs promptly to the appropriate ALC as required
by TO 00-5-1.
3.36. The VCP in the Using Activity. Provide vehicle status to the using organization’s VCO
or VCNCO. VM&A maintains a complete and current list of these individuals, to include:
   3.36.1. Name, grade, telephone number and email address of the person(s).
   3.36.2. Name of the organization, its assigned code and mailing address.
   3.36.3. Reference Chapter 10 for further information regarding VCO and VCNCO
   requirements.
3.37. Vehicle Redistribution. Ensure vehicles and equipment designated for shipment meet
serviceability standards. Local Traffic Management Flight will assist with guidance on funding
the transportation costs associated with an RDO as provided in AFI 24-201, Cargo Movement,
Chapter 3. Unless directed by the parent MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff for intra-
command shipments, for shipments between commands, vehicles are not redistributed when they
reach replacement eligibility as outlined in TO 36-1-191. The VFM or VMS certifies on an
AFTO Form 91 that the vehicle being shipped meets serviceability standards.
3.38. Vehicle Improvement Working Group (VIWG). The VIWG is established to improve
the communications between MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs and the Vehicle System
Manager located at WR-ALC. The VIWG meets annually, or as directed, to review deficiency
and unsatisfactory reports, and to discuss technical matters. TO 36-1-191 stipulates the
responsibilities of the VIWG.
84                                    AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


3.39. Vehicle Transformation Acquisition Council (VTAC). The VTAC is established to
provide a forum for discussion of Vehicle Management issues between HQ USAF/A4LE and
MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs The VTAC meets annually or as directed, normally in
conjunction with the VIWG.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         85


                                           Chapter 4

                         VEHICLE MANAGEMENT & ANALYSIS

Section 4A—Managing the Maintenance Workload

4.1. Vehicle Management & Analysis. Vehicle Management & Analysis (VM&A) is
responsible for the efficient and economical operation and maintenance of the base vehicle fleet.
The element is responsible for accountability of the vehicle fleet, analysis and scheduling of
maintenance requirements, base vehicle buy submissions, establishing and managing the vehicle
control program, and general analysis.
4.2. Specific Responsibilities of VM&A. VM&A’s specific responsibilities include:
   4.2.1. Managing AFEMS/REMS functions specific to vehicles.
       4.2.1.1. (Added-PACAF) . Monthly (NLT the 10th of each month), all main operating
       bases, and the 607th ASUS will forward a ship, salvage, receipt report to OL-A
       PACAF/LGR at olahqpacaf.lgr.uc@robins.af.mil.
       4.2.1.2. (Added-PACAF) . 7AF units (607ASUS, 51LRS, and 8LRS) will forward an
       OLVIMS Fleet Management Module transmittal file to OL-A PACAF/LGR during the
       months of January, April, July, and October. Transmittal files must arrive NLT than the
       10th of the month.
       4.2.1.3. (Added-PACAF) . 18LRS, 374LRS, and 35LRS will forward an OLVIMS
       Fleet Management Module transmittal file to OL-A PACAF/LGR during the months of
       February, May, August, and November. Transmittal files must arrive NLT than the 10th
       of the month.
       4.2.1.4. (Added-PACAF) . 15LRS, 3LRS, 354LRS, and 36LRS will forward an
       OLVIMS Fleet Management Module transmittal file to OL-A PACAF/LGR during the
       months of March, June, September, and December. Transmittal files must arrive NLT
       than the 10th of the month.
   4.2.2. Utilizing the Fuels Automated System (FAS) program.
       4.2.2.1. Download the fuel input for OLVIMS from the DESC FAS program, commonly
       referred to as the "Purple Hub". Download frequency will be at the direction of the
       MAJCOM.
   4.2.3. Submitting vehicle buy requirements.
       4.2.3.1. Develop vehicle buy plan across Future Years Defense Plan (FYDP).
   4.2.4. Managing VAL.
   4.2.5. Monitoring workload status and controlling work flow through the work centers.
   4.2.6. Performing required analysis.
   4.2.7. Preparing the computer-generated Vehicle Historical Record, when required.
   4.2.8. Completing the static and variable data entries on data collection forms.
86                                             AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     4.2.9. Maintaining the master vehicle historical record file.
     4.2.10. Obtaining Vehicle Identification Numbers (VINs) from newly assigned vehicles and
     entering them into OLVIMS. Note: Enter the complete number.
     4.2.11. Developing and maintaining an 18-month scheduled maintenance plan.
        4.2.11.1. Accomplish a review of vehicles requiring completion of AF Form 4355 by
        October of each year. If a vehicle has not had AF Form 4355 completed within the last
        12 months VM&A must schedule the vehicle to be brought in as soon as possible.
        4.2.11.2. Consider seasonal needs, labor-hour availability, organizational needs and fair
        apportionment of the 18-month requirement when developing a plan. Scheduled
        maintenance has priority and is not delayed. When necessary, resort to a two-shift
        operation, overtime, or contract to fulfill this need.
        4.2.11.3. Vehicles used as static training aids (not operated on-base or public highways)
        are exempt from scheduled maintenance. Also, vehicles such as mobile communication
        vans positioned in a semi-permanent or permanent site are exempt. Perform scheduled
        maintenance before operating these vehicles over public roads.
        4.2.11.4. Develop, as necessary, work cards and checklists for certain vehicle types or
        special inspection and servicing requirements. Bilingual work cards and checklists may
        be mandatory when local national employees are not required to read and speak English.
     4.2.12. Monitoring all OLVIMS (Fleet and Maintenance Modules) sites and helping resolve
     any problems encountered while processing OLVIMS data.
        4.2.12.1. Capture and input all maintenance historical data in OLVIMS from supported
        Geographically Separated Units (GSU).
     4.2.13. Processing OLVIMS data as prescribed by Air Force Computer System Manual
     (AFCSM) 24-1, On-Line Vehicle Interactive Management System.
        4.2.13.1. (Added-PACAF) . All Main Operating Bases will process Government
        Purchase Card (GPC) transactions into OLVIMS daily.
        4.2.13.2. (Added-PACAF) . VM&A and Materiel Control will verify the accuracy of
        Force Activity Designator (FAD) codes assigned to the vehicle fleet on an annual basis.
     4.2.14. Preparing and submitting deficiency, warranty and unsatisfactory reports using
     procedures provided in TO36-1-191, Chapter 7.
     4.2.15. Developing the VPRL and vehicle MEL.
        4.2.15.1. Execute, initiate and conduct all vehicle recalls. Vehicles will then be
        distributed to the appropriate agencies.
     4.2.16. Reviewing base support and OPLANs with LGRR. Establish vehicle recall and
     redistribution procedures to support these plans as applicable. Incorporate vehicle recall and
     redistribution plans in the transportation annex to the basic plan as applicable.
     4.2.17. Establishing a VCP.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                            87


   4.2.18. Filling vehicle authorizations with the most suitable asset in the inventory. Note:
   Substituted assets will be the oldest vehicles of each type in the fleet. Newer assets should
   only be used to fill authorizations that correlate with the prime stock number.
   4.2.19. Provide COCOM reporting and LIMS EV data as directed.
   4.2.20. Establish and monitor an organizational email account that will be used to receive
   Vehicle Management related correspondence and data calls from C-NAF, MAJCOM,
   VEMSO and Air Staff.
       4.2.20.1. Vehicle Management activities should establish the organizational email
       address    using    the   following     example    as     a    naming     pattern:
       50LRS.VM&A@CHANUTE.AF.MIL.
   4.2.21. (Added-PACAF) . OLVIMS system and data files shall be backed up at least
   weekly. Backed-up media shall be stored in an off site location (facility other than primary
   location).
   4.2.22. (Added-PACAF) . OLVIMS monthly archive (historical) media will be maintained
   for 1 year and will be stored in an off site location (facility other than the primary location).
4.3. VCP. VM&A personnel will develop a training plan and thoroughly train newly appointed
VCOs and VCNCOs on their duties. Additionally, a knowledge test will be administered that
will be rated pass/ fail to ensure VCO/VCNCOs attain an acceptable knowledge level during
training. A sample test can be downloaded from the VCF Program folder within the AF Vehicle
Management                                                                         Neighborhood
(https://wwwd.my.af.mil/afknprod/ASPs/CoP/OpenCoP.asp?Filter=OO-LG-AF-66).
VM&A personnel may modify or add to the questions on the test to meet local requirements. All
new VCOs and VCNCOs will be administered the test and must attain a satisfactory grade of 70
percent or higher to assume their new duties. Associate units will participate in and support the
host VCP. Associate unit VCPs are subject to assessment by the host command Inspector
General (IG). Note: AFOSI) vehicles leased through GSA in Continental United States
(CONUS) are exempt from inspections and staff assistance visits.
4.3. (PACAF) VCP Vehicle Management and Analysis will provide orientation training to all
newly appointed VCO/Vehicle Non-Commissioned Officer (VCNCO) on Air Force vehicle
management policies within 15 days of receiving appointment letters.
   4.3.1. A VCP assistance visit will be conducted annually. The results will be documented to
   include the topics discussed, noted discrepancies, and noteworthy comments, and provided to
   the Unit Commander or equivalent within 14 days after the visit. Copies may be provided to
   tenant command staff assistance teams and IG teams upon request. The VCO and VCNCO
   are provided the following information during each visit:
       4.3.1.1. An analysis of vehicle utilization as it compares to AF goals.
       4.3.1.2. Issues such as operational problems, vehicle rotations, utilization, requirements,
       security, operator training, licensing, lesson plans and misuse will be discussed.
       4.3.1.3. A computation of O&M cost per mile for each unit vehicle.
   4.3.2. Utilization/Rotation Analysis. Rotate vehicles when practical and economical to help
   ensure they will reach their programmed life expectancy. The OLVIMS Fleet Module will be
88                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     used to determine how well the fleet compares to established AF and base mileage averages
     and other Vehicle Management objectives. AF goals listed in the VMIF are used as the basis
     for utilization/rotation analysis. Analysis and summary of actions need to be documented.
     Authorization deletions, changes and rotation need to be considered for under-utilized
     vehicles. Consider utilization data, mission requirements and the cost of moving equipment
     when determining if rotation actions are necessary. Results of this analysis must be
     documented to include rationale for action(s). Note: GSA or other leased assets are exempt
     from this analysis.
        4.3.2.1. (Added-PACAF) . Annual Vehicle Utilization and Rotation Analysis: All
        vehicle types or assets with a utilization goal identified in the Vehicle Management Index
        File will be evaluated during the annual utilization/rotation analysis. The analysis will be
        reviewed and approved by the MSG/CC. The analysis will address the following at a
        minimum:
            4.3.2.1.1. (Added-PACAF) . Monthly utilization averages (use 12 months of
            historical data) by management code. When the fleet average for a specific
            management code is less than 50 percent of the AF goal, consideration should be
            given to reducing vehicle requirements.
            4.3.2.1.2. (Added-PACAF) . Evaluation of severely under-utilized assets (those
            producing less than 25 percent of AF goal) will be prime candidates for elimination.
            When it is determined an asset meeting this criteria will not be eliminated, the
            justification must be documented and approved during the MSG/CC’s annual review
            of the effectiveness of the local vehicle utilization program.
            4.3.2.1.3. (Added-PACAF) . Vehicles in replacement code‖K‖ and above will be
            evaluated annually for rotation. Management code and year group will determine the
            average accumulated mileage. At local discretion, one-of-a-kind vehicles within a
            specific year group may be exempted from the rotation analysis.
            4.3.2.1.4. (Added-PACAF) . Vehicles will be evaluated for rotation when the
            accumulated mileage/hours is/are plus or-minus 20 percent of the fleet average for
            like assets within the same year group. Once the assets meeting the criteria are
            identified, the monthly utilization data will be evaluated to determine if rotation is
            warranted. When it is determined an asset meeting this criteria will not be rotated,
            the justification must be documented and approved during the MSG/CC’s annual
            review of the effectiveness of the local vehicle rotation program.
     4.3.3. Perform Semiannual Wing Assessment Vehicle Inspections. At a minimum, conduct
     inspection of at least 25 percent of each unit’s AF owned or leased vehicle fleet every 6
     months using the vehicle assessment inspection checklist at Attachment 8. If 25 percent of
     unit’s assets are not scheduled for maintenance in a 6-month period, establish a schedule to
     accommodate the remaining vehicles needed to reach the 25 percent mark using the vehicle
     assessment inspection checklist at Attachment 8. An emphasis should be placed on operator
     care and maintenance of leased vehicles since AF vehicle maintenance personnel do not
     maintain these assets. Any vehicle found to be in operation with a documented (noted on AF
     Form 1800 or 1807) safety discrepancy is an automatic failure for that vehicle (score
     recorded as zero). After completing all vehicle inspections for a unit, the individual vehicle
     scores will be averaged to produce an overall assessment score. For example, a unit had
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          89


   three vehicles inspected: vehicle A received 80 points, vehicle B received 70 points and
   vehicle C received 90 points, equaling an overall assessment score of 80 percent (80 + 70 +
   90 = 240 points/3 vehicles = overall assessment score of 80 percent). Inspection results will
   be provided to the Unit Commander or equivalent within 14 days after 25 percent of their
   vehicle fleet has been inspected. A consolidated report will be provided to the MSG
   Commander or equivalent after each semi-annual inspection cycle.
   4.3.4. The VCF will conduct a VCO meeting at least twice a year. Topics will include:
   preventative maintenance, official use guidance, safety, operator care and any other
   information deemed necessary by the VCF.
4.4. DOD Fleet Credit Card System. The DOD Fleet Credit Cards are used to obtain fuel and
services from off-base commercial service stations. Services are limited to those which are
needed in order keep a USAF vehicle in (or return to) serviceable condition when the vehicle is
operating outside of the using organization’s Permissible Operating Distance (POD). Each
registered AF motor vehicle authorized for off-base use may be assigned a DOD Fleet Credit
Card, if the vehicle is normally operated outside of the base’s POD or if an authorized DOD or
AF base refueling facility (that utilizes the Vehicle Identification Link Key) is not available.
DOD Fleet cards are not to be used in place of an organization’s Government Purchase Card
when purchasing items required to support field operations or fleet maintenance support. DESC
is the Program Manager and policy oversight for the DOD Fleet card, however units will
develop, and ensure execution of, local programs and procedures IAW with the DESC sponsored
fuel charge card guidelines and this AFI. To facilitate multi-vehicle fuel purchases, each Vehicle
Management activity is authorized to obtain generic cards. Generic cards should reflect unit
descriptions, i.e., 96th Vehicle Management. Keep in mind that the Vehicle Management
community should maintain as few credits cards as possible to ensure mission accomplishment.
CAMs or unit Agency Program Coordinators (APC) may restrict Fleet card purchases to fuel
only. Car wash purchase amount limits may also be set by CAMs or unit APCs, i.e. $10 per car
wash.
   Notes:
   1. LRS Commanders or equivalents have the option of establishing alternative off-base
      refueling programs, using the Fleet Credit Card, when alternative fuel requirements
      cannot be met by local fuels management agencies and/or supported by other federal
      agencies (refer to paragraph 1.13.4.). When Fleet Credit Cards are authorized for this
      use, APCs will ensure that funds for fuel purchases of non-UDI vehicles are reimbursed
      to the Fleet Credit Card account fund code. Additionally, APC will restrict purchases to
      fuel only.
   2. Air Force Material Command (AFMC) and AFOSI activities with indigenous assets
      assigned are exempt from this policy.
   3. As a rule, vehicle operators should obtain approval from the host base VM&A office
      before using the fleet credit card to obtain off-base maintenance or towing services.
      Vehicle Management function may waive POD requirements if individual purchase or
      service procured with the DOD Fleet Credit Cards are more advantages to the
      government.
90                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     4.4.1. Unit Level Program Management Positions. Normally, the Vehicle Management
     activity is responsible for administration of the DOD Fleet Credit Card Program. Appropriate
     personnel within controlling activity/flight should be appointed to the following positions:
        4.4.1.1. APC.
        4.4.1.2. Accountable Official (AO).
        4.4.1.3. Certifying Official.
        4.4.1.4. In-depth responsibilities for the positions above can be found on the DESC
        website at: http://www.desc.dla.mil/default.asp.
            Note:
            1. The APC position would normally be held by the VFM, VMS or flight OIC,
               however small units/functions with limited supervisory personnel authorizations
               may combine the APC and AO position/responsibilities.
            2. Certifying Officials may be the unit Resource Advisor.
            3. All program management position appointments should be made by the unit
               commander or appointing authority utilizing a DD Form 577,
               Appointment/Termination Record – Authorized Signature. Signed DD Form
               577(s) must be forwarded to the DESC Account Manager and maintained in unit
               program file. AOs also require completion of the Fleet DoD/DESC AO
               Nomination Form, this form is also forwarded to DESC and maintained in a
               program file. Alternates should also be appointed for each position and have the
               same appointment form requirements as stated above. All responsibilities of the
               positions, as outlined in the DESC policy, must be adhered to.
     4.4.2. Establishing DOD Fleet Credit Card Account. Units should contact the AF
     Component Program Manager (AFCPM) and/or visit the DESC website for details.
     4.4.3. Non-Fuel Purchase Funding and Payment Procedures. Specific payment procedures
     must be established at each host base when accounts are established. Make all payments
     directly to the authorized vendor. Provide the Accounting Liaison Office (ALO) an estimate
     of non-fuel purchases to be made against all DOD Fleet Credit Cards each fiscal year or
     quarter as required. This can be accomplished by preparing the appropriate funding
