     document, i.e. AF Form 406, Miscellaneous Obligation/ Reimbursement Document, and
     forwarding the original and one copy to ALO for approval at the beginning of each year
     and/or quarter. The approved copy is authority to cite funds for purchases. A separate DOD
     Fleet Card Program funding file will be maintained for each account for each fiscal year. The
     file will include:
        4.4.3.1. Copies of the current FY funding documents (i.e. AF Form 406 and DD Form
        250).
        4.4.3.2. Fund cite authorization.
        4.4.3.3. Requests for additional or supplemental funds.
        4.4.3.4. Copies of current FY vendor monthly invoices, to include all purchase and other
        transactions receipts. Note: The current Fleet card vendor, Wright Express, only
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          91


     produces monthly invoices for download using the WEX Online Account Management
     System if non-fuel purchases were made during the billing cycle (first calendar day to last
     calendar day each month). The ―balance due‖ amount on the monthly invoice will only
     reflect the amount due to non-fuel purchases.
         4.4.3.4.1. All purchase receipts must have the following associated information
         documented:
             4.4.3.4.1.1. The full name, grade, unit and duty phone number of purchaser.
             4.4.3.4.1.2. Description of purchase. If fuel, type of fuel and gallons. If service,
             part or repair, provide full description.
             4.4.3.4.1.3. Vehicle registration number and odometer/hour meter at the time of
             purchase. NOTE: All vendor invoices and transaction receipts must be
             maintained for three years.
  4.4.4. Administration and Management Controls. The AO will maintain a control file to
  account for the DOD Fleet Credit Cards. The control file will contain, but not be limited to:
  local program policies/procedures, appointment letters and training certificates, a receipt for
  on-hand credit cards to include list of PIN numbers (PINS must be secured at all time),
  copies of documents certifying loss, investigation, destruction, turn-in, semiannual validation
  and credit card register. The register will be valid for one FY. All cards must be reissued on
  a new register by the 1st of October each year. Develop a local credit card control log to
  document use. Store unused cards in a suitable locked container. MAJCOM Account
  Managers (CAM) and unit level AOs must establish on-line account management access with
  the credit card vendor (WEX Online). On-line account management will allow CAMs
  transaction oversight and AOs the ability to retrieve monthly statements, set-up ―alert‖
  emails, quickly view status of account(s), card(s) used and to verify transactions against their
  account(s). Other duties of the APC, AO and Certifying Official include, but are not limited
  to, the following:
     4.4.4.1. Developing a local card user/training guide.
     4.4.4.2. Acquiring the minimum amount of DOD Fleet Credit Cards to meet installation
     requirements.
     4.4.4.3. Controlling the DOD Fleet Credit Card register and the issuance of Fleet Credit
     Cards.
     4.4.4.4. Reviewing user control documents and DOD Fleet Credit Card register twice a
     year to include a physical inventory.
     4.4.4.5. Reporting questionable purchases to Unit Commander (or equivalent), CAM and
     AFCPM.
     4.4.4.6. Posting all non-fuel delivery tickets on AF Form 406.
     4.4.4.7. Ensuring all fuel (to include mileage update) and maintenance transaction costs
     are input into OLVIMS as an off-base cost at least weekly.
     4.4.4.8. When received, verifying and certifying vendor’s invoice against purchase
     receipts.

        4.4.4.9. Forwarding invoice and delivery tickets for non-fuel purchases to the ALO.
        4.4.4.10. (DELETED) .
        4.4.4.11. Ensuring all card users sign a Statement of Understanding prior to initial use,
        and annually thereafter, that outlines card user responsibilities and authorized purchases.
        This may be accomplished by preprinting AF Form 1297 with the following statement:
        ―By signing this form, the above named individual acknowledges their responsibilities for
        Fleet card use and authorized purchases‖.
        4.4.4.12. Notifying DESC, AFCPM, CAM and card contractor immediately of changes
        to your account including telephone numbers, addresses, POCs, AOs, Certifying
        Officials, Department of Defense Activity Address Codes (DODAACs), etc.
        Subsequently, if your unit is disbanded or relocated, the AO responsible for the fuel card
        account is required to provide the card contractor with a forwarding address where any
        unpaid invoices can be sent. Further, if the unit is disbanded, the unit is responsible for
        proper disposition of the cards and personal identification numbers (PIN) to prevent
        unauthorized use or fraudulent activity.
        4.4.4.13. Ensuring the PIN associated with each DOD Fleet card is different and unique
        and that steps are taken to ensure PINs are not divulged to unauthorized personnel. When
        a PIN has been compromised, the cardholder shall contact the contractor immediately for
        card cancellation or resetting of the PIN.
        4.4.4.14. Establish reimbursement policy/procedure for units/individuals that purchase
        unauthorized items or car washes that are over AO directed policy limits.
        4.4.4.15. Ensuring complete documentation (specific item/service purchased and rational
        for purchase) of all non-fuel purchases are maintained on file.
     4.4.5. Disposition of the DOD Fleet Credit Cards. Destroy credit cards no longer required,
     authorized or expired. Maintain a record of DOD Fleet Credit Card destruction for 1 year
     after the expiration date of the card. Channel request to activate or permanently deactivate
     (cancel) account card(s) to the Fleet Credit Card vendor, CAM, AFCPM or DESC. Notify
     Fleet Credit Card vendor of all lost and/or stolen cards.
        4.4.5.1. Lost or stolen account numbers and cards must be reported immediately to the
        Fleet Credit Card vendor. Refer to account control files, account statements, or the back
        of a Fleet Credit Card for vendor contact information. Notification is mandatory whether
        or not the fuel card is to be replaced to enable the contractor to update the data file.
        4.4.5.2. Fuel cards that have been replaced for any reason, including those reported as
        lost and subsequently found, shall be destroyed immediately.
     4.4.6. DOD Fleet Card Training.
        4.4.6.1. Training is mandatory for CAMs and local account APC/AO. New APCs, AOs
        and alternates must complete required training within 30 days of appointment and
        annually thereafter. The mandatory AO training can be found on the DESC website,
        http://www.desc.dla.mil/default.asp. CAMs will maintain current contact in formation
        for all AOs under their MAJCOM hierarchy.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                           93


      4.4.6.2. All card users must receive initial training prior to using the DOD Fleet fuel card
      and annually thereafter. A mandatory card user training presentation can be locally
      developed or downloaded from the DESC website, http://www.desc.dla.mil/default.asp.
      A list of trained card users will be maintained at the point of issue.
4.5. Fuel Issues. The FMF is responsible for the Automated Fuel Service Station (AFSS)
equipped for Vehicle Identification Links (VIL).
   4.5.1. VIL. VM&A will provide the FMF a quarterly, or as required, master list depicting
   all assigned vehicles and organization codes to include a break out of all vehicles that have
   changed since the previous list. This list must include the vehicle registration number, unit,
   all grades of product that will be used (e.g., MUR, MRR, DL1, DL2, CNG, LNG, etc.), and if
   it is an alternative fuel capable vehicle. FMF will use this list to encode the VIL with a UC.
   A system will be developed between the FMF and VM&A to ensure notification of vehicle
   deletions, assignments, rotations, nontaxable and alternative fuel use. VIL keys will only be
   encoded with the appropriate alternative fuel code when the required alternative fuel type is
   available. Local procedures will be developed to ensure alternative fuels are used to the
   maximum extent possible in vehicles equipped to use them (see paragraph 1.13.3). Failure
   to use reasonably available alternative fuels in AFVs may be considered as vehicle abuse.
   Some vehicles, like bi-fuel CNG, require a minimum amount of gasoline to be used
   periodically. In this case, VIL keys for those types of vehicles may be encoded with all fuel
   types required, provided fuel requirement documentation is maintained in the vehicle’s
   Vehicle Historical File.
   4.5.2. Recording Taxable Fuel Consumption. Current Internal Revenue Service (IRS)
   guidance identifies fuel for government vehicles operated solely on government installations
   as exempt from Federal and some state levied taxes. In order to ensure the DOD obtains
   appropriate tax credit for the fuel consumed by these vehicles the following procedures must
   be followed. Note: If any vehicle uses a county, state or federal highway one or more times
   during a fiscal quarter, fuel consumed by that vehicle is taxable for that period. Crossing over
   a county, state or federal highway at an intersection does not count as use. All off-road
   vehicles, e.g., graders, forklifts and K-loaders, qualify. DESC is responsible to issue
   guidance clearly outlining taxable and non-taxable guidelines for DOD fuel use. Additional
   information can be found on the DESC website at http://www.desc.dla.mil/.
      4.5.2.1. VCOs and VCNCOs, in conjunction with VM&A, must verify and list all
      vehicles designated for travel off the installation during the upcoming quarter.
      4.5.2.2. Once finalized, VM&A then forwards the list of vehicles expected to travel off
      the installation to the FMF IAW paragraph 4.5.1 The FMF then verifies each vehicle’s
      VIL is encoded to properly reflect taxable status of fuel to be consumed by the vehicle.
   4.5.3. Fuel Tax Refund Requests. The AF is not authorized to seek reimbursement for DLA-
   owned fuel or fuel purchased under a GSA lease as they are purchased under standard
   pricing. For information on obtaining reimbursement of fuel taxes on non-DLA-owned fuel
   or fuel purchased under a GSA wet lease, contact the local Accounting and Finance office.
4.6. Scheduling Maintenance. VM&A uses good judgment and exercises flexibility in
scheduling work into the shop. Parts availability, work center manning and the needs of the
customer are considered when VM&A plans, schedules and adjusts the shop workload.
94                                            AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     4.6.1. The VM&A work center should be accessible and recognizable to its customers.
     4.6.2. Monitor workload status and control work flow through the work centers.
     4.6.3. Schedule vehicles for needed inspections, services and repairs. An appointment
     system is recommended.
     4.6.4. Ensure work is authorized before it is started and notify the VFM or VMS of any
     estimated repair costs that exceed the one-time repair limit for the vehicle.
     4.6.5. Assign work priority. Notify the VFM or VMS when the total NMC or number of
     mission essential vehicles NMC exceeds acceptable levels. PCN SB004-008 can be used to
     aid in this requirement.
     4.6.6. Inform the work center supervisor of scheduled work, TCTOs, SBs, OTIs,
     Manufacturer Recalls, completed defers and other needs.
     4.6.7. Initiate and route AF Form 1823/1823-1 to the work centers. Process using at least 90
     days of OLVIMS vehicle historical data.
     4.6.8. Update the workload control board with vehicle and personnel status as required by
     the VFM or VMS.
     4.6.9. Consider maintenance in progress, backlog maintenance and work awaiting shop
     when an ETIC is requested. The VM&A Workload Controller and the applicable work center
     supervisors jointly determine the ETIC to be assigned.
     4.6.10. Delay work when needed.
     4.6.11. Check the delayed workload and schedule vehicles for work when the shop
     capability and needs of the customer permit.
     4.6.12. Recommend, in coordination with the work center supervisor, contract repair action
     when repair work or the workload becomes too excessive. Initiate contract documents after
     approval is received from the VFM or VMS.
     4.6.13. Ensure that vehicle and parts warranties are used.
     4.6.14. Monitor cannibalization and vehicles on NMCS.
     4.6.15. When applicable monitor contract repair funds and advise the VFM or VMS and
     Cost Center Manager as appropriate.
     4.6.16. Assist work centers in preparing LTI forms and deficiency reports.
     4.6.17. Ensure repairs for TCTOs, SBs, OTIs and Manufacturer Recalls are scheduled,
     tracked, accomplished and recorded.
     4.6.18. Establish and control Vehicle Management labor hour reporting in OLVIMS as
     prescribed by AFCSM 24-1.
     4.6.19. Process OLVIMS Maintenance data as prescribed by AFCSM 24-1.
4.7. Repetitive Maintenance, Warranty and Authorized Repairs. Before sending an AF
Form 1823/ 1823-1 to the shop, the VM&A Workload Controller:
     4.7.1. Reviews the AF Form 1823/1823-1, Vehicle Historical Record and the OLVIMS
     repetitive maintenance screen for repetitive maintenance.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          95


   4.7.2. Estimates repair costs (for major repairs and repairs that may cause the one-time repair
   limit to be exceeded) and ensure repairs are authorized according to TO 36-1-191.
   4.7.3. Decides whether the repair is covered by a new vehicle warranty or a previous
   contract, COPARS or other parts warranty.
4.8. Vehicles in Replacement Codes A Through J. VM&A identifies vehicles that will be
tentatively replaced by new vehicle gains by registration number. Perform only minimum
essential repairs on these vehicles to keep them in service until replacements are received.
Process requests for disposition instructions IAW TO 36-1-191. Process requests for repair
authority and disposition instructions for vehicles assigned to tenant organizations using the
OLVIMS Automated LTI function to the owning MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff.
4.9. Work Order and Vehicle Processing for Outlying Work Centers. The operator
debriefing and incoming inspection is done in the work center. Repair needs are validated. The
de-briefer gives the information to initiate the AF Form 1823/1823-1 to the VM&A Workload
Controller and makes sure any scheduled maintenance and delayed requirements are known. The
work center supervisor (or a designated technician) accomplishes final inspections, which will be
shown on the AF Form 1823/1823-1.
4.10. Work Order Control for Delayed Maintenance.
   4.10.1. Delayed maintenance is work that may be put off without damage to the vehicle or
   equipment and without compromising safety standards. Delayed maintenance codes are in
   AFCSM 24-1, Attachment 4, and on the OLVIMS help screen.
   4.10.2. When delayed work is entered on a closed AF Form 1823/1823-1, OLVIMS
   generates a delayed maintenance AF Form 1823/1823-1 for the delayed items and maintains
   delayed work by work center.
   4.10.3. A copy of the new (delayed) AF Form 1823/1823-1 and parts requisition document is
   sent to Materiel Control when parts are required. Another copy of the AF Form 1823/1823-1
   is retained by VM&A in a delayed maintenance file.
   4.10.4. VM&A uses the delayed maintenance report to verify shop backlog, maintain NMCS
   status, make sure parts are installed after receipt, and catalog identified malfunctions and
   discrepancies until repaired. Routine delayed maintenance is accomplished during the next
   scheduled/unscheduled work occurrence, workload and mission permitting. Delayed
   maintenance can be accomplished as workload allows or be done by mobile maintenance.
4.11. Work Order Number Control. OLVIMS controls and assigns work order numbers to
AF Form 1823/1823-1. VM&A can assign blocks of work order numbers to outlying work
centers. The PCN SB004-018 is used to monitor work order number assignment.
4.12. AF Form 1823/1823-1Processing for Vehicles NMCS. These procedures apply when
needed parts are not readily available through Materiel Control and the vehicle cannot be
returned to the user.
   4.12.1. The work center supervisor ensures that all necessary parts are annotated on the parts
   requisitioning form or worksheet accompanying the AF Form 1823/1823-1.
   4.12.2. Materiel Control selects the supply source and processes the parts request. If the
   parts are not available from normal sources (including bench/working stock, work order
96                                           AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


     residue and delayed parts in stock), Materiel Control, together with the work center
     supervisor and VM&A, checks whether parts are available from a vehicle approved to be
     sent to DRMS. If all other attempts to locate parts are unsuccessful and the NMCS vehicle
     would seriously affect the user’s mission, Materiel Control and the work center supervisor
     may consider cannibalization.
     4.12.3. When parts are not immediately available, the AF Form 1823/1823-1 is taken to the
     VFM, VMS or designee, who reviews each possible NMCS condition to make sure all
     attempts have been made to return the vehicle to service and approves placing the vehicle in
     NMCS status.
     4.12.4. Once a NMCS condition is approved, the AF Form 1823/1823-1 is taken to the
     VM&A Workload Controller who places the vehicle on NMCS. The work order is then sent
     to Materiel Control and the work center supervisor is advised to prepare the vehicle for
     NMCS storage.
     4.12.5. Materiel Control obtains parts according to Chapter 5.
     4.12.6. As soon as the parts are received, Materiel Control sends the work order to VM&A.
     VM&A will take the vehicle off NMCS status and schedule it for work.

Section 4B— Procedures

4.13. Procedures for Processing Contract Maintenance Work Orders.
     4.13.1. VM&A keeps active and inactive files on contract maintenance work order
     correspondence, coordinates with the VFM or VMS and the work center supervisor, plans the
     workload, monitors the funding status and keeps files on work specifications.
     4.13.2. VM&A initiates the AF Form 1823/1823-1 and funding documents, i.e. AF Form 9
     and GPC, for all work done commercially. They include work specifications and other data
     as needed. The completed documents are sent to the VFM, VMS or designee for review and
     signature. Note: Vehicle down time for contract work orders, including awaiting contract
     action, is NMCM time.
     4.13.3. After the funding documents are signed, one copy is retained.
     4.13.4. VM&A arranges to send the vehicle to the vendor.
     4.13.5. VM&A monitors the downtime of vehicles being repairs and informs the VFM or
     VMS if corrective action is needed.
     4.13.6. When work is completed, the work is inspected for compliance with agreement,
     estimate and/ or industry standard requirements. The VFM, VMS or designee checks the AF
     Form 9 (if used) and the vendor’s invoice for accuracy against the AF Form 1823/1823-1.
     Warranty provisions are programmatically entered during ―JZ‖ transaction processing.
     Additional warranty information may be entered in the remarks area of the closed AF Form
     1823/1823-1.
     4.13.7. A ―JZ‖ transaction is accomplished in OLVIMS to input the repair cost. If an actual
     vendor's invoice is not received with the vehicle, use the price on the contract document.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         97


       4.13.7.1. Upon receipt of the vendor's invoice, compare the cost to the agreed price and
       change OLVIMS if necessary. (Not applicable if using the GPC).
   4.13.8. The ALO develops and certifies SF 1034, Public Voucher for Purchases and
   Services Other Than Personal, (original and three copies) to pay the vendor. The ALO
   reports discounts for prompt payment or other changes to the original invoice cost to VM&A
   for adjustment to the original input to OLVIMS (not applicable if using the GPC).
   4.13.9. The original invoice is attached to the original voucher for submission by the ALO.
   A copy of the invoice is attached to the ALO’s copy of the voucher and another copy
   returned to the vendor with the payment. (Not applicable if using the GPC).
4.14. Procedures for Distribution and Processing COPARS Sales Slips. The Vehicle
Management activity establishes filing and retention procedures for COPARS sales slips as it
pertains to the tracking of expenditures, warranties and vehicle historical repair documentation.
   4.14.1. Distribute sales slips as follows:
       4.14.1.1. Copy one is retained by the contractor, attached to the invoice, and sent to
       Contracting, and Accounting and Finance, in turn.
       4.14.1.2. Copy two is sent to the QAP for verification, and then forwarded to VM&A, in
       batch sequence, for processing into the OLVIMS and filing.
       4.14.1.3. Copy three is attached to the filed copy of the AF Form 1823/1823-1.
       4.14.1.4. Other copies are distributed according to documentation needs.
   4.14.2. Sales Slip Processing. Materiel Control checks for the following data elements on
   sales slips each duty day for obvious errors:
       4.14.2.1. Date.
       4.14.2.2. Work order number.
       4.14.2.3. Nomenclature.
       4.14.2.4. Quantity.
       4.14.2.5. Charge code ("M," "N" or "D").
       4.14.2.6. Category of part (new or rebuilt).
       4.14.2.7. No changes have been made on the slip.
       4.14.2.8. Vehicle registration number.
       4.14.2.9. Part number.
       4.14.2.10. RC/CC Code.
       4.14.2.11. Unit price, discount and total price by line item.
       4.14.2.12. Warranty (if applicable).
       4.14.2.13. Sales slip is "Z'd" out after the last entry.
       4.14.2.14. Bin number when charge code "D" is used.
98                                             AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


        4.14.2.15. Total of sales slips on adding machine tape or other printed media, and
        attached to sales slip.
     4.14.3. Each person authorized to sign for parts is responsible for seeing that the data
     elements listed above are present on each sales slip before signing for the parts. Upon
     completion of the sales slip, the recipient signs the sales slip using the same signature as the
     sample signature on the COPARS authorization list. Materiel Control ensures that discounts
     have been figured accurately and provides them to VM&A along with the adding machine
     tape or other printed media, of the total of all sales slips on a daily basis. Sales slips for the
     day are numbered consecutively, to include copies of voided slips.
     4.14.4. Process COPARS transactions through OLVIMS each duty day.
        4.14.4.1. VM&A processes the sales slip cost data by line item (except L9999) into
        OLVIMS.
        4.14.4.2. VM&A verifies the sales slip line items with PCN SB004-005 and makes
        corrections as necessary. These sales slips are then returned to Materiel Control for filing.
        4.14.4.3. Input all discounts or charges such as premium communications and
        transportation, and COPARS overtime, to OLVIMS, as identified by Materiel Control.
        4.14.4.4. VM&A adjusts cost data in OLVIMS, as identified by the ALO for such things
        as prompt payment discounts or other financial adjustments.
     4.14.5. When a part costing more than $100 comes with a warranty VM&A records the
     provisions in OLVIMS on the "PZ" transaction, which can then be monitored using the PCN
     49. Specific warranties are noted on the COPARS sales slip. VFM or VMS determines if
     warranty tracking is accomplished for parts costing less than $100.
4.15. Procedures for Processing AF Form 15, United States Air Force Invoice, and DOD
Fleet Credit Card.
     4.15.1. Process AF Form 15 cost into OLVIMS for all vehicle-related services. If the ALO
     notifies VM&A of changes to the AF Form 15, such as discounts for prompt payment,
     VM&A will process the change into OLVIMS.
     4.15.2. Process the Fleet Credit Card cost after VFM or VMS certification. After VM&A
     enters and validates the data in OLVIMS (reference AFCSM 24-1), the Fleet Credit Card
     receipts are processed IAW paragraph 4.4
4.16. Control of TCTOs, SBs and OTIs. TCTOs are managed differently than regular TOs.
They must be requisitioned individually and as a series they must be identified for automatic
distribution. TCTOs, SBs and OTIs are managed according to these procedures:
     4.16.1. VEMSO is notified by WR-ALC concerning newly released TCTOs, SBs and OTIs.
     VEMSO will provide MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs a list of vehicles requiring the
     TCTO, SB or OTI for forwarding this information to units in their command for action. Upon
     receiving new TCTO release notification, these units ensure the TO Monitor places the unit
     on distribution for the specific TCTO.
        4.16.1.1. Units must ensure they are on distribution for each TCTO series. These series
        are listed in the ―-36‖ index for the type of vehicle they pertain to. The TO monitor
        should review the ―-36‖ index on receipt and ensure that for each type of vehicle
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                       99


       assigned, if there is an applicable TCTO series that it is on distribution. This ensures
       TCTOs published under that series are sent to the unit. The system is not foolproof;
       however, as new TCTOs are sometimes issued for which a series has not been
       established. That is why a manual notification is usually made.
   4.16.2. VM&A should date stamp each TCTO, SB or OTI once received (electronically
   dated e-mail/ message traffic is sufficient); determine TCTO, SB or OTI action and/or parts
   kit requirement by reviewing the TCTO, SB or OTI cover page for affected vehicle
   registration numbers; and notify Materiel Control to order required parts kits after
   determining and verifying base requirements. Note: Use the ―T‖ prefix for work order
   numbers when a TCTO will be completed on that work order. Use the ―S‖ prefix for work
   order numbers when a SB will be completed on that work order.
       4.16.2.1. WR-ALC requires verification of correct TCTO or SB ordering before kits are
       released for shipment. Contact the appropriate IM or Equipment Specialist for the
       affected vehicle type by telephone, fax or electronic mail, provide vehicle registration
       numbers and requisition due-in document numbers, obtained from Materiel Control, to
       enable kit release.
   4.16.3. Take continuous supply follow-up action until kits are received.
   4.16.4. Schedule TCTOs, SBs and OTIs as soon as possible. See the "when work will be
   done" part of the specific TCTO, SB or OTI. A TCTO, SB or OTI that is not completed by
   this date is an "outstanding" TCTO, SB or OTI and places the affected vehicles’
   serviceability in jeopardy. When directed by the WR-ALC, VEMSO and/or MAJCOM, these
   vehicles are removed from service until the outstanding TCTO, SB or OTI is accomplished.
   The VFM or VMS advises VEMSO and the MAJCOM within 24 hours after a TCTO, SB or
   OTI becomes outstanding.
   4.16.5. Record the completion of the TCTO, SB or OTI on the computer-generated Vehicle
   Historical Record (OLVIMS PCN SB004-828). VEMSO will collect completion/compliance
   reporting via LIMS EV monthly data files for completed TCTOs and SBs. Urgent action
   TCTO and SB completion reporting will be included with all others, however they may
   require manual completion reporting depending on time constraints and fleet safety concerns.
   VEMSO will notify applicable units as the need arises.
       4.16.5.1. When closing TCTO/SB work orders, VM&A activities must ensure the
       TCTO/SB number entered into OLVIMS exactly matches the TCTO/SB Number shown
       in LIMS EV TCTO view for that registration number.
   4.16.6. Maintain active master TCTO, SB and OTI files. A rescinded file may be maintained
   when needed for special programs and projects. When a rescinded TCTO is needed, it can be
   obtained by following the procedures in TO 00-5-1.

Section 4C— Policy

4.17. Vehicle Abuse Repairs. Local procedures are established for reporting suspected vehicle
abuse. Usually, damage not attributable to fair wear and tear (acts of nature) or accidents is
characterized as abuse. Note: Wind damage to the door is not an act of nature.
100                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


4.18. Accident Repairs. When the shop receives a vehicle with accident damage, CSC
personnel will initiate an AF Form 1823/1823-1 estimating the cost of repair. When computing
estimated cost for repairing accident damage, indirect cost is included only to determine one-
time repair limitations.
   4.18.1. Document accident repairs separately from normal work.
   4.18.2. Prepare an AF Form 20, Repair Cost and Reparable Value Statement, when required
   by local policy or requested by the Surveying Officer. Note: Both military and civilian
   Direct Labor charges computed by OLVIMS are used for determining labor cost for in-house
   repairs of vehicles/equipment on the AF Form 20.
4.19. Excess Vehicles. Redistribute excess vehicles to base activities having open vehicle
authorizations or reassign them to replace less serviceable and/or maintainable (usually older)
vehicles eligible for replacement. Do not assign excess vehicles to organizations waiting
approval for additional vehicle requirements. VM&A will control excess vehicles pending
MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff action.
   4.19.1. If reassignment to another base activity is not possible, change the vehicle status
   code to ―I‖ and place in an excess detail using ASC ―048‖ and applicable base code and user
   org code (e.g., 048CNEG). Accomplish an AFTO Form 91 and send the LTI requesting
   disposition instructions to the MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff within 60 calendar days
   from the date the vehicle becomes excess on the Custodian Authorization/Custody Receipt
   Listing (CA/CRL).
   4.19.2. Initiate follow-up action after 60 calendar days from the date the LTI was sent to the
   MAJCOM.
   4.19.3. Asset becomes excess once it is rotated from a valid authorization into an excess
   detail.
   4.19.4. Excess assets may not be used for deployments or special projects.
4.20. AF LSV and OGMVC. Slow moving conveyances (e.g., neighborhood EVs, golf cars,
scooters and other small low-speed utility vehicles, etc.) will be managed in several different
categories with a prime NSN for each category. This guidance does not include non-appropriated
funded LSVs and OGMVCs.
   4.20.1. Vehicles, whose maximum speed is not greater than 25 MPH will be categorized as a
   LSV and assigned the appropriate prime NSN based on the categories listed in Table 1.4
   This item will be loaded in AFEMS AS 010 and managed as a registered vehicle. This
   category must meet Title 49 CFR 571.500 Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standard (FMVSS).
       4.20.1.1. For those LSVs purchased with unit funds prior to June 2006, organizations
       may continue to manage these assets as equipment until the vehicle has reached its life
       expectancy. This category of LSVs will be assigned prime NSN 2340-00-540-3900, AS
       036 and will be considered as non-REMS reportable LSVs.
   4.20.2. Self-propelled assets providing a basic passenger and/or light cargo carrying
   transportation capability (i.e., golf carts, ATVs, quad-runners, snowmobiles, etc.) not
   meeting specifications of Title 49 CFR 571.500 FMVSS will be categorized as OGMVCs
   and assigned prime NSN 2340-00-585-7495 in AFEMS, AS 036. Note: Skid steer loaders
   and mini-excavators made by Bobcat or other manufacturers are classified as registered
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                    101


  vehicles and will be managed            as   vehicles   under   the   category   of   Base
  Maintenance/Construction Equipment.
  4.20.3. OGMVCs will be procured and managed as equipment items. Non-REMS
  reportable LSVs will no longer be procured, but existing assets will be managed as
  equipment items.
     4.20.3.1. As equipment (refer to AFMAN 23-110, chapter 22 for policy on equipment),
     OGMVCs and non-REMS reportable LSVs will be loaded in AFEMS (NF3) and
     managed on the CA/CRL (R14). MAJCOMs may track OGMVCs and non-REMS
     reportable LSVs on the VAL. The serial number (or other unique identification number),
     part number and cage code must be recorded in the AFEMS in-use serialized asset
     screen.
     4.20.3.2. OGMVCs and non-REMS reportable LSVs will be maintained IAW
     manufacturer recommended intervals or standards in TO 36-1-191 for a comparative
     asset, and at a minimum will have a complete serviceability inspection, to include all
     safety related systems, at least annually. Owning organizations will fund and manage all
     aspects of the maintenance program. Vehicle Management will provide technical
     assistance as requested.
        4.20.3.2.1. (Added-PACAF) . The decision to maintain non-registered Low Speed
        Vehicle (LSV) and Other Government Vehicle Conveyances (OGMVC) through
        contract, Blanket Purchase Agreement (BPA), GPC, or through unit self-help will be
        made locally. If utilizing self-help, Vehicle Management facilities will not be used.
        Only LSV and OGMVCs owned by LRS units may be maintained in LRS Vehicle
        Management facilities as mission needs dictate. Owning units desiring to perform
        their own maintenance via self-help will use their own shop or make arrangements
        with the Base Automotive Skills Development Center. To ensure maintenance is
        adequate and the assets are safely maintained, owning organizations are required to
        have an annual (safety) inspection performed by a civilian automotive maintenance
        firm (via contract, BPA, etc.). This inspection will not be completed through self-
        help. Safety discrepancies identified during the inspection will be repaired prior to
        use.
        4.20.3.2.2. (Added-PACAF) .     For all non-registered LSV and OGMVC
        maintenance performed through contract, BPA, GPC, or through unit self-help, the
        owning unit must supply VM&A with proof of annual safety inspection.
        4.20.3.2.3. (Added-PACAF) . Operation checks will be performed on the same
        basis as those for General Purpose Vehicles using an AF Form 1800, Operator’s
        Inspection Guide and Trouble Report.
  4.20.4. OGMVCs will be purchased IAW the Federal Acquisition Regulation (FAR),
  Defense FAR Supplement, AF FAR Supplement, related AFIs and AFPD 64-1, The
  Contracting System, and managed IAW AFMAN 23-110 and AFI 91-207, Air Force Traffic
  Safety Program. Purchase requests for OGMVCs will be processed through the Base Ground
  Safety Office (coordination), Contracting (coordination),Vehicle Management Flight
  (coordination) and LRS Equipment Accountability Office (approval).
102                                       AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


      4.20.4.1. Wing/Installation Ground Safety will review each purchase IAW AFPAM 91-
      210, Contract Safety, paragraph 7.1.4.
      4.20.4.2. The Vehicle Management Flight will review and forward purchase requests to
      their MAJCOM for clarification to ensure the desired asset is an equipment item and not
      a vehicle. Vehicle Management will load and track any scheduled inspections on
      OGMVCs and non-REMS reportable LSVs in the OLVIMS for the purpose of notifying
      owning organizations pending maintenance actions due and ensuring inspections are
      accomplished (tracking purposes only). OGMVCs and non-REMS reportable LSVs will
      be assigned X-registration numbers. Request X-registration numbers from VEMSO.
      MAJCOMs may authorize bases to utilize a separate site code for tracking OGMVC and
      non-REMS reportable LSV inspections only. Owning organization will provide to
      VM&A, the original warranty documents and specifications prior to the assets being
      loaded into OLVIMS.
         4.20.4.2.1. (Added-PACAF) . All non-REMS reportable LSV and OGMVC assets
         will be issued an X registration number. Use management code 8299 for all LSV
         assets and use the National Stock Number (NSN) as prescribed in the basic
         publication. Use management code 8499 for all OGMVC assets and use the NSN as
         prescribed in the basic publication. For LRS owned assets being maintained in LRS
         Vehicle Management facilities a maximum of 0.3 equivalents will be applied to LSVs
         and OGMVCs.
         4.20.4.2.2. (Added-PACAF) . PACAF authorizes use of separate OLVIMS site
         code to track non-registered LSV and OGMVC inspections.
      4.20.4.3. (Added-PACAF) . Owning organizations of non-registered LSVs and
      OGMVCs must maintain documentation showing coordination with Wing Ground Safety
      Office, Vehicle Management Flight, and approval from the Equipment Management
      Section with the Management Systems Flight for each asset owned which was procured
      after 1 December 2004.
         4.20.4.3.1. (Added-PACAF) . All requests for approval of an authorization or
         procurement of a LSV or OGMVC which requires Command Equipment
         Management Office (CEMO) approval must be accompanied by documentation of
         coordination with Wing Ground Safety Office and the Vehicle Management Flight, a
         listing of the requesting unit’s currently authorized and assigned LSVs and
         OGMVCs, and a listing showing the requesting unit’s light duty general purpose
         vehicle authorizations as described in paragraph 4.20.5.1.
   4.20.5. Installation Commanders or equivalents should set a ceiling on the number of
   OGMVCs while reducing the current fleet when OGMVCs are purchased based on
   guidelines provided by their respective MAJCOM.
      4.20.5.1. (Added-PACAF) . The ceiling on the number of non-registered LSV and
      OGMVC authorizations will be set at 10 percent of the light duty general purpose vehicle
      authorizations, 1.5 ton and below, excluding ambulances, trailers, and Special Purpose
      (Management Code C) telephone maintenance trucks, identified on the unit’s Vehicle
      Authorization List (VAL). For units with no vehicle authorizations, the number of non-
      registered LSV and OGMVC authorizations is capped at a maximum of 1ea. Unit Type
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                       103


      Code (UTC) tasked OGMVC requirements/authorizations are exempt from the 10 percent
      ceiling restriction.
   4.20.6. LSVs and OGMVCs programs will be an UCI checklist item(s) to ensure all
   management and maintenance requirements are being met. During VVVs, OGMVCs and
   non-REMS reportable LSVs will be considered as an element of a unit’s total motor vehicle
   capability when assessing vehicle fleet size adequacy.
      4.20.6.1. Specialized OGMVCs such as Bobcats, quad-runners and ATVs will not be a
      consideration for reducing existing general purpose or passenger carrying vehicles
      authorizations.
   4.20.7. Salvage Procedures. Owning units will process OGMVCs and non-REMS reportable
   LSVs in the same manner, as local procedures dictate for disposal of other organizationally
   owned government equipment. License plates provided by Vehicle Management will be
   turned in as accountable items and assets will be removed from the OLVIMS database.
   4.20.8. (Added-PACAF) . LSVs and OGMVCs will only be operated on military
   installations or government property/roads unless waivered by Wing Safety.
   4.20.9. (Added-PACAF) . All non-registered LSVs and OGMVCs will be procured,
   accounted for, and maintained according to guidance provided in AFI 23-302 and this
   instruction. However, prior to 1 December 2004, numerous assets were procured as
   equipment items which exceeded established maximum speed criteria for LSVs. The
   following guidance applies to those LSVs acquired prior to 1 December 2004 which exceed
   established LSV criteria:
      4.20.9.1. (Added-PACAF) . Non-registered LSV and OGMVC assets exceeding
      established speed criteria and procured prior to 1 December 2004 may remain in use until
      they are no longer economically repairable. These assets will continue to be accounted
      for as non-registered LSV and OGMVC on unit equipment accounts under ASC 036.
      4.20.9.2. (Added-PACAF) . All non-registered LSVs in this category must have a
      placard placed in the asset, visible to the operator, which states ―LSV – Do not exceed 25
      mph/42 kph‖.
4.21. Withdrawing Vehicles from DRMS. The following procedures apply for withdrawing
vehicles from DRMS:
   4.21.1. Vehicles may be considered for withdrawal from DRMS only when an open
   authorization exists or when the vehicle in DRMS is in better condition than the vehicle
   assigned. MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff must approve vehicles withdrawn from
   DRMS to be placed in the AF inventory. Vehicle Management must certify a vehicle as
   economically repairable and warrants withdrawal action.
   4.21.2. Vehicles previously identified as REMS reportable can be withdrawn for use in AF
   training courses as a Vehicle Management training aid for non over-the-road use with
   approval from MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff. Submit request through the LRS
   Equipment Liaison Office (ELO).

Section 4D— Vehicle Authorization
104                                          AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


4.22. Vehicle Requirements. Federal law controls the purchase of vehicles for government use.
Congress authorizes the purchase of government vehicles through the Appropriations Act and
sets statutory price limitations for purchasing of certain vehicles. Quantities listed in
authorization documents for vehicles determine budgetary requirements and must not include
additional assets for in-maintenance replacements, pipeline or vehicles in depot maintenance.
Meet peak workload and unusual requirements for vehicles by borrowing from other government
agencies, renting or leasing vehicles from GSA or commercial sources. POVs may be used on a
reimbursable basis according to the JTR.
   4.22.1. Limousines. Restrict the use of Class V sedans (see Figure 4.1) to these DOD
   officials and visiting foreign officials of comparable rank (Title 41 CFR, Chapter 101,
   Subpart 101-38.1 and 101-39.2):
       4.22.1.1. The Secretary of Defense.
       4.22.1.2. The Deputy Secretary of Defense.
       4.22.1.3. The Chairman, JCS.
   4.22.2. Large Sedans. Restrict the use of Class IV sedans to these DOD officials and to
   visiting foreign officials of comparable rank:
       4.22.2.1. The Secretaries of the AF, Army and Navy.
       4.22.2.2. The Chiefs of Staff of the AF, Army, Chief of Naval Operations and the
       Commandant of the Marine Corps.
       4.22.2.3. The Under Secretaries of Defense.
       4.22.2.4. All four-star officers.
       4.22.2.5. Directors of Defense Agencies.
       4.22.2.6. (DELETED) .
   4.22.3. Class III midsize sedans or SUV equivalent. Public Law stipulates that Class I or
   Class II vehicles be used to meet daily mission requirements. When Class I or Class II
   vehicles clearly do not meet mission requirements, Exception authority to authorize the use
   of Class III AFV or Hybrid vehicles must be fully justified and coordinated through the Base
   & MAJCOM/CC or equivalent. Once coordination is approved all requests for exception to
   policy will be submitted to HQ USAF/A4LE for AF/A4/7 consideration. MAJCOM, wing
   and unit commanders will heavily scrutinize any exceptions to policy that are not in line with
   the SECAF, CSAF and OSD policy.
   4.22.4. Class I or II. Passenger sedans, station wagons, mini-vans and SUVs acquired for
   support, other than those specified in paragraphs 4.22.1., 4.22.2. and 4.22.3 will be Class I
   or II.
       4.22.4.1. Wing commanders, equivalents or higher are no longer authorized an upgrade
       to a Class III AFV or non-AFV, sedan or SUV equivalent (refer to Table 1.3) since they
       are not required as a mission essential upgrade. With regulatory mandates to purchase,
       and the increased availability of AFVs, Class II AFVs must be used to the fullest extent
       possible. See paragraph 1.27 for further guidance.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                      105


      4.22.4.2. Law Enforcement Sedans. The size of sedans authorized for use for law
      enforcement shall be the minimum size available with the equipment modifications
      necessary to meet mission requirements. Since the size of police-equipped vehicles
      varies by model year, fleet management activities may authorize sedans larger than Class
      II when the HQ USAF A4/7 has authorized procurement prior to acquisition if that class
      of vehicle is not factory equipped to perform the law enforcement mission.
   4.22.5. AF vehicle management activities are required to acquire (procure, rent and lease)
   and use the most fuel efficient vehicle to meet mission requirements in order to support the
   National Strategy for Energy Security, DOD 4500.36-R and this AFI. Refer to paragraph
   1.13 and 4.22.3 for AFV acquisition requirements.

Figure 4.1. GSA Sedan and Station Wagon Classifications.




4.23. Vehicle Authorization Review Authority. IAW Title 40 United States Code (USC)
Section 491, only the minimum number of vehicles necessary to support the mission should be
authorized. The wing MSG Commander or equivalent is the vehicle authorization review
authority for the installation. The MSG Commander or equivalent:
   4.23.1. Reviews and validates vehicle requirements and vehicle change requests.
   4.23.2. Recommends increases or decreases in vehicle authorizations.
   4.23.3. Reviews and approves the annual base vehicle buy submission.
   4.23.4. Approves the VPRL and vehicle MEL annually.
   4.23.5. Reviews the vehicle distribution and sourcing plan to support the Emergency War
   Order (EWO) and/or other contingency tasking during the BSP process.
   4.23.6. Evaluates effectiveness of the local rotation program using data in the annual
   utilization and rotation report.
   4.23.7. Considers the following to address additional vehicle authorizations:
      4.23.7.1. Use of vehicles from the U-Drive It (UDI) fleet to satisfy short duration or
      sporadic mission requirements.
106                                          AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


       4.23.7.2. Types and quantities of vehicles must be clearly the minimum number to
       accomplish the mission.
       4.23.7.3. Do not authorize vehicles for reasons of grade, prestige, personal convenience
       or to individual persons except as previously stated.
       4.23.7.4. Review vehicles that do not meet AF or base utilization goals for possible
       authorization, deletion or rotation actions.
       4.23.7.5. Services staff engaged in direct administrative support may use general purpose
       vehicles acquired with appropriated funds. Do not acquire vehicles with appropriated
       funds justified either partially or wholly for transportation support of Morale, Welfare
       and Recreation (MWR) activities. See AFI 65-106, Appropriated Fund Support for
       Morale and Recreation and Non-appropriated Fund Instrumentalities, for additional
       guidance.
4.24. AS. AS 010 identifies core AF owned vehicle allowances. Core allowances are those
allowances common to all AF commands. AS 012 identifies core AF leased vehicle allowances.
If a Basis of Issue (BOI) does not exist, a request to establish a BOI must be sent to the
MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff. If approved by the MAJCOM, the request will be sent to
WR-ALC for final approval and inclusion in the applicable AS. ASs prescribe the required
authorizations for vehicles to accomplish functional and organizational missions. ASs constitute
authorization and approval authority for vehicles.
   4.24.1. ASs are identified in AFMAN 23-110v2. The ASs most commonly used in VM&A
   are:
       4.24.1.1. 048 – Excess: Unauthorized equipment on hand.
           4.24.1.1.1. (DELETED) .
       4.24.1.2. (DELETED) .
       4.24.1.3. (DELETED) .
       4.24.1.4. 051 - Contractor support (not AF replaced): Use when AF vehicles are
       Government Furnished Property (GFP) to a contractor and will not be replaced by the
       government (USAF). VM&A will not rotate vehicles to/from a contractor
       authorized/assigned under ASC 051. Authorizations under this allowance will be
       reduced/deleted upon final disposition of the vehicle.
       4.24.1.5. 054 - Special project: Use to report authorizations supporting a MAJCOM or
       USAF approved special project/program. 054 authorizations should not exceed 1 year.
       If the authorization is needed beyond the termination date, MAJCOMs will establish
       permanent authorizations using another AS or the authorization will be deleted.
       4.24.1.6. 076 - Base closure: Reports authorizations at installations projected for closing.
       4.24.1.7. 987 - A temporary authorization not to exceed 179 days: Use for short-term
       vehicle requirements or projects. A numeric Julian date will be used at the end of the AS
       (e.g., 9878014) to identify when the authorization expires. Consecutive 987
       authorizations for the same requirement or project are not authorized.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                            107


       4.24.1.8. 034 - Contingency:      Reports authorizations at contingency locations (non-
       normalized) worldwide.
       4.24.1.9. 037 - Contractor support (AF replaced): Use when AF vehicles are GFP to a
       contractor and will be replaced by the government (USAF).
       4.24.1.10. 024 DEPOT specific support assets: Reports authorizations at DEPOT
       locations.
       4.24.1.11. 049 Research and Development Equipment (Vehicles) support assets.
4.25. Vehicle Justification Requests. Use MAJCOM approved format to justify adjustments to
vehicle requirements. Use the same form to justify vehicles if they are the same type, they
perform similar functions or they fall under the same ASC in the ASs. The AS is the allowance
document for validating vehicle authorizations and is not an authorization document. Initiate
follow-up disposition action after 60 calendar days.
   4.25.1. Authorization Analysis. VM&A will conduct an authorization analysis on all vehicle
   authorization requests. The objective of the analysis is to validate the requirement and
   determine whether a more effective avenue, such as short-term leasing or co-utilization of
   assets, can satisfy the requirement without adding additional authorizations. The VFM or
   VMS will use the conclusions of the analysis to make approval/disapproval
   recommendations through the LRS Commander or equivalent prior to submission to the
   MSG Commander or equivalent.
   4.25.2. Justification Requirements. Each of the following questions must be addressed and
   answered in the affirmative before the request can be sent to the applicable MAJCOM for
   disposition:
       4.25.2.1. Does the justification indicate the current VAL using activity or the proposed
       user?
       4.25.2.2. Does the justification cite the directive, project or publication that generated the
       request, if appropriate?
       4.25.2.3. Does the justification fully explain the proposed use of the vehicle?
       4.25.2.4. Does the justification identify expected utilization information (miles, hours,
       passengers, equipment, supplies, materials, number of trips, etc.)?
       4.25.2.5. Does the justification list the number of vehicles currently authorized and
       assigned to the requesting unit and justify why co-utilization will not meet mission
       requirements?
       4.25.2.6. Does the request justify why transportation support from Vehicle Operations
       (taxi or UDI) cannot satisfy the vehicle requirement (OLVIMS data must substantiate
       lack of support)?
       4.25.2.7. Does the justification include a mission impact statement on the organization,
       base or wing if the request is denied?
       4.25.2.8. Does the justification cite any actions taken to realign other authorizations to
       accommodate the requirement?           Note: The MSG Commander or equivalent
       signs/approves the justification package.
108                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


4.26. Control Numbers. Assign a control number to the vehicle justification package using
OLVIMS Fleet Module. For example; a 9-digit code like ―V91250001‖ where:
   4.26.1. ―V‖ denotes vehicle request.
   4.26.2. ―9125‖ denotes the Julian date the request was submitted to higher headquarters for
   action.
   4.26.3. ―0001‖ denotes the next available control number from the log for that Julian date.
4.27. Processing of Returned Vehicle Justification Requests. Requests returned will be
processed as follows:
   4.27.1. Update the OLVIMS Fleet Module control log approved or disapproved.
   4.27.2. Update the SBSS and VAL if approved.
   4.27.3. Notify the unit of approval or disapproval action.
   4.27.4. Maintain approved and disapproved justifications for 3 years. VFM or VMS may
   determine a longer retention period.
   4.27.5. Retain requests for special authorizations (048, 054, 987, etc.) for as long as the
   requirement exists.
4.28. Vehicle Allocations and Due-In Listing. Each MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff is
provided vehicle procurement allocation and delivery information from WR-ALC. The
MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff provides shipping information, to include add-ons such as
special paint, air conditioning, towing package, pintle hooks, heavy duty alternator, etc., to the
IM, and notifies each base VM&A of allocations they can expect to receive with delivery dates if
available. Changes affecting allocation or status information are provided to each installation
when they become available. Vehicle allocation listings (due-ins) should be updated as required.
This data is also used to validate annual vehicle buy requirements and as a source for vehicle
repair decisions. Note: MAJCOM MAFIS and base AFIS systems must be updated with current
vehicle due-in information.
4.29. Repair Authority and Disposition. Guidelines for determining repair allowances and
approval levels are in TO 36-1-191. Repair approval or disposition request is documented on an
AFTO Form 91 and routed through the VFM or VMS to the LRS Commander, equivalent
commander of equivalent or designee who has authority to exceed one-time repair limits.
   4.29.1. (Added-PACAF) . Vehicle disposition authority rests with the LRS/CC at Main
   Operations Base (MOB), and 607 ASUS/LGT for the COBs in Korea. The only exceptions
   to this policy are for those vehicles listed as AF critical in Vehicle Management Index File.
   Disposition requests for AF critical vehicles will be forwarded to OL-A PACAF/LGR at
   olahqpacaf.lgr.uc@robins.af.mil for action.

Section 4E— Vehicle Rental and Leases

4.30. Vehicle Rental and Lease Administration.
   4.30.1. DOD components may rent or lease motor vehicles when any of these conditions
   exist:
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                      109


     4.30.1.1. An Economic Analysis (EA) verifies a cost benefit to the government.
     Reference AFI 65-501, Economic Analysis, for EA requirements and procedures.
     4.30.1.2. Unforeseen requirements demand vehicles prior to acquisition through normal
     procurement.
     4.30.1.3. Local laws or Status of Forces Agreements (SOFAs) prevent using government
     vehicles.
     4.30.1.4. Normal REMS procedures or resources cannot fill the authorization.
  4.30.2. The leasing or rental of passenger sedans, station wagons, mini-vans and SUVs shall
  be limited to those designated as Class I and II by GSA. Class III and Class IV will not be
  rented or leased unless filling a valid Class III or Class IV requirement. Refer to paragraph
  4.22.3
  4.30.3. The requester may accept the next larger size vehicle (if rented/leased less than 60
  days) without obtaining SECAF approval if the rental agency does not have the authorized
  size vehicle. This does not apply to Class III and IV sedans.
  4.30.4. The LRS Commander or equivalent will coordinate on all lease requests prior to
  submission to contracting.
     4.30.4.1. VM&A validates all requests for rentals and leases for installation activities.
     Coordinate with contracting to ensure vehicles are not rented/leased without prior
     validation regardless of who funds for the rental/lease. Lease or rental may be executed
     with an AF Form 9 or, where guidance allows, GPC. A copy of the validated AF Form 9
     or related GPC documents will be retained in VM&A.
     4.30.4.2. VM&A will maintain a log of all leases/rentals. The log should list each
     purchase request in numerical sequence and the reason for its initiation. Note: CE
     occasional leases accomplished IAW paragraph 4.30.4.5 are not exempt from this
     requirement.
     4.30.4.3. Requesting units/users provide funds for each lease. Note: All requests for
     leases exceeding 60 days are justified using the MAJCOM-approved vehicle justification
     request format and forwarded to the MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff for action
     before entering into a lease agreement through contracting. Approved requests must
     remain on file until the lease is terminated.
     4.30.4.4. Upon termination of a vehicle rental or lease, VM&A verifies and certifies
     charges.
     4.30.4.5. CE Special Purpose Equipment Leasing. Special consideration should be given
     to base-level CE activities concerning lease on demand of base maintenance and
     construction vehicles and vehicular equipment. The intention of offering this special
     consideration is to reduce AF infrastructure costs.
         4.30.4.5.1. VM&A personnel should jointly review the vehicles authorized for the
         CES with the unit VCO, VCNCO or other personnel as deemed appropriate focusing
         on vehicles with low utilization or open vehicle authorizations.
110                                        AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


          4.30.4.5.2. Open authorizations, vehicles with low utilization, or vehicle types with
          multiple assets assigned, should be considered for coding of the vehicle authorization
          for lease, with the assets assigned in those authorizations processed for disposition.
          4.30.4.5.3. In-turn, CES should enter into a lease on demand agreement with local
          vendors through use of BPAs or other firm fixed price contractual arrangements to
          provide required vehicle support on demand, without first processing the request
          through the base-level LRS. This arrangement accommodates charging the cost of the
          lease of construction and base maintenance vehicles and vehicular equipment to the
          specific project for which the vehicles are required, and expedites the lease process
          for the CE community.
          4.30.4.5.4. The special consideration described above is applicable to construction
          and base maintenance vehicles and vehicular equipment only. Under no
          circumstances will passenger-carrying vehicles be leased under the occasional use
          lease program.
      4.30.4.6. Fuel servicing vehicle lease requests will be coordinated with the MAJCOM
      Fuels Management Staff, AFPET and WR-ALC to ensure commercially available
      vehicles meet the compatibility, safety and servicing requirements of AF systems.
      Contact AFPET for baseline requirements for leasing aircraft fuel servicing vehicles.
   4.30.5. (Added-PACAF) . Leased vehicles will be loaded in OLVIMS in the following
   manner:
      4.30.5.1. (Added-PACAF) . Vehicles will be loaded under management code 8299.
      4.30.5.2. (Added-PACAF) . The word "Lease" will be entered in the NSN block.
      4.30.5.3. (Added-PACAF) . For Government Services Administration (GSA) vehicles
      use the GSA license plate number. For all other leases, request registration number
      through VEMSO.
4.31. Vehicle Lease Procedures.
   4.31.1. Short-Term Lease. LRS Commanders or equivalents may rent or lease vehicles to
   meet peak workloads and unusual or emergency requirements for periods not to exceed 1
   year (provided organizational O&M money is available) without established authorizations.
   For any rental or lease of vehicles exceeding 60 days, request written approval from the host
   MAJCOM identifying the vehicle type, quantity and duration of the lease. Use GSA vehicles
   if they are available. Confirm non-availability from the MAJCOM before executing a
   commercial lease exceeding 60 days for general purpose vehicles. Keep non-availability
   certification documents for 1 year. Do not use this authority to provide transportation for
   normal or routine purposes, when vehicles are available. Rentals or leases that exceed 1 year
   must have a valid authorization. Leases that exceed 18 months have to be coordinated with
   contracting and should be justified IAW DFARS Part 207.401. Concurrent leases are not
   authorized.
   4.31.2. Long-Term Lease. Leasing over 1-year is generally to fill open authorizations not
   filled through normal acquisition procedures.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                        111


       4.31.2.1. Requests must be sent to the MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff for
       approval. The MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff approves all lease requests and
       coordinates on all "lease with option to buy" clauses.
       4.31.2.2. VM&A reviews and validates all vehicle lease requests. VM&A will process
       requests to the MSG commander or equivalent for approval or disapproval
       recommendations. Forward the justification requests to the MAJCOM Vehicle
       Management Staff for processing.
           4.31.2.2.1. (Added-PACAF) . All vehicle order requests for GSA leased vehicles
           authorized on the PACAF VAL, regardless of the organization funding the vehicle
           lease or the Build Office Address Code (BOAC) the leased GSA vehicles fall under,
           will be coordinated with Vehicle Management prior to submission to GSA.
   4.31.3. Use short-term leases under 60 days to satisfy emergency requirements pending
   receipt of long-term lease approval.
4.32. Funding for Long-Term Leased Vehicles. Vehicle leases are funded by unit O&M
funds. When executing a long-term lease, contracts with option to buy require prior approval by
WR-ALC (see paragraph 4.33).
4.33. Lease with Option to Buy. Lease with option to buy is the preferred method of entering
into long-term vehicle leases per the FAR, Sections 7.401 and 7.402 and DFARS 207.401. WR-
ALC must approve all leases with an option to buy clause. In a lease with option to buy contract,
the cumulative lease costs and the cost to exercise the purchase option must not exceed the
purchase cost unless fully justified in writing.
   4.33.1. Once the lease asset is purchased, the authorization must be changed to budget code
   ―V‖ and a vehicle registration number must be requested through the MAJCOM Vehicle
   Management Staff.
4.34. Insurance Coverage and Maintenance for Rented or Leased Vehicles.
   4.34.1. ―For Hire‖ solicitations and resulting contracts provide insurance coverage as
   prescribed by applicable portions of the FARs. Unless the rental company requires
   purchasing insurance, rented or leased vehicles are obtained with the AF providing self-
   insurance.
   4.34.2. Vehicle operators conduct daily operator care on rented or leased vehicles unless
   otherwise specified in the contract.
   4.34.3. GSA approved local vendor performs all maintenance on rented or leased vehicles,
   unless a prior agreement is made showing it is more economical for the AF to perform
   maintenance, or a matter of military necessity. All waivers must be submitted and approved
   by AF/A4LE prior to any maintenance action taken on the vehicle fleet. AF/A4LE will only
   approve waivers based on the lack of a commercial maintenance facility within the local area
   or within the normal travel distance from the base.
   4.34.4. (Added-PACAF) . Only Andersen and Eielson have obtained a waiver to maintain
   GSA vehicles. No other VM activity will provide maintenance to GSA leased vehicles.
4.35. Installation of Radio Equipment in Rented or Leased Vehicles. When two-way radio
sets are required, hire vehicles having radio equipment already installed. Install radio sets in
112                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


government-owned, rented or leased vehicles when it is not economical to rent or lease
equipment. Use portable or non-fixed radios when feasible.
4.36. Exceptions for Acquiring, Renting or Leasing Foreign Made Buses. Federal law
requires the armed forces to use US manufactured buses to satisfy requirements, unless their use
is not economical or not in the best interest of the US. The rule applies when you purchase,
lease, rent or make contractual arrangements for transportation services. These are exceptions to
the Federal Law:
   4.36.1. When US manufactured buses are not available to meet requirements that cannot be
   postponed; foreign manufactured buses may be used temporarily. However, this time must
   not exceed the lead time required for acquiring and delivering US manufactured buses.
   MAJCOMs can submit a waiver request to AF/A4LE if it is not economically feasible to
   lease US manufactured buses.
   4.36.2. To meet a special but nonrecurring requirement or where a recurring requirement is
   sporadic and infrequent. The time of use must not exceed the time needed to meet the
   nonrecurring or recurring infrequent requirement.
   4.36.3. Where foreign manufactured buses are available at no direct or indirect acquisition
   cost to the US Government.

Section 4F—Identifying, Marking and Registering Motor Vehicles

4.37. Prescribed Identification. Except for vehicles hired for 60 days or less, vehicles acquired
for official purposes are identified by specific markings (Title 40 USC 491). Specific marking
instructions are in TO 36-1-191. Identification consists of three parts:
   4.37.1. Title of DOD component.
   4.37.2. The registration number.
   4.37.3. The legend, "Official Use Only". NOTE:         This legend must not be covered or
   blacked out with organizational markings.
4.38. Markings. Removing Markings. Remove all prescribed or authorized vehicle markings
when the vehicle is permanently disposed.
   4.38.1. Special Marking Procedures. Only a minimum number of special markings may be
   affixed to vehicles. For economical reasons, they must be removable to speed the rotation of
   vehicles. All markings must comply with TO 36-1-191.
   4.38.2. Installation and Activity Markings. TO 36-1-191 prescribes using AF installation,
   activity or organizational markings.
4.39. Exemptions from Identification Markings. Vehicles which are exempt from DOD
identification markings (paragraph 4.44) shall be registered and inspected IAW the laws of the
State, Commonwealth, territory or possession in which they are primarily used (Title 41 CFR
101-38.201-2).
   4.39.1. Unlimited Exemptions. Motor vehicles regularly used for intelligence, investigative
   or security purposes are exempt from identification and marking provisions. These include
   vehicles:
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                      113


      4.39.1.1. Used by the AFOSI.
      4.39.1.2. Required to be exempted under a SOFA.
4.40. Registration Numbers.
   4.40.1. Registration numbers are assigned to motor vehicles and designated non-motorized
   vehicular equipment. Vehicular equipment in Federal Supply Group (FSG) 17, 23, 24, 38,
   and 39; Federal Supply Class (FSC) 4210, and Material Management Aggregation Codes
   (MMAC) CT and YW have registration numbers. Registration numbers are also required for
   all AF activities (including the ANG and the AFR) that record vehicles on any type of
   property account.
   4.40.2. These vehicles do not require REMS reportable registration numbers:
      4.40.2.1. Any vehicular-type equipment in FSGs, FSCs or MMACs not listed in
      paragraph 4.40.1
      4.40.2.2. Non-self-propelled MHE. Examples include two- or four-wheeled hand trucks,
      warehouse trailers or hoists.
      4.40.2.3. Aerospace ground or hanger equipment. Examples include bomb lift trailers,
      trailer-mounted air conditioners and oxygen or nitrogen-servicing carts.
      4.40.2.4. Vehicle attachments. Examples include bulldozer and snowplow blades or
      refuse containers.
      4.40.2.5. Non-motorized bicycles.
      4.40.2.6. Non-self-propelled agricultural implements.
      4.40.2.7. Mobile homes or house trailers.
      4.40.2.8. Vehicles earmarked for the Military Assistance Program (MAP).
   4.40.3. The vehicle IM at WR-ALC assigns all REMS vehicle registration numbers.
   Registration numbers will be applied by Vehicle Management as specified in TO 36-1-191.
   4.40.4. The owning base (VM&A) requests X-registration numbers from VEMSO for
   equipment listed in paragraphs 4.40.2.1 through 4.40.2.8 or considered by the IM as not
   requiring REMS control. X-registration numbers are not reportable in REMS.
      4.40.4.1. Vehicles changed by modification to a different basic type must have old
      registration numbers canceled by the losing IM and new registration numbers assigned by
      the gaining IM.
      4.40.4.2. The responsible IM obtains registration numbers for vehicular support
      equipment from WR-ALC.These numbers must have an alpha "W" in the third position.
      They are not reportable in REMS.
   4.40.5. The VCO or VCNCO submits a request for a registration number to VM&A. The
   VFM or VMS forwards approved recommendations through the MAJCOM Vehicle
   Management Staff to the appropriate IM at WR-ALC for any vehicle that does not have a
   registration number but meets the above criteria. If doubt exists, VFM or VMS will request a
   registration number. The IM either assigns the number or advises VFM or VMS to request an
   X-registration number from the VEMSO.
114                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


       4.40.5.1. Registration number requests will include NSN, description, model year or year
       of manufacture, and chassis serial or VIN of the vehicle. AF Form 86, Request for
       Cataloging Data/ Action, lists this information if the vehicle does not have a valid NSN.
       4.40.5.2. Government license plates are applied to vehicles as soon as practical after the
       receipt of registration numbers.
   4.40.6. WR-ALC:
       4.40.6.1. Assigns registration numbers or advises activities to request an X-registration
       number from VEMSO.
       4.40.6.2. Makes sure a current listing of reportable vehicle NSNs is maintained.
       4.40.6.3. Makes sure that other AF publications citing definitions or registration
       techniques conform to this AFI.
   4.40.7. Vehicle Management destroys license plates or obliterates registration numbers
   according to TO 36-1-191 when vehicles are removed from the AF inventory and transferred
   to:
       4.40.7.1. The DRMS.
       4.40.7.2. Another agency for other than repair and return.
       4.40.7.3. A MAP.
       4.40.7.4. Conversion to a training aid.
4.41. General and Flag Officer Identification. Plates indicating the occupancy of a vehicle by
a general or flag officer are affixed to the front of the vehicle. In addition, AF Commanders or
equivalents at the installation group level or above, and other persons as designated by
MAJCOM Commanders may display distinguishing metal plates on their motor vehicles.
4.42. Registering, Inspecting and Licensing Motor Vehicles.
   4.42.1. Motor vehicles that are regularly based or housed in the states, territories,
   possessions or foreign countries and are exempt from identification provisions under
   paragraph 4.40 must be registered and licensed according to local laws.
   4.42.2. All other vehicles will display official markings using US Government tags IAW TO
   36-1-191.
   4.42.3. Federal Motor Vehicle Registration System (FMVRS): All non-tactical Highway
   Vehicles that travel or may travel on public highways are required to be registered in
   FMVRS and plated with the new design plate, PN AF05. Units have three years from
   January 2009 to transition over to the new design plate and must be ordered pre-stamped
   with the registration number from http://www.amerimac.net/. Notes: 1. Only those vehicles
   that display or will display plate number AF05 are required to be registered on the FMVRS
   website https://fmvrs.fas.gsa.gov/. 2. AFCENT locations are exempt from FMVRS.
4.43. Complying with International Agreements. When required by the North Atlantic Treaty
Organization (NATO) or other international agreements, AF vehicles must contain the markings
prescribed in standards that have been ratified by the US commands having jurisdiction over the
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                        115


military activities in these countries. Unless HQ USAF/A4LE instructs otherwise, logistics
readiness officers must make sure military activities comply with these international agreements.

Section 4G—Special Authorizations

4.44. Vehicle Support Resulting From Terrorist Threats. Because of terrorist activities, the
AF has a program to provide heavy and light armored vehicles, domicile-to-duty transportation,
and vehicle painting and marking exceptions for threatened key personnel and senior officers.
HQ USAF Criminal Investigation & Counterintelligence (SAF/IGX) consolidates and validates
all requests for these special vehicles or marking waivers in response to terrorist threats.
   4.44.1. Submission Procedures:
       4.44.1.1. The requesting MAJCOM, DRU or Field Operating Agency (FOA) Vehicle
       Management Staffs submits all requests for special vehicle requirements to SAF/IGX.
       4.44.1.2. SAF/IGX validates special vehicle requirements based on terrorist threats.
       Once validated, SAF/IGX provides a recommendation to HQ USAF/A4L and A4P.
4.45. Armored Vehicle Requirements.
   4.45.1. New Vehicle Procurement. HQ USAF/A4PR ensures the recommendation is
   consistent with public law, EOs and DODDs and approves the recommendation.
   Procurement, both quantity and unit cost, must be authorized by Congress. If approved, the
   MAJCOM allocates necessary BP8200 funds.
   4.45.2. Light Armored Vehicles. MAJCOMs, FOAs or DRUs may request SAF/IGX
   approval for procuring and installing approved protection on existing vehicles. Submit
   requests when any of these conditions exist:
       4.45.2.1. The level of protection required makes the installation of armor on an existing
       vehicle more advantageous or economical.
       4.45.2.2. Agreements provide separate funding for vehicles and armor.
       4.45.2.3. Application of armor on an existing vehicle is the only method for obtaining
       armored vehicles.

Section 4H—Vehicle Buy

4.46. Vehicle Requirements Process. WR-ALC programs vehicle acquisitions for the AF
through the vehicle buy program. WR-ALC is the central procurement agency for all AF vehicle
purchases. AF agencies outside of WR-ALC will not purchase vehicles without prior
coordination and approval through WR-ALC. Note: WR-ALC is required to go through GSA
initially unless they are unable to support buy requirements.
   4.46.1. WR-ALC annually:
       4.46.1.1. Provides MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs with specific vehicle buy
       submission instructions/guidelines.
       4.46.1.2. Compares MAJCOM vehicle buy submissions against requirements stated in
       AFEMS (DSDC001).
116                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


       4.46.1.3. Jointly resolves any inventory discrepancies with MAJCOM Vehicle
       Management Staffs.
       4.46.1.4. Compiles the AF vehicle budgetary requirement.
       4.46.1.5. Is the review authority for specifications, purchase options, purchase
       descriptions and standards for procuring AF vehicles.
       4.46.1.6. Determines MAJCOM allocations and coordinates shipment of assets acquired.
   4.46.2. MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs annually:
       4.46.2.1. Provide vehicle buy submission guidelines to base-level LRS activities.
       4.46.2.2. Compile and prioritize MAJCOM requirements.
       4.46.2.3. Submit MAJCOM vehicle requirements through CARS.
       4.46.2.4. Work with WR-ALC to resolve any inventory data discrepancies.
       4.46.2.5. Provide WR-ALC with shipping information and special specification
       requirements.
       4.46.2.6. Monitor due-ins.
       4.46.2.7. Prepare Mission Need Statement (MNS), as required. Document all vehicle
       requirements and modifications in a MNS when research and development efforts are
       required during program development or the program has joint service or allied nation
       applicability. Follow procedures in AFI 10-601, Capabilities Based Requirements
       Development, for processing a MNS.
4.47. Specification Review. WR-ALC forwards the vehicle specifications for all other vehicles
by 15 October to the lead command for use during the following FY’s buy process. The lead
command is usually the dominant user of a specific vehicle type. WR-ALC does not review
specifications for: Vehicles bought through GSA, M-series vehicles or vehicles on an optional or
multi-year contract for the follow-on FY.
   4.47.1. The Lead Command:
       4.47.1.1. Coordinates the specifications with appropriate agencies within that command.
       4.47.1.2. Forwards one copy of the specifications to each using MAJCOM Vehicle
       Management Staff.
       4.47.1.3. Consolidates all responses and works out all disparities and forwards a single
       coordinated response with recommended changes by 15 February to WR-ALC.
   4.47.2. Using Commands:
       4.47.2.1. Coordinate the specifications with the appropriate command agencies.
