which charges are refundable or reimbursable (see AFCSM 24-1, Attachment 4). At the
beginning of each FY, and when a change is required, VM&A furnishes a list of tenant
organizations supported to Accounting and Finance (through the Budget Office) for certification.
Accounting and Finance identifies which organizations are reimbursable (Code 3) or refundable
(Code 4) (refer to AFI 65-601, Volume 1, Chapter 7, Support Guidance, and Volume 2,
Attachment 10, WIMS, OLVIMS, and Other Management Reports). Accounting and Finance
returns this certified list to VM&A to be used to enter the correct codes into OLVIMS.
   7.51.1. All reimbursable and refundable cost data must be reconciled monthly with
   Accounting and Finance. This data must be verified for accuracy, to include validating that
   all reimbursable and refundable units are loaded properly in OLVIMS.
   7.51.2. Vehicle and equipment work orders for vehicles assigned to reimbursable and
   refundable units will be retained for at least 1 year after the close-out date for reference for
   inquiries and audits.
   7.51.3. RC/CC codes will be validated at least annually.
7.52. System Codes. Vehicle system codes define the specific repair on a vehicle. They are
used for historical purposes and failure data capture toward improvements in reliability,
maintainability and deploy ability. Find these codes in the OLVIMS ―Help File‖.
7.53. System and Subsystem Descriptions. Subsystem codes are used to more closely define
the actual work performed during the repair, inspection and service cycle. These subsystem
206                                        AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


codes are required entries in block 20 of the Vehicle Historical Record (OLVIMS PCN SB004-
828). When conscientiously applied, they help detect and control repeat maintenance. Sub codes
not assigned a specific description may be developed locally, when required. Find the codes and
their descriptions in the OLVIMS ―Help File‖.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                     207


                                         Chapter 8

                                          VEMSO

8.1. Authority and Responsibilities
   8.1.1. Program Authority. The Headquarters United States Air Force, Deputy Chief of Staff,
   Logistics, Installations and Mission Support, Directorate of Logistics (HQ USAF/A4L) is the
   VEMSO Executive Agent.
   8.1.2. Program Responsibility. The Materials Support Division (HQ USAF/A4LE), acts on
   behalf of the Executive Agent. HQ USAF/A4LE establishes and enforces element policy,
   goals, objectives and proposes projects of interest to the AF Vehicle Management
   community.
      8.1.2.1. HQ USAF/A4LE designates the VEMSO authority to perform in the capacity as
      an adjunct to the staff. They are responsible for all data collection and draft report
      generation required above the MAJCOM level. While they are responsible for the data
      collection and draft report generation, each MAJCOM finalizes their own written
      narrative to those reports as required.
8.2. VEMSO Duties on Behalf of HQ USAF/A4LE
   8.2.1. Manage and draft for approval all changes or revisions to transportation policy
   directives, instructions and TO 36-1-191. The VEMSO will collect all inputs, consolidate
   and create a draft for MAJCOM review and coordination. Upon reconciling all MAJCOM
   inputs (or identifying unresolved conflicts), the VEMSO will present the draft to HQ
   USAF/A4LE for final review, approval and coordination to publish. Additionally, the
   VEMSO staff will review all MAJCOM supplements to the above listed publications and
   forward to HQ USAF/A4LE for final approval. The VEMSO will coordinate suggested
   changes to supplements with the submitting MAJCOM before forwarding to A4LE.
   8.2.2. Collect and generate all annual reports and data updates as required by HQ
   USAF/A4LE. Some examples of these annual reports are: (1) Federal Automotive
   Statistical Tool (FAST), (2) Presidential Budget (PB) 41, (3) OMB Circular Exhibits 33 and
   55, (4) AFI 65-503, Cost and Planning Factors update, (5) AF Financial Plan Input (lease
   cost data) and (6) Annual Energy Report to name a few. Note: Each session of Congress,
   the names, content and quantity of these reports are subject to change.
   8.2.3. Analyze vehicle authorization policy to ensure up-to-date compliance with federal
   vehicle fleet policies, alternative fuel solutions and Congressional mandates.
   8.2.4. Manage, analyze, improve and implement vehicle automated management systems.
   8.2.5. The AF Vehicle Management community focal point for Vehicle Management safety.
   Maintain and update the Vehicle Management Safety Handbook.
   8.2.6. Manage the AF Vehicle Management Neighborhood and assist MAJCOMs with
   establishing MAJCOM Communities of Practice within the neighborhood.
   8.2.7. The AF Component Manager for the DoD Fleet Fuel Credit Card Program.
   8.2.8. The AF representative to INTERFUEL and FedFleet.
208                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


   8.2.9. Manage the AF Vehicle License Plate program. Refer to TO 36-1-191 for more details
   on this program.
   8.2.10. The AF vehicle community focal point for all matters related to AS management.
   Maintain the AS and coordinate all recommended changes with each MAJCOM.
   8.2.11. The preferred AF POC with the GSA Regional and National Fleet Managers. This
   does not preclude each base or MAJCOM from interacting with GSA at appropriate levels,
   only offers a common POC for GSA. The VEMSO will reach out to appropriate contacts
   within the vehicle community to resolve issues or concerns with the GSA leased vehicle
   program.
   8.2.12. Perform VVVs on all vehicle fleets.
      8.2.12.1. Remaining within current ceiling authorization-levels should be a consideration
      during the decision-making process. If a genuine mission change has not occurred (i.e.,
      additional aircraft assigned, new weapon systems deployed, new units assigned to a base,
      etc.) then the total number of authorized vehicles at a base cannot increase.
      8.2.12.2. Some additional factors to consider during the process are the mission,
      base/unit population, physical layout of the installation and geographical region/climate
      as well as the needs of the customer.
   8.2.13. TCTOs, SBs and OTIs management. The VEMSO will manage and monitor all
   TCTOs, SBs, and OTIs and other related vehicle compliance inspections that are loaded into
   CARS, and make updates into the WR-ALC CARS database. The VEMSO will provide a
   summary to AF/A4LE and MAJCOMs upon request.
      8.2.13.1. Follow-up on units not in compliance with established completion dates.
      8.2.13.2. Collect compliance data and forward to WR-ALC points of contact as required.
   8.2.14. Provide regular summaries to AF Vehicle Management units of maintenance tips and
   techniques to enhance efficiency and safe maintenance operations. Summarize this
   information in user-friendly publications (may be electronically transmitted) that effectively
   transmit information to the technician level.
   8.2.15. The VEMSO will correspond and interact directly with unit/base level OPRs to
   consolidate reoccurring monthly and quarterly legacy system data call requirements.
      8.2.15.1. The VEMSO will provide consolidated data/reports to MAJCOMs and K-
      Loader SPO as required.
   8.2.16. The VEMSO is the approving authority for all Air Force Forms 601 that require Air
   Staff approval for new missions and requirements.
   8.2.17. AF/A4LE has designated the VEMSO as approval/disapproval authority of all
   command levy requests for vehicle shipments between commands. Losing and gaining
   MAJCOMs will provide coordination on requests prior to submitting to the VEMSO.
   Gaining MAJCOMS must have valid authorizations for all assets requested for approval. All
   requests    will be    sent   to    the   VEMSO’s         common       e-mail    address:
   afelm.vemso@langley.af.mil. The VEMSO will return approval/disapproval to the
   respective MAJCOMs with a courtesy copy to AF/A4LE. Additionally, AF directed cross
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                       209


   command redistribution orders will be generated by the VEMSO as required to support
   routine, priority and contingency missions.
      8.2.17.1. Transfer of AFRC or ANG assets between any commands requires AFRC or
      ANG A4R approval respectively. The A4R approval letter must state if recoupment or
      non-recoupment of funds/asset(s) are required in accordance with Title 10 law before
      command levy action can occur.
8.3. VEMSO Support to MAJCOMs
   8.3.1. (DELETED) .
   8.3.2. (DELETED) .
      8.3.2.1. (DELETED) .
      8.3.2.2. (DELETED) .
   8.3.3. Research and assist in management of TO and repair information systems for AF
   Vehicle Management use. Evaluate available systems to ensure repair information system
   standardization in the AF Vehicle Management community and efficient maintenance
   operations.
   8.3.4. Research and validate depot overhaul work specifications when requested.
   8.3.5. Participate in vehicle and equipment FAT as requested by MAJCOMs, Air Staff and
   WR-ALC.
      8.3.5.1. Send proposed vehicle evaluations to MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs,
      WR-ALC (Vehicle Management Branch) and HQ AFCESA/CEO for coordination and
      comments.
   8.3.6. (DELETED) .
   8.3.7. IDEA Evaluation Support. The VEMSO is available to all MAJCOM and base-level
   suggestion evaluators. The VEMSO will coordinate and research vehicle modification
   suggestions with the appropriate WR-ALC Program Manager or IM. The VEMSO is not a
   part of the official evaluation and approval matrix, but is available to advise, research and
   coordinate on all suggestions regarding vehicles and Vehicle Management processes.
   8.3.8. Vendor Product Evaluations. The VEMSO will conduct vendor product evaluations as
   requested by at least two interested MAJCOMS. This is necessary to ensure time and
   resources expended during product evaluations produce tangible benefits to the AF vehicle
   community, with the primary focus on enhancement of deployed operations. See
   Attachment 8 for additional information regarding the vendor product evaluation process.
8.4. AEF Support. The VEMSO will be the vehicle community focal point to create, collect
and monitor all issues related to AEF support. This includes development and maintenance of
TMSK, deployment lessons learned database, and research and evaluation of tools and
equipment to support Vehicle Management operations in an expeditionary, deployed
environment.
   8.4.1. Tools and equipment will be specifically chosen for transportability (light weight and
   small size); ease of use in the field (power requirements, etc.); and overall necessity and
   practicality for the type of maintenance performed.
210                                       AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


      8.4.1.1. VEMSO approved tools and equipment for deployment will be formalized into
      appropriate UTC for AEF and contingency tasking.
   8.4.2. Develop vehicle parts support kits such as TMSKs and MRSPs to support Vehicle
   Management operations (especially vehicle maintenance) in an expeditionary, deployed
   environment.
      8.4.2.1. TMSKs and MRSPs will be standardized for AF use by vehicle make, model and
      type. The VEMSO will distribute/post these kit listings for AF use on their website.
   8.4.3. Research and develop management and maintenance techniques, procedures and
   guidance necessary to guide Vehicle Management operations in an expeditionary, deployed
   environment.
      8.4.3.1. Policy guidance for maintenance in a deployed environment, to include tips and
      lessons learned, will be developed and distributed to enhance knowledge level of
      personnel subject to deploy.
   8.4.4. Develop standards of vehicle condition for deploying vehicles to ensure maximum
   reliability in field conditions with minimal investment. Monitor condition of vehicles
   deployed through collection and dissemination of ―lessons-learned‖ and other means to
   institutionalize readiness and maximize return on investment.
   8.4.5. Perform "reach-back" tech data support for deployed vehicle maintainers with
   emergency tech data requirements.
8.5. VEMSO Product Support Cell (PSC), previously known as Centralized Registered
Equipment Management System (C-REMS). PSC performs a monthly scheduled command
reconciliation between selected base-level Automated Fleet Information System (AFIS),
Standard Base Supply System (SBSS), MAJCOM Automated Fleet Information System
(MAFIS) and the Air Force Equipment Management System (AFEMS) ensuring 100%
authorization integrity and asset accountability.
   8.5.1. As technologies evolve, customer needs and other external conditions change, PSC
   will be continually refined and improved to ensure our ability to:
      8.5.1.1. Collect, integrate, assimilate, and effectively manage vehicle Custodian
      Authorization Custody Receipt Listing (CA/CRL) for all base-level host and tenant units.
      8.5.1.2. Develop new or improved processes for all vehicle authorization/asset
      transactions in SBSS.
      8.5.1.3. Monitor and maintain individual MAJCOM and base Vehicle Authorization
      Lists (VAL) for reconciliations, changes, updates, additions, and deletions.
      8.5.1.4. Advance organizational performance across the entire PSC work portfolio to
      include: 100% accountability for all products, physical and informational infrastructure
      and workforce management practices.
   8.5.2. Over time, these core functions will drive PSC’s ability to facilitate resource
   management decisions and provide 100% data integrity of all Air Force vehicles. This
   transformation effort supports the Air Force Command and Control Enabling Concept
   (Change 2) and supplements the responsibilities and organizational construct of Component
   MAJCOMs and Component NAFs that are addressed in HQ USAF Program Action Directive
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                      211


   (PAD) 06-09, Air Force Component Organization. It formalizes, supplements, and
   implements appropriate provisions of HAF PAD 07-13, Implementation of the CSAF
   Direction to Transform and Consolidate Headquarters Management Functions, Annex D,
   Logistics, Installations and Mission Support and applicable Appendices; and implements
   results of the AF/A4R AFSO21 centralized vehicle accountability Rapid Improvement Event,
   23 March 2007.
   8.5.3. Background. Traditionally, our vehicle management processes have been marginally
   successful in sustaining accountability by using multiple legacy operating systems. This has
   been validated by various audits conducted at unit and AF levels. Establishing PSC at the
   enterprise level will achieve data synchronization by centralizing execution of accountable
   vehicle transactions and monthly reconciliation of legacy systems databanks.
   8.5.4. The flow charts in Figure 8.1 and Figure 8.2 depict the current flow of vehicle
   accountability data and the future state. When the process of REMS was transferred to
   vehicle management in the late 1980s, each main operating base earned one full-time
   equivalent to support this function. Over time, requirements have been reduced by
   modernization of legacy systems and the manning has been integrated with other duties;
   however units have retained the same manning level.

Figure 8.1. Current Accountability Process.
  212                                        AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


  Figure 8.2. Future State Accountability Process




      8.5.5. Creation and implementation of PSC generates significant savings by eliminating 90%
      of the unit-level activities associated with data reconciliation between multiple legacy
      systems. Efficiencies gained in man-hour processing time will be captured during the
      capabilities based manpower standard transformation. For outsourced operations, reduced
      requirements determination will be addressed via contract updates or when contracts come up
      on their normal renegotiation schedule.
      8.5.6. The manpower requirement for PSC in Table 8.1 are based on one authorization per
      2,000 vehicles and resulted from benchmarking HQ ACC’s South West Asia C-REMS
      function currently in place, with minor adjustments due to a variety of MAJCOM fleet
      postures. The following specific MAJCOM contributions will be required to stand up the C-
      REMS in FY 08 under operational responsibility of the Air Force Element, Vehicle and
      Equipment Management Support Office (AFELM VEMSO), Langley AFB, VA. The
      expectation is manpower positions will be sourced from base level; however MAJCOMs
      have the latitude to use Headquarters or other command positions to fill the requirement.
      Note: Transfer of manpower resource adjustments for this transformation effort will be
      based on negotiated and approved realignments between the gaining and losing MAJCOMs
      and AFELM VEMSO. FY 08 PB manpower profile provided by MAJCOM/A1M should
      correctly reflect what manpower authorizations remain in the MAJCOMs as a result of PBD
      720 reductions. This instruction represents the MAJCOM/A4R Functional agreement and
      coordination for MAJCOM/A1M to initiate the above manpower programming and
      realignment actions.

  8.5.8. Operations that are currently A-76/contract will maintain current functions until
  contracts come up for renegotiation, at which time, contracts will be modified to transfer PSC
  functions to AFELM VEMSO or remain a reach back capability if legal constraints prevent
  transfer. The MAJCOM functional community will coordinate PSC generated contract
  modifications with the VEMSO as they occur.
  8.5.9. The VEMSO will form a PSC Working Group with the MAJCOMs to work out any
  additional issues required for PSC. The VEMSO will convene the working group at least
  quarterly via video teleconference to provide updates on progress toward implementation and
  address MAJCOM concerns.
  8.5.10. Local fleet managers and MAJCOMs retain sustainment responsibilities for day-to-
  day management of the AF’s fleet. The PSC function will coordinate/collaborate with the
  base-level fleet manager and owning MAJCOMs to ensure resulting updates crossing
  multiple legacy systems and reconciliations are executed in a synchronized manner.
  8.5.11. AF Enterprise-Wide Implementation Key Functions, Roles and Responsibilities:
     8.5.11.1. The VEMSO is responsible for:
         8.5.11.1.1. Providing operational guidance and oversight for PSC function as the
         organizational process owner.
         8.5.11.1.2. Providing assistance in staffing contract modifications and vetting legal
         requirements as they apply to the PSC function at the corporate level. Information
         obtained during staffing actions will be distributed during all MAJCOM PSC working
         group meetings.
         8.5.11.1.3. Coordinating and publishing guidance in AFI 23-302 to clarify roles and
         responsibilities between contract operations and PSC until contract updates are
         processed.
     8.5.11.2. Process of REMS/OLVIMS Reconciliation (scheduled):
         8.5.11.2.1. Base-level Vehicle Management and Analysis (VM&A) will:
             8.5.11.2.1.1. VFM, VMS or representatives from VM&A will be appointed by
             the LRS Commander or equivalent, as the equipment custodian for their vehicle
             accounts. They will be responsible to sign the CA/CRL annually to validate the
             inventory actually took place and to verify that action has been taken to resolve
             any noted discrepancies. The LRS Commander or equivalent will review and
             endorse the CA/CRL after VM&A has accomplished the inventory.
214                                      AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


             8.5.11.2.1.2. Produce On-Line Vehicle Interactive Management System
             (OLVIMS) to AFIS mismatch files and reconcile errors before transmitting a
             clean file to PSC. (Local exchange)
             8.5.11.2.1.3. Produce the base-level transaction file and forward to PSC. (Hand
             off)
         8.5.11.2.2. The VEMSO (PSC) will:
             8.5.11.2.2.1. Research information received from base-level fleet managers and
             correct discrepancies in AFIS and SBSS, as required.
      8.5.11.3. Process of AFIS/Supply (M06) Asset Reconciliation (daily):
         8.5.11.3.1. The VEMSO (PSC) will:
             8.5.11.3.1.1. Process the SBSS M06 file in the base-level AFIS module and take
             appropriate action to research and correct discrepancies in AFIS and SBSS, as
             required, during the daily reconciliation.
             8.5.11.3.1.2. Clear computer rejects. Correct rejected REMS and AFEMS
             transactions in a timely manner. Close coordination with the ELO D-16 monitor
             and Document Control Section is necessary.
      8.5.11.4. Process of MAFIS to AFIS Reconciliation (scheduled):
         8.5.11.4.1. MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff will:
             8.5.11.4.1.1. Provide current copies of the MAFIS ESCM06.DBF and
             TVAL.DBF databases when requested by PSC (Hand off).
         8.5.11.4.2. The VEMSO (PSC) will:
             8.5.11.4.2.1. Process the MAJCOM to AFIS transmit file.
             8.5.11.4.2.2. Identify discrepancies listed between the MAJCOM and base VAL,
             take appropriate action to research, and fix authorization data in AFIS and SBSS
             until the reconciliation report matches.
             8.5.11.4.2.3. Provide updated MAFIS database file to MAJCOM (Hand off).
      8.5.11.5. Process of AFIS to MAFIS Transmit File (bi-weekly):
         8.5.11.5.1. The VEMSO (PSC) will:
             8.5.11.5.1.1. Download the M06 daily from applicable supply source and
             perform the AFIS to Supply (M06), AFIS to MAFIS, and MAFIS to AFIS
             reconciliation in the applicable base-level AFIS module.
             8.5.11.5.1.2. Take appropriate action to research and correct discrepancies in
             AFIS and SBSS to ensure near real-time (within 24 hr) 100% authorization
             integrity and asset accountability.
             8.5.11.5.1.3. Provide updated transmittal file to MAJCOM (Hand off).
      8.5.11.6. Process of AFIS Vehicle Master Report and CA/CRL (monthly):
         8.5.11.6.1. The VEMSO (PSC) will:
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                       215


             8.5.11.6.1.1. Download the most current CA/CRL from SBSS and perform a line-
             by-line reconciliation with the base-level AFIS Vehicle Master Report.
             8.5.11.6.1.2. Take appropriate action to research and fix vehicle discrepancies in
             AFIS and SBSS, as required, to ensure 100% authorization integrity and asset
             accountability.
     8.5.11.7. Process of AFEMS Reconciliation (weekly):
         8.5.11.7.1. The VEMSO (PSC) will:
             8.5.11.7.1.1. Access AFEMS and review all vehicle SBSS rejects and variances
             related to authorizations and assets.
             8.5.11.7.1.2. Take appropriate action to research and fix all vehicle discrepancies
             in AFIS and SBSS, to include clearing the rejects or variances from AFEMS.
             8.5.11.7.1.3. Collaborate resolution with MAJCOM on AFEMS rejects or
             variances caused by required Allowance Standard changes/updates (Hand-off).
8.6. AFEMS and MAJCOM VAL Data Interface. MAJCOM VAL data is used to populate
the following authorization tables in AFEMS:
  8.6.1. DB86 - Vehicle Authorizations.
  8.6.2. War Plans Additive Requirements Incoming MAJCOM VAL data must pass edits
  within AFEMS in order to populate the above database tables. PSC emphasis will be placed
  on correcting rejected MAJCOM VAL records since they inhibit base-level reporting.
  8.6.3. There are two types of edits; Rejects and Variances. A rejected MAJCOM data record
  is not processed and results in SBSS data rejecting in AFEMS because the authorization
  record is not loaded. A variance MAJCOM VAL record is processed in AFEMS but requires
  modification.
  8.6.4. PSC will research rejects and variances one duty day after VAL data has been
  transmitted to AFEMS.
  8.6.5. PSC will process rejects and variances by utilizing the edit logic/corrective action
  information. Once MAJCOM VAL record corrections and/or corrective action have been
  implemented by another agency (i.e., LGR ROF Monitor) retransmit the VAL data to
  AFEMS. Note: It is vital to retransmit the VAL data file after discrepancies are corrected.
  The AFEMS "Daily Corrupt Report" can also be used to locate rejects/variances.
  8.6.6. Vacant vehicle authorizations.
     8.6.6.1. 3400 funded authorizations. If an authorization is vacant for more than 18
     months and no asset is programmed for purchase to fill the authorization it is
     automatically considered invalid and deleted, unless an Exception to Policy has been
     granted by HAF/A4LE.
     8.6.6.2. 3080 funded authorizations. If an authorization is vacant for more than 2
     programming cycles and no asset is programmed for purchase to fill the authorization it is
     automatically considered invalid and deleted, unless an Exception to Policy has been
     granted by HAF/A4LE.
216                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


8.7. Leased Vehicle Authorization Management. The following actions will be taken to
establish accountability for leased vehicles.
   8.7.1. After the vehicle is received, verify and use the prime NSN applicable from the
   VMIF, and process a REC to receive the vehicle with the registration number assigned by the
   VEMSO. After processing the REC, process an issue.
   8.7.2. Issues must always be for a quantity of one (1) since a REMS detail is created for each
   registration number issued.
   8.7.3. Issue inputs must contain a transaction exception code of ―6‖, indicating a ―post-post‖
   transaction.
   8.7.4. Ensure the detail record contains equipment code ―V‖; otherwise, the REMS detail
   will not be established during issue processing.
   8.7.5. A vehicle will be loaded into REMS as a suitable (S) substitute only if the asset NSN
   cross-references to the prime NSN. When an asset NSN does not cross to a prime NSN, but
   has similar capabilities, load it as an unsuitable (U) substitute.
   8.7.6. Vehicles will be loaded with the AF registration number issued by the VEMSO. The
   third character will be an ―N‖. For the GSA leases, vehicle will be marked in the same
   manner as OSI vehicles or in a manner to ensure no cost is incurred when GSA turn in action
   is accomplished. Do not change the GSA license plate to the AF assigned registration
   number.
   8.7.7. To ensure audit trail and accountability of lease vehicle turn-ins accomplish the
   applicable following transaction.
      8.7.7.1. For lease turn-in of a ―like asset‖ such as a B102 for a B102 turn the vehicle into
      Base Supply using Status Code ―Q‖ and reissue the replacement with the new registration
      number.
      8.7.7.2. For lease turn in of a ―unlike asset‖ such as a B102 for a B222 turn the vehicle
      into Base Supply using Status Code ―Q‖ and do an FCH Identity Change from the old
      master NSN to the proper NSN to the new master NSN.
      8.7.7.3. For lease turn-in of an asset that does not have an immediate replacement or
      when one won’t be received do a paper work only turn in to DRMO, Status Code ―M.‖
   8.7.8. All assets obtained under a 580 CBSS (WR-ALC) approved Lease With the Option to
   Buy (LWOB) package will be loaded under an equipment code of ―P‖ authorization and
   assigned an ―N‖ registration number by the VEMSO. At the end of the LWOB period, and
   following the assignment of a permanent AF registration number by 580 CBSS, the
   authorization will change to equipment code ―V‖.
8.8. Air Force Owned Vehicle Authorizations. The following actions will be taken to
establish accountability for blue fleet vehicles.
   8.8.1. After the vehicle is received, verify the asset NSN, and process a REC to receive the
   vehicle. After processing the REC, process an issue.
   8.8.2. Issues must always be for a quantity of one (1) since a REMS detail is created for each
   registration number issued.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                        217


   8.8.3. Issue inputs must contain a transaction exception code of ―6‖, indicating a ―post-post‖
   transaction.
   8.8.4. Ensure the detail record contains equipment code ―V‖; otherwise, the REMS detail
   will not be established during issue processing.
   8.8.5. A vehicle will be loaded into REMS as a suitable (S) substitute only if the asset NSN
   cross-references to the prime NSN. When an asset NSN does not cross to a prime NSN, but
   has similar capabilities, load it as an unsuitable (U) substitute.
8.9. P-Series Registered Vehicles. The Office of Special Activities (HQ AFMC/A5J) is the AF
focal point for special project vehicles. Do not report P-series vehicles through REMS. HQ
AFMC/A5J assigns P-series registration numbers and accounts for the acquisition, procurement
and distribution of the vehicle fleet until disposition.
8.10. Vehicle Shipments. MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs normally direct vehicle
shipments. Local Traffic Management Flight will assist with guidance on funding the
transportation costs associated with an RDO as provided in AFI 24-201, Cargo Movement,
Chapter 3. When a vehicle is shipped, the computer-generated Vehicle Historical Record,
Vehicle Master Transfer Report, floppy disk and pertinent technical data will be sent to the
gaining installation. Process AF Form 2005, Issue/Turn-In Request, to remove the vehicle from
the SBSS (DD Form 1348-1A). In either case, the C-REMS Manager must sign in block one.
Send vehicle record jacket and either the ―A5J‖ or ―SHP‖ document to TMF. The gaining VM
initiates follow-up action on vehicles not received within the specified time frame.
8.11. Vehicle Shipments to Depot Repair. Certain types of vehicles are eligible for depot-
level repairs. Local Traffic Management Flight will assist with guidance on funding the
transportation costs associated with an RDO as provided in AFI 24-201. Criteria for these
vehicles are contained in TO 36-1-191, Chapter 9. MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs will
provide shipping instructions for vehicles scheduled for depot repair. Three vehicle status codes
apply to depot shipments. Status codes ―B‖ and ―G‖ (accountability not retained by the shipping
base) require processing of turn-in documents. Input of either of these two codes will
automatically create shipping documents. Status code ―R‖ (vehicle programmed for return to the
base) requires preparation only of an off-line ―DO NOT POST‖ shipping document. An FCI 2C
transaction is required to enter status code ―R‖ into the REMS records.
8.12. SBSS Accountable Record Inventory Discrepancy Management.
   8.12.1. False duplicate vehicle registration number in SBSS. Correct by processing an
   inventory adjustment document (IAD; 1GP/SRC). Use of IAD processing will cause M10
   reporting and full explanation on the cause of action and copy of transaction must be
   provided to the responsible LRS office. Also, annotate that a reverse post will not work for
   REMS details per AFMAN 23-110 Volume 2, Part 2, Chapter 7 ―I235 MGT Vehicle Issues
   Not Authorized Reverse-Post.‖
   8.12.2. To remove a false NSN serviceable balance (vehicle record). If you discover the
   serviceable balance before issuing any assets to detail process a reverse post, however if you
   have ran an issue on any of the records process an IAD to eliminate the remaining balance.
   Use of IAD processing will cause M10 reporting and full explanation on the cause of action
   and copy of transaction must be provided to the responsible LRS office. Also, annotate that a
218                                          AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


   reverse post will not work for REMS details per AFMAN 23-110 Volume 2, Part 2, Chapter
   7 ―I235 MGT Vehicle Issues Not Authorized Reverse-Post‖.
   8.12.3. NSN discrepancy between Authorized in use Detail (201) and REM-Vehicles only
   Detail (214). Process an IAD to correct this discrepancy. If the IAD processing does not
   resolve the discrepancy submit FIX action request. Use of IAD processing will cause M10
   reporting and full explanation on the cause of action and copy of transaction must be
   provided to the responsible LRS office. Also, annotate that a reverse post will not work for
   REMS details per AFMAN 23-110 Volume 2, Part 2, Chapter 7 ―I235 MGT Vehicle Issues
   Not Authorized Reverse-Post.‖
   8.12.4. When SBSS asset quantity (vehicle count) is greater than the number in AFIS.
   Research AFIS historical records to determine appropriate action required in SBSS. Attach
   historical documentation to accountable documents and file. For balance mismatches that
   historical activity records cannot be found initiate the proper resolution action (i.e., report of
   survey).
8.13. Vehicle Status Codes. These codes indicate the current utilization or physical status/loss
of a vehicle.
   8.13.1. A - Assigned for authorized use (except for Use Code ―M‖ WRM assets). ASC
   cannot be ―987‖.
   8.13.2. B - Vehicle is being shipped to a repair activity. Disposition instructions have been
   or will be, provided to the repair facility by the MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff. The
   vehicle will not return to the former owning organization and is a loss to the LRS.
   8.13.3. C - Vehicle is used for maintenance training (AETC only).
   8.13.4. D - Have disposition instructions, but vehicle accountability is maintained on
   authorized/ in-use and REM-vehicles-only detail records pending shipment, maintenance,
   transfer to DRMS, sale, etc.
   8.13.5. E - Vehicle is unserviceable. Accountability is maintained on authorized/in-use and
   REM-vehicles-only detail records until transfer to DRMS. Cannibalization is authorized
   prior to transferring to DRMS.
   8.13.6. F - Vehicle assigned to a special project or exercise (not WRM or Mobility). Use
   code must be ―K.‖
   8.13.7. G - Vehicle is being shipped to a facility for repair and subsequent IM directed
   redistribution. The vehicle is a loss to the base and excess to the MAJCOM.
   8.13.8. H - Vehicle is in place for an authorized WRM requirement and is in serviceable
   condition. ASC must be a Base Augmentation Support Set (BASS) composition code and
   UC must be ―M‖.
   8.13.9. I - Vehicle is awaiting LTI.
   8.13.10. J - Vehicle is not authorized but is in use and required. Justification request
   submitted to MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staff for approval (ASC 048 must be
   assigned).
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          219


  8.13.11. K - Vehicle is excess to the owning MAJCOM and is being held at the direction of
  the IM for distribution instructions. ASC 048 must be assigned and Use Code must be ―K.‖
  8.13.12. L - Vehicle is on loan in excess of 30 days to a non-AF organization. ASC 051
  must be assigned and UC must be ―K.‖
  8.13.13. M - Vehicle is being transferred to DRMS. C-REMS must ensure that the vehicle
  historical record cites the specific disposal activity and location.
  8.13.14. N - Vehicle is unserviceable and disposition instructions have been requested from
  the owning MAJCOM.
  8.13.15. P - Turn In (TIN) code is used for all other physical losses where the vehicle will
  not return to AF REMS. Examples include losses to DOD or governmental agencies, foreign
  governments, commercial agencies (excluding AF vehicles on loan to contractors), theft, etc.
  C-REMS must submit a delete (loss) record (an off-line shipment must be processed to
  remove the vehicle from LRS Stock Control supply records following a status code ―P‖
  TIN.). Be sure that the vehicle historical record lists applicable recipients or other clarifying
  specifics.
  8.13.16. Q - Used for turn-in inputs to correct erroneously assigned registration numbers,
  NSNs, etc. For example, the vehicle was gained in error, the registration or NSN was entered
  incorrectly, or there was a change in status from REMS to non-REMS. This code will not be
  used for normal file maintenance NSN changes distributed through Stock Number User
  Directory (SNUD).
  8.13.17. R - At the option of the MAJCOM, the status code may be changed to ―R‖ for
  vehicles in base- or depot-level repair for over 60 days - accountability remains in the local
  SBSS.
  8.13.18. S - Vehicle transferred to an organization of another MAJCOM. The losing and
  gaining organizations are both supported by the same LRS.
  8.13.19. T - Vehicle is in transit to an AF activity of another MAJCOM, and is a loss to the
  LRS and MAJCOM. The TIN input reflecting code T will not be processed until
  immediately before turnover of the vehicle to LRS.
  8.13.20. U- Vehicle is in transit to an AF activity of the same MAJCOM. Vehicle is a loss
  to the LRS.
  8.13.21. V - Vehicle is on loan within or between commands not to exceed 180 days. ASC
  must be ―987‖ and UC must be ―J‖ or ―K.‖
  8.13.22. W - Vehicle is being held by AFMC for system support requirements (AFMC use
  only).
  8.13.23. Y - In-place WRM asset is in unserviceable (repairable) condition and expected to
  be NMC for 30 days or more. Use code ―M‖ applies and ASC must be a BASS composition
  code.
  8.13.24. Z - Vehicle is in transit to Port of Embarkation (POE), either to or from overseas
  destination. It is anticipated that shipment time will exceed 180 days.
220                                          AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009

                                           Chapter 9

                      QUALITY ASSURANCE PERSONNEL (QAP)

9.1. Overview. This section applies to all Vehicle Management personnel who develop
requirements and provide oversight of contractor performance. QAP is a term developed to
encompass both Quality Assurance Evaluators (QAEs) and Quality Assurance Specialists
(QASs). QAPs access contractor performance to ensure the contractor is performing IAW
contract requirements, provisions and standards. The Functional Commander or Functional
Director must ensure assigned personnel are competent on the acquisition process; capable of
identifying and defining mission needs and requirements, and available full time, if the
individual is a full time QAP, for the life of the services acquisition.
9.2. Duties of the Primary and Alternate Vehicle Management QA.
   9.2.1. Assess and documents a contractor’s performance IAW the Quality Assurance Plan
   (QASP) or Performance Plan (PP).
   9.2.2. Notifies the Contracting Officer of any significant performance deficiencies; assess
   performance and provides documentation.
   9.2.3. Recommends improvements to the QASP, PP and PWS throughout the life of the
   contract.
   9.2.4. Participates as a member of the Multi-Functional Team.
   9.2.5. Assesses and manages contractor performance data in CPARS. The QA personnel
   provides the Contracting Officer with feedback on the contractor’s performance.
   9.2.6. Assesses/monitors contractor compliance with and currency of TOs and directives
   throughout the life of the contract IAW QASP or PP (as applicable) if that area is not the
   contractor’s responsibility under the governing contract or PWS.
   9.2.7. QA personnel are to be objective, fair and consistent in evaluating contractor
   performance against the performance standards and the contract requirements.
   9.2.8. Represents the Contracting Officer in all technical matters concerning the contract.
   9.2.9. Assists in developing and updating the PWS and assess performance plans.
   9.2.10. Provides a summary of QAP performance assessment activities to the Contracting
   Officer in accordance with the performance plan.
   9.2.11. Accepts and provides performance assessment of services; acceptance shall
   ordinarily be evidenced by execution of an acceptance certificate on a DD Form 250 or
   similar documents.
   9.2.12. Performs contract performance assessment; assesses and documents contractor
   performance.
   9.2.13. Submits contractor performance reports to the Contracting Officer in the frequency,
   format, and detail prescribed by the Contracting Officer.
222                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


   9.2.14. Reviews and ensures contractor compliance with the contractor’s quality control
   program. Periodically reviews contractor’s performance with the commander or equivalent,
   the Contracting Officer and the contractor.
   9.2.15. Reviews and/or purges all incoming correspondence (i.e. Service Bulletins, TCTOs
   and One-Time Inspections) before routing it to the contractor.
   9.2.16. Reviews the contractor’s reports for accuracy, adverse trends and mission
   accomplishment.
   9.2.17. Reviews contractor reports submitted to higher headquarters.
   9.2.18. Validates contractor TO requirements IAW PWS.
   9.2.19. Administration of a contract is a vital and necessary requirement; therefore, it is
   imperative that all QAPs involved in the requirement, from requirements identification
   through contract award and administration, are represented on the Multi-Functional Team.
   9.2.20. QAPs assigned to a multi-functional team are responsible for the following:
   acquisition planning; market research; government cost estimates; requirements and
   solicitation development; source selection; contract performance management and
   administration; provide contract changes; periodically meet with contractor; providing
   contractor performance status to leadership, as required; and gather and submittal of past
   performance information.
9.3. QA for Vehicle Management Flights.
   9.3.1. Provides support to senior leadership as required: Uses their technical expertise to
   assist the LRS Commander or equivalent to arrive at informed decisions when coordinating
   with higher headquarters, Defense Contract Management Agency and DLA.
   9.3.2. Evaluates unit maintenance management procedures, including locally developed
   forms, publications, OIs, etc., for accuracy, intent and necessity.
   9.3.3. Acts as focal point to ensure appropriate actions are taken to notify the MAJCOM
   when deficiencies are found in AF or MAJCOM instructions.
   9.3.4. Ensures all required government training is scheduled for both contractor personnel
   and QAPs.
   9.3.5. Reviews QA performance assessments and assist in resolving performance problems.
   9.3.6. Ensures all assigned 2T3XX QA inspectors complete all required inspection, safety,
   qualification, HAZMAT and environmental awareness training.
   9.3.7. Documents all training for military inspectors on AF Form 1098 and/or AF Form 797
   as applicable.
   9.3.8. Verifies training is correctly documented to ensure QAPs are qualified to perform
   evaluated tasks and inspections.
   9.3.9. Assists, as needed, the VM&A with reports and studies.
   9.3.10. Initiates actions when additional attention is required to resolve adverse maintenance
   trends or training problems. Actions include preparing cross-tell information bulletin and
   messages for MAJCOM release to other similarly equipped units, when necessary.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         223


  9.3.11. Performs review of Deficiency Reports, TCTOs, SBs, OTIs and Manufacturer
  Recalls.
  9.3.12. Reviews publications and technical data files for compliance with applicable AFIs.
  9.3.13. Reviews adequacy of housekeeping practices.
  9.3.14. Reviews reports to include timely and accurate submission, suspense control,
  procedures for review prior to submission and coordination with other affected agencies.
  9.3.15. Reviews documentation to include adequacy of files, directive compliance, accuracy
  and documentation disposition.
  9.3.16. Reviews management and scheduling of items requiring calibration or weight testing
  to include currency of calibration/weight test due dates, adherence to TMDE calibration
  schedule and control of items.
  9.3.17. Reviews documents maintained by work center contractor for support equipment (to
  include maintenance and inspection).
  9.3.18. Periodically reviews contractor-initiated waiver requests for approval/coordination
  through MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs.
  9.3.19. Reviews government furnished property inventories upon contract award and
  annually thereafter. Provides guidance on resolving issues related to government furnished
  property.
  9.3.20. Maintains technical competency in their assigned performance assessment areas.
  They must stay abreast of all industry trends, safety requirements, and environmental and
  HAZMAT laws.
  9.3.21. Performs periodic assessment on contractor maintained activities during hours of
  operation that include all shifts, weekends, nights, holidays, exercise and contingency
  operations.
  9.3.22. Surveys and assesses contractor compliance with federal, state and local
  environmental laws, and AFIs.
  9.3.23. QAPs may be required to periodically inventory government property and to provide
  information to the Contracting Officer on any loss, damage or destruction of government
  property.
  9.3.24. During contract renewals; ensures Vehicle Management portion of the PWS is
  coordinated through MAJCOM Vehicle Management Staffs.
  9.3.25. The QAP may not:
     9.3.25.1. Act in such a manner as to cause the contractor to believe they have authority
     to bind and/or obligate the Government.
     9.3.25.2. Clarify, make or infer legal interpretation on the scope or intent of the contract.
     Questions pertaining to interpretation of any contract provision shall be referred to the
     Base Contracting Officer for resolution.
     9.3.25.3. Approve contractor’s procedures.
     9.3.25.4. Authorize the expenditure of funds.
224                                          AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


       9.3.25.5. Levy or impose upon a contractor any task or permit any substitution not
       specifically provided for in the contract.
       9.3.25.6. Enter into or make changes to contract requirements.
       9.3.25.7. Give direction to the contractor or employees. Offer advice to the contractor
       which may adversely affect contract performance or compromise the rights of the AF.
9.4. Performance Plan (PP). Identifies the multi-functional team, their roles and
responsibilities, how the team will assess performance and manage the contract to obtain
efficiencies, improved performance, and cost savings throughout its life cycle.
   9.4.1. Use the PP to assess the services provided by the contractor. The PP provides for
   effective and efficient performance assessment to ensure acceptable service is received. The
   performance plan includes:
       9.4.1.1. Objective(s) in having the service provided, i.e., to provide quality vehicle
       maintenance for AF vehicles, while complying with all environmental, air pollution and
       mandated requirements.
       9.4.1.2. Incorporate the strategy, methods and tools the multi-functional teams have
       developed to assess the contractor’s performance against the performance thresholds,
       measurements, metrics and incentives identified in the contract. Performance thresholds
       are measured in terms of quality and timeliness. Include a table that incorporates the
       performance threshold, measurement and metrics.
       9.4.1.3. Develop a management approach, to include methods and tools the multi-
       functional team has developed to validate the objectives and goals identified as part of the
       Performance Plan, i.e. benchmarking, etc.
       9.4.1.4. Provide an incentive plan that validates the objective and goals of the multi-
       functional team.
   9.4.2. Performance metrics are used to track contractor progress towards meeting stated
   performance objectives. The multi-functional team ensures that the performance metrics are
   aligning with the performance-based work statement and overall mission support objectives.
9.5. Performance Assessment Methods. The suggested source of performance assessment is
the contractor’s Management Information System. The purpose of having an information system
is to validate the contractor is performing in accordance to the terms and conditions of the
contract. The data system is used to validate contractor response times, schedules, etc..
   9.5.1. Random Inspection/Sampling. Random visits to assess performance provide the QAP
   with a valuable management tool. Random samplings provide good overall performance
   indicators. Each job is evaluated against the PWS or performance standard to ensure the
   contractor is in compliance with the terms and conditions of the contract. .The critical
   element in a random sampling evaluation is the samplings taken are truly random and they
   depict the true average performance.
   9.5.2. Checklists. The checklist system is an easy method to identify the routine functions of
   the contractor’s activities. Prepare initial checklists from previously existing inspection
   guidelines and specific provisions in the contract. Review and modify the checklist as
   necessary to ensure accuracy and currency.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                         225


   9.5.3. Customer Complaints. The QAP can use customer complaints to identify potential
   problems. The QAP must train the customer on the terms and conditions of the contract to
   ensure the customer complaint is valid. The QAP must respond quickly to the customer
   complaint with an objective evaluation. Feedback and involvement with the dissatisfied
   customer are key if the complaint system is to have validity.
9.6. Vehicle Management QAP Administrative Duties:
   9.6.1. Responsible to the LRS/CC or equivalent to perform as a technical advisor for vehicle
   management when clarification is required.
   9.6.2. Validates the contractor is properly managing Deficiency Reporting, TO Distribution,
   TCTOs, SBs, OTIs and Manufacturer Recalls.
   9.6.3. The QAP will maintain an organized filing system. Records are subject to
   inspection/review by the IG and auditors, etc., and can be used in litigation to support either
   the government or contractor position in disputes.
      9.6.3.1. QAP File Content. QAPs will establish and maintain a contract performance
      assessment file for each active service contract. The file will contain the following, as
      applicable:
          9.6.3.1.1. A duplicate copy of the QAP appointment letter signed by the Contracting
          Officer and Training Certificate (e.g., Phase I and II Training).
          9.6.3.1.2. A copy of the contract with attachments and the contractor’s Quality
          Control Plan.
          9.6.3.1.3. A copy of all modifications to the contract. Modifications are executed on
          a SF 30, Amendment of Solicitation/Modification of Contract.
          9.6.3.1.4. A copy of the Performance Plan. To include the roles and responsibilities
          of the QAP.
          9.6.3.1.5. Copies of all documents relating to the acceptance and payment for
          services received.
          9.6.3.1.6. Correspondence to and from the Multi-Functional Team, Contracting
          Officer and contractor. This correspondence should include special instructions from
          the Contracting Officer and correspondence relating to contractor performance
          assessment.
              9.6.3.1.6.1. A copy of any memoranda for the record to document:
              9.6.3.1.6.2. Telephone conversations with the contractor and the Contracting
              Officer.
              9.6.3.1.6.3. Pre-performance and Post award conference meeting minutes.
              9.6.3.1.6.4. Any other conversations or meetings with the contractor, Multi-
              Functional Team or Contracting Officer.
              9.6.3.1.6.5. Records of the contractor’s internal inspection system, if obtained
              from the contractor.
              9.6.3.1.6.6. Schedules    and   documents     pertaining   to   and   documenting
226                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


              performance assessment.
              9.6.3.1.6.7. Samples, photographs, witness statements and other factual data to
              support documentation.
              9.6.3.1.6.8. Names of individuals who are functioning as technical and
              administrative assistants.
              9.6.3.1.6.9. Applicable test reports, data required by the contract, AF Form 9s
              and funding obligations for the contract.
   9.6.4. Disposition of QAP Files. Upon contract close-out, the QAP forwards all records to
   the Contracting Officer.
   9.6.5. Suspense Files. A suspense system will be established to advise the Multi-Functional
   Team, QAPC or Contracting Officer of the contractor’s failure to complete acceptable
   performance or delivery IAW the contract terms and conditions.
9.7. Contract Administration. The QAP has certain responsibilities to be familiar with. The
following are the primary functions and personnel the QAP will routinely deal with:
   9.7.1. FAC. The FAC is a Functional Commander or Functional Director of any functional
   area with government program management responsibility to oversee the functional mission.
   For example, for Vehicle Management the LRS Commander or equivalent is the FAC. They
   are generally responsible for:
      9.7.1.1. Developing and sustaining a sound Quality Assurance Evaluation Program.
      9.7.1.2. Implementing the PP and establishing a comprehensive training program.
      9.7.1.3. Overseeing development of the PWS, PP, market research, government cost
      estimates, funding and evaluation assessment guides.
          9.7.1.3.1. The requirements in the PP and assessment guides are "outcome-based" in
          that they only reflect the desired end results--not the process. Each outcome-based
          requirement includes clear, unambiguous and measurable performance thresholds so
          there is no question whether our mission requirement was met. Performance
          assessment methods are consistent with the standards-focusing on end results, not the
          processes.
   9.7.2. The Contracting Officer is empowered to award and/or administer contracts. The
   Contracting Officer acts as an agent between the AF and the contractor. The Base
   Contracting Officer is the only person authorized to enter into contracts and is responsible for
   reviewing the contractor’s performance to ensure that it is satisfactory and the AF receives
   the products and/or services requested.
   9.7.3. QAPs may be involved in the modification process in the following areas: Identifying
   the required change(s), preparing documentation on the proposed change(s), preparing
   government cost estimate(s), advising the Contracting Officer on technical aspects of the
   change(s), participating in reviews of contractor technical proposals, supporting the
   Contracting Officer in the negotiations of change.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          227


                                           Chapter 10

                                    VEHICLE CONTROL

Section 10A— Introduction

10.1. Vehicle Control Officer Program. DOD policy requires that government motor vehicle
resources are organized and managed to ensure optimum responsiveness, efficiency and
economy in support of the DOD mission. To ensure day-to-day management of those motor
vehicles permanently assigned to units and agencies, the Air Force has adopted the vehicle
control program. As established in this AFI, each applicable organization will appoint a Vehicle
Control Officer (VCO) and alternate, in writing, and forward that appointment to the base
Vehicle Fleet Manager (VFM) or Vehicle Management superintendent (VMS). The VFM/VMS
will ensure VCO training is accomplished.
10.2. Vehicle Management Policy. Public law directs the DOD and Air Force to maintain the
minimum number of fuel-efficient motor vehicles to accomplish the mission and limits their use
to official purposes. All management echelons must put emphasis on controlling and conserving
vehicle assets. The vehicle user is responsible for operation, conservation and condition of
vehicles used. This responsibility is enforced through the operator’s supervisor, commander, and
commander appointed vehicle control officers.
10.3. Host Logistics Readiness Services. The host logistics readiness activity provides
maintenance support, fleet management, and transportation services not within the using
agencies capability.
   10.3.1. See AFI 24-301, Vehicle Operations, for specific guidance on Government Motor
   Vehicle (GMV) usage, services and assistance. Vehicle Operations flights normally provide
   the following services:
       10.3.1.1. Taxi Service. This service provides a quick response, point-to-point service to
       all requestors requiring official transportation.
       10.3.1.2. U-Drive-It (UDI) Service. A limited number of passenger and cargo vehicles
       are available to support organizations that do not have assigned vehicles and to augment
       units with assigned vehicles in meeting infrequent peak requirements for short term
       (normally limited to 72hrs) use.
       10.3.1.3. Bus Service. Depending upon the installation, various modes of mass
       transportation services may be available.
       10.3.1.4. Operator Records and Licensing. All matters related to operator licensing and
       certain vehicle certification. Will validate unit plans of instruction for vehicle licensing
       and manage the Commercial Driver’s License (CDL) program.
       10.3.1.5. Vehicle Recovery Service. Local procedures will be developed by the host
       logistics readiness squadron for vehicle recovery services and procedures.
   10.3.2. Vehicle Management flights normally provide the following services:
       10.3.2.1. Vehicle Management and Analysis (VM&A). Provides assistance to VCOs
       with such services as, vehicle justifications, leasing procedures, vehicle analysis, DOD
228                                         AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


      Fleet Credit Cards, briefing VCOs, conducting vehicle assessment inspections and staff
      assistance visits. See paragraph 4.3 for more information.
      10.3.2.2. Scheduled maintenance, to include Preventive Maintenance and Inspections
      (PM&I) and Special Inspections. These inspections are maintenance actions normally
      scheduled in advance, based on a vehicle’s actual or projected mileage, hours of
      operation, or by calendar time. VM&A will coordinate scheduled maintenance with unit
      VCOs.
      10.3.2.3. Unscheduled Maintenance. VCOs should ensure that any motor vehicle
      malfunction is reported to the vehicle management customer service section (or
      equivalent element) in a timely manner.
      10.3.2.4. Minor Maintenance Road Side Assistance. During normal duty hours, roadside
      service for most disabled vehicles can be provided. This service may also be available
      after normal duty hours for urgent or emergency situations. Follow the installation
      prescribed procedures for requesting this assistance.
10.4. Vehicle Control Duties. Locally developed VCO orientation briefings should cover all
aspects of a VCO's duties. As a minimum unit VCOs are responsible for:
   10.4.1. Acting as a liaison between their unit and the host logistics readiness squadron for all
   unit government motor vehicle matters.
   10.4.2. Controlling unit vehicles and obtaining transportation services required to support
   unit mission requirements.
      10.4.2.1. VCOs are required to receipt for permanently assigned unit vehicles from the
      base VFM/VMS or the Vehicle Management and Analysis Element using the On-Line
      Vehicle Interactive Management System (OLVIMS) VCO Master Listing Hand Receipt.
      VCOs then assign the vehicles to their respective authorized functions.
   10.4.3. Defending vehicle requirements, justifying requests for additional vehicle
   authorizations; complying with the base vehicle rotation and priority recall plans; and
   notifying the VFM when assigned vehicles are no longer required.
      10.4.3.1. Unit vehicle requirements are justified using the host MAJCOM approved
      format. The requirement(s) is verified by the VFM and approved by the base Mission
      Support Group Commander. If locally approved, the VFM sends the requirement to the
      MAJCOM vehicle management staff for final action. The authorization, when approved
      by the MAJCOM, will be supported with the appropriate vehicle type when it becomes
      available. Note: Vehicles are not assigned pending approval of the authorization. See
      paragraph 4.25 for additional information.
          10.4.3.1.1. Purchase requests for Other Government Motor Vehicle Conveyances
          (OGMVC) must be reviewed by the VFM or VMS and forwarded to the host
          MAJCOM to ensure the desired asset is an equipment item and not a vehicle.
          Additional guidance on the procurement of OGMVCs can be found on paragraph
          4.20 Note: Purchase requests for other non-registered equipment (i.e. ATVs,
          mowers, etc.) will need to be coordinated with the VFM or VMS to ensure parts,
          facilities, manpower, funds, etc. are available to support the equipment before it is
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                       229


         acquired. Organizations must first consider purchasing a maintenance agreement to
         support the equipment.
         10.4.3.1.2. LSVs will not be purchased by using organizations. Refer to paragraphs
         1.26 and 4.20 for further clarification.
     10.4.3.2. New vehicle authorization requests and requirements must comply with the Air
     Force Vehicle Fleet Growth Policy IAW paragraph 1.22
     10.4.3.3. VCOs provide vehicle management with mission impact statements to
     substantiate annual base vehicle buy submissions.
     10.4.3.4. Continued retention of vehicle authorizations is predicated on the continuing
     need and asset utilization.
  10.4.4. Providing justification data to support unit minimum essential vehicle levels (MEL).
  MELs indicate the number of vehicles, by type, that can be in the vehicle maintenance shop
  at one time and not seriously affect the user’s mission.
  10.4.5. All requests for installation of organizational equipment will be submitted, in
  writing, to the Vehicle Management and Analysis Element. Requests must address the extent
  of the proposed work, impact if denied, and availability of funds for contracting the
  equipment installation. The vehicle will be placed into original configuration at unit cost if
  vehicle is rotated/shipped. All requests will be reviewed by the VFM or VMS for final
  approval.
  10.4.6. Ensuring supplies, tools, and equipment for unit vehicles, such as highway warning
  kits, first aid kits (when required by local authorities), tire chains, polish, wax, chamois,
  sponges, jacks, lug wrenches, fire extinguishers, and spare tires (unless items are original
  equipment on vehicles). These items are procured by the VCO with unit O&M funds
  through GPC or standard supply chain management.
  10.4.7. Ensuring only qualified and properly licensed military, DOD employees, or
  authorized DOD contractors who meet the criteria established in AFI 24-301 operate
  assigned motor vehicles.
     10.4.7.1. Ensuring that each authorized unit vehicle operator has an active driver history
     record, AF Form 2296, Vehicle Operator Information (Part 3), established in the host
     Logistics Readiness Squadron’s On-Line Vehicle Integrated Management System
     (OLVIMS) prior to operating assigned vehicles.
     10.4.7.2. Using qualified unit instructors approved by the host base Distribution Section
     Chief/Superintendent (DSC/DSS) to train and supervise special purpose vehicle
     operators. Note: In those units that are not required to reorganize to have a Distribution
     Section, the Vehicle Operations Manager/Superintendent (VOM/VOS) will sign for the
     DSC/DSS.
     10.4.7.3. Developing and maintaining unit vehicle lesson plans that have been reviewed
     by the DSC/DSS and VFM/VMS and approved by the unit commander/director. NOTE:
     In those units that are not required to reorganize to have a Distribution Section, the
     VOM/VOS will sign for the DSC/DSS.
230                                        AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


   10.4.8. Ensuring that operator maintenance is performed and vehicle malfunctions are
   reported to vehicle management IAW paragraph 3.13.2.2
      10.4.8.1. Maintain Operator Inspection Guide and Trouble Report IAW AFMAN 37-123
      and dispose of in accordance with the Air Force Records Disposition Schedule (RDS)
      located at https://webrims.amc.af.mil.
   10.4.9. Take appropriate measures to prevent misuse, abuse and damage to Air Force motor
   vehicles. Motor vehicle accident, abuse prevention programs at all levels should include:
      10.4.9.1. Conducting and documenting monthly vehicle safety orientation and education
      briefings.
      10.4.9.2. Conducting and documenting monthly inspections to ensure assigned vehicles
      are serviceable and clean. The appropriate operator’s inspection guide and trouble report
      must be used when performing these inspections.
      10.4.9.3. Providing flight line training to assigned personnel when required.
      10.4.9.4. Ensuring unit vehicles are washed in accordance with intervals prescribed in
      TO 36-1-191, Table 6-3, and waxed when required in accordance with paragraph
      3.13.1.3 and local directives.
      10.4.9.5. Providing vehicle operators with instructions to follow, including agencies to
      phone, when accidents occur.
          10.4.9.5.1. The using organization commander designates an official to investigate
          each accident and provides results to safety.
          10.4.9.5.2. The Chief of Safety investigates and analyzes to determine the causes or
          possible corrective actions; accident trends involving government owned or rented
          motor vehicles are analyzed or investigated by the Chief of Safety.
          10.4.9.5.3. An operator surrenders the AF Form 2293 with the SF 91 to the VCO
          after the accident. Unit commanders may reinstate the license at their discretion.
          10.4.9.5.4. Accident reporting for commercial rental and General Services
          Administration (GSA) vehicles is the same as reporting an accident involving a
          government owned vehicle.
          10.4.9.5.5. When payment for damage (either voluntary or on a DD Form 200,
          Financial Liability Investigation of Property Loss) is involved, the unit VCO requests
          an AF Form 20 from Vehicle Management and Analysis (VM&A) for the actual
          repair cost.
   10.4.10. Ensure low-utilization or low mileage vehicles are rotated with high-usage or high
   mileage vehicles within the organization.
      10.4.10.1. Base and associate units must comply with vehicle rotation and utilization
      programs.
   10.4.11. The unit VCO will provide supplies for operator care such as oil, window cleaner,
   wax and other cleaning items as required.
AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009                                                          231


   10.4.12. Ensure all unit vehicle leasing actions are coordinated through Vehicle
   Management. Associate units are required to have vehicle lease requests coordinated
   through the host logistics readiness squadron’s vehicle management flight. Vehicle leasing
   may possibly effect vehicle buy submissions, vehicle rotations, MEL, etc.
10.5. Permissible Operating Distance (POD). Since it is usually more economical to use
services of commercial carriers for the transportation of personnel and cargo to destinations
outside the immediate areas of the installation, each base has an established permissible
operating distance for assigned motor vehicles. POD applies to all government-owned and leased
vehicles. Be aware of approved POD and seek approval from Vehicle Operations before
traveling outside the POD.

Section 10B— Motor Vehicle Official Use Policy

10.6. Official Use of Government Vehicles. AFI 24-301, contains specific policy guidance on
official use of government vehicles. General official use rules listed in AFI 24-301, Attachment
8 are non-inclusive and are provided to aid unit vehicle control personnel in interpreting official
use policy. The DSC/DSS (VOM/VOS in those units that are not required to reorganize to have
a Distribution Section) can give guidance in specific cases where the official nature of vehicle
usage is in question. Questions concerning the official use of government vehicles shall be
resolved in favor of strict compliance with statutory provisions.

Section 10C— Vehicle Operators

10.7. Vehicle operators:
   10.7.1. Will understand the guidelines in AFJMAN 24-306, Manual for the Wheeled Vehicle
   Driver, related AFIs, technical orders, technical and commercial manuals and plans of
   instruction for the vehicles operated.
   10.7.2. Use government rented, leased or owned motor vehicles for official purposes only.
   10.7.3. Will not use tobacco products in Air Force vehicles.
   10.7.4. Will not consume alcoholic beverages in any government vehicle.
   10.7.5. Notify the VCO of any personal status changes (e.g. physical profile change, use of
   prescription medications, and significant infraction of civil traffic laws).
   10.7.6. Perform required operator care and inspection on all government-owned and leased
   vehicles using appropriate vehicle inspection guides and signs the form.
   10.7.7. Report vehicle malfunctions to the Vehicle Management Customer Service Center
   (or equivalent) element within one normal workday. Operators do not delay discrepancy
   reporting on systems or devices adversely affecting the safety of personnel or the operation
   of vehicles/equipment. When any of the discrepancies listed in paragraph 3.13.2.2 are
   identified, the operator will discontinue use of the vehicle and report the discrepancy to
   Vehicle Management as soon as possible. Note: If the discrepancy occurs outside Vehicle
232                                       AFI23-302_PACAFSUP_I 23 NOVEMBER 2009


   Management duty hours, discontinue vehicle use and notify Vehicle Management of the
   discrepancy the next duty day. Failure to report malfunctions may constitute vehicle abuse.
